The Universal Questioning in the Grave and Its Process
Al-Sawi affirms universal questioning and describes the grave trial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that every person is questioned in the grave, the manner of the questioning, and the fate of believers versus disbelievers.

Core Idea
Everyone is questioned in the grave, and the response determines the outcome.

This passage from Al-Sawi clarifies a key point of Islamic eschatology: the universal nature of the grave questioning. He corrects a minority view that only believers are questioned, and then describes the dramatic process that unfolds in the grave for both believers and disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing on analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the full narrative.
Notice the clear structure: affirmation of universality, then description of events.
2
Identify the correction of a misconception
Find where Al-Sawi states the correct view and names the scholars he disagrees with. Understand why this matters.
The doctrine of grave questioning is a samʿiyyāt matter.
3
Trace the process of the questioning
Follow the sequence: soul return, questions asked, responses of believer vs disbeliever, the striking, the scream, and the treatment by the angels.
Notice the angels' different treatment and the mention of language.
4
Reflect on the evidence provided
Al-Sawi cites mutawātir ḥadīths and a line of poetry from al-Suyūṭī. Consider how these support the majority view.
The poetry emphasizes that the whole body is revived.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (مؤمناً كان أو كافراً ... إلخ): هذا هو الصحيح، خلافاً لقول ابن عبد البرّ والسُّيوطي، لا يسئل الكافر. قوله : (الَّذي يستقرُّ فيه) : أي : وأمَّا من عَلِمَ الله أنَّه ينقل من قبر. ويُعيد الله فيه الرُّوحَ بتمامه، وقيل: في نصفه، ويسألانه: «من ربُّك وما دينك؟ وما تقول في الرّجل الذي بعث فيكم؟ فيقول المؤمن : ربِّيَ الله، وديني الإسلام والرَّجلُ المبعوث فينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فيقولان له: انظر مقعدك من النار قد أبدلك الله به مقعدا في الجنة فيراهما جميعاً. وأما المنافق أو الكافر فيقول : لا أدري فيقولان له: «لا دريت ولا تليت»، ويضرب بمطراق من حديد في يد أحدهما، فيصيح صيحة يسمعها من يليه غير الثقلين ويَتَرفّقان بالمؤمن، ويَنْهران الكافر والمنافق. ويسألان كل أحد بلسانه لآخر؛ فلا يسئل إلَّا في القبر الذي يبعث منه . قوله : (ويعيد الله الرُّوح فيه تمامه هذا هو قول الجمهور لظاهر الأحاديث المتواترة، ولذا قال السيوطي : [ من الرجز] وكلُّـه يـحـيـا لـدى الـجـمـهـور لا جزؤه لـظـاهـر الـمـأثـور قوله : (ويترفَّقان بالمؤمن) : أي : ولو عاصياً بحسب تفاوت مراتب المؤمنين .
His saying: (whether believer or disbeliever... etc.): this is the correct view, contrary to the statement of Ibn ʿAbd al-Barr and al-Suyūṭī that the disbeliever is not questioned. His saying: (which he permanently settles in): i.e., as for the one whom Allah knows will be transferred from his grave. And Allah returns the soul to him entirely, and it was said: in half of it. And they ask him: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What do you say about the man who was sent among you?' So the believer says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and the man sent among us is the Messenger of Allah ﷺ.' So they say to him: 'Look at your seat in the Fire; Allah has replaced it for you with a seat in Paradise,' so he sees both of them. As for the hypocrite or disbeliever, he says: 'I do not know.' So they say to him: 'You neither knew nor recited.' And they strike him with an iron mallet in the hand of one of them, so he screams a scream heard by those near him except the two weighty ones. And they are gentle with the believer, and they are harsh with the disbeliever and hypocrite. And they ask everyone in his own language. He is only questioned in the grave from which he will be resurrected. His saying: (And Allah returns the soul to him entirely) – this is the saying of the majority due to the apparent meaning of the mutawātir ḥadīths, and thus al-Suyūṭī said: [from rajaz] 'All of it is revived according to the majority, not part of it, due to the apparent transmitted evidence.' His saying: (And they are gentle with the believer) – i.e., even if he is a sinner, according to the varying degrees of believers.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage addresses the scope of the questioning in the grave and describes the actual process. First, it affirms the correct view that every person, believer or disbeliever, is questioned, contrary to the opinions of Ibn Abd al-Barr and al-Suyuti who claimed the disbeliever is not questioned. Then it explains that questioning occurs in the grave in which the person will permanently reside, unless Allah knows he will be transferred. Then it describes the return of the soul to the body entirely (according to the majority) and the questions asked: about Lord, religion, and the Prophet. The believer answers correctly and is shown his replacement seat in Paradise. The disbeliever or hypocrite says 'I do not know' and is struck with an iron mallet, causing a scream heard by all except jinn and humans. The angels are gentle with the believer and harsh with the disbeliever. They question each in his own language. Finally, it cites the majority evidence from mutawatir hadith and quotes al-Suyuti's poetic summary that the entire body is revived, not just part. The commentary also clarifies that the gentleness extends even to the sinful believer according to their ranks.

Key Terms
سؤال القبر
منكر ونكير
مطراق من حديد
الثقلين
رجز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some scholars claimed disbelievers are not questioned in the grave.
Correction: The correct view is that everyone, believer or disbeliever, is questioned, as affirmed by Al-Sawi.

Checkpoint
What happens to the disbeliever or hypocrite when asked in the grave?
A) He answers correctly and is shown his seat in Paradise.
B) He says 'I do not know' and is struck with an iron mallet.
C) He remains silent and is left alone.
D) He is transformed into an angel.

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is universal and the response determines one's fate, with the believer rewarded and the disbeliever punished.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the angels were to question you right now, would your answer be confident and certain? What doubts in your heart need to be addressed today?
?
The believer is shown both his seat in Paradise and his seat in Hell as a mercy. Does your current life reflect a preparation for that moment, or are you living as if the grave is not your next destination?
?
The angels ask in your own language. How prepared is your tongue to declare your Lord and His Messenger? What daily habit can you start today to ensure your answer is true?

The Complete Resurrection of the Spirit
Sawi presents the majority opinion on the complete return of the spirit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the majority opinion that Allah returns the entire spirit into the body in the grave, supported by mutawatir hadiths, and the minority view that only part returns.

Core Idea
The spirit returns completely, not partially, according to the majority.

The resurrection of the spirit is a foundational belief about the barzakh. While some held that only half the spirit returns, the overwhelming consensus of Sunni scholars is that the entire spirit is restored. This lesson examines that majority position and the textual evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on spirit return
Start by reading carefully the lines that state Allah returns the spirit completely, and the minority view of half. Then study the commentary's explanation.
2
Identify the two opinions
Note the majority view ('the spirit completely') and the minority view ('it is said: in half'). Recognize that the passage affirms the majority as correct.
The minority is mentioned but not endorsed.
3
Understand the evidence
The commentary cites the majority view based on the apparent meaning of mutawatir hadiths, and quotes al-Suyuti's poetic summary affirming complete revival.
Mutawatir hadiths are those transmitted by many chains, giving certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعيد الله فيه الرُّوحَ بتمامه، وقيل: في نصفه، ويسألانه: «من ربُّك وما دينك؟ وما تقول في الرّجل الذي بعث فيكم؟ فيقول المؤمن : ربِّيَ الله، وديني الإسلام والرَّجلُ المبعوث فينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فيقولان له: انظر مقعدك من النار قد أبدلك الله به مقعدا في الجنة فيراهما جميعاً. وأما المنافق أو الكافر فيقول : لا أدري فيقولان له: «لا دريت ولا تليت»، ويضرب بمطراق من حديد في يد أحدهما، فيصيح صيحة يسمعها من يليه غير الثقلين. ويَتَرفّقان بالمؤمن، ويَنْهران الكافر والمنافق. ويسألان كل أحد بلسانه [؟] لآخر؛ فلا يسئل إلَّا في القبر الذي يبعث منه . قوله : (ويعيد الله الرُّوح فيه تمامه) هذا هو قول الجمهور لظاهر الأحاديث المتواترة، ولذا قال السيوطي: [ من الرجز] وكلُّـه يـحـيـا لـدى الـجـمـهـور لا جزؤه لـظـاهـر الـمـأثـور قوله : (ويترفَّقان بالمؤمن) : أي : ولو عاصياً بحسب تفاوت مراتب المؤمنين.
And Allah returns the spirit into it completely, and it is said: into half of it. And they (the two angels) ask him: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What do you say about the man who was sent among you?' So the believer says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and the man sent among us is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' So they say to him: 'Look at your seat in the Fire; Allah has replaced it for you with a seat in Paradise,' so he sees both of them. As for the hypocrite or the disbeliever, he says: 'I do not know.' So they say to him: 'You do not know and you did not learn.' And they strike him with an iron hammer between his ears, and he screams a scream that is heard by whoever is near him except the two weighty ones (jinn and humans). And they are gentle with the believer, and they are harsh with the disbeliever and the hypocrite. And they ask everyone in their [؟] tongue to the other; so no one is asked except in the grave from which he will be raised. His saying: (And Allah returns the spirit into it completely) — this is the opinion of the majority due to the apparent meaning of the mutawatir hadiths, and thus al-Suyuti said [in rajaz]: 'It is all revived according to the majority, not a part, due to the manifest transmitted reports.' His saying: (And they are gentle with the believer) — i.e., even with a disobedient one, according to the difference in ranks of the believers.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the text of the Sharh al-Kharidah, explaining the resurrection of the spirit and the details of the grave questioning. It begins by stating the majority view that Allah returns the entire spirit into the body, not just part of it, with a minority opinion that it is only half. Then it presents the standard narrative of the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) questioning the deceased. The believer correctly answers the three questions about his Lord, religion, and prophet, and is shown his former place in Hell replaced by Paradise. The hypocrite or disbeliever fails to answer and is struck painfully. The commentary then notes that the angels treat the believer gently, even if he was sinful, according to his rank. The final line notes that every person is asked in the grave from which he will be raised, implying that the questioning is universal. The author cites al-Suyuti's poetic summary affirming the majority view of complete resurrection.

Key Terms
الرُّوح
الجمهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think only half the spirit returns to the body in the grave.
Correction: The majority of scholars hold that the entire spirit returns, based on mutawatir hadiths, as stated in the text.

Checkpoint
According to the majority opinion, what does Allah return into the body in the grave?
A) The spirit completely
B) Only half the spirit
C) Nothing
D) Only the soul

Key Takeaway
The majority of Sunni scholars affirm that Allah returns the entire spirit into the body in the grave, as proven by multiple authentic hadiths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your entire spirit will return to your body in the grave, or do you harbor doubts that affect how you live? If you are certain, why does that certainty not compel you to prepare for that moment every single day?
?
You have just learned that the majority of scholars affirm the complete return of the spirit based on mutawatir hadiths. If you were to die tonight, would your spirit be ready to return to its body with a record you are proud of? What will you change today to ensure that?
?
The mutawatir hadiths give us certainty about the return of the spirit. Are you living as if that return is more real than your next meal? If not, where is the disconnect between what you know and how you live?

The Questioning by the Angels Munkar and Nakir
Sawi narrates the grave questioning by the angels and the responses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the details of the grave questioning: the three questions, the responses of the believer and the disbeliever, the treatment by the angels, and the universal nature of the questioning.

Core Idea
Every soul is questioned in the grave by two angels after death.

One of the core beliefs of Ahl al-Sunna is the questioning in the grave by the angels Munkar and Nakir. This lesson examines the narrative as presented by Sawi: the three questions about Lord, religion, and prophet; the contrasting responses; and the gentle or harsh treatment based on faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the questioning narrative
Read the passage describing the angels' questions and the answers given by the believer and the disbeliever/hypocrite.
2
Contrast the two responses
Notice the believer answers correctly and is shown both his former place in Hell and his new place in Paradise. The disbeliever says 'I do not know' and is struck with an iron hammer.
3
Understand the angels' treatment
The passage says the angels are gentle with the believer (including disobedient ones) and harsh with the disbeliever and hypocrite.
Even a sinful believer receives gentle treatment.
4
Note the universality of the questioning
The final line states that everyone is asked in the grave from which they will be raised, implying that the questioning occurs for all people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعيد الله فيه الرُّوحَ بتمامه، وقيل: في نصفه، ويسألانه: «من ربُّك وما دينك؟ وما تقول في الرّجل الذي بعث فيكم؟ فيقول المؤمن : ربِّيَ الله، وديني الإسلام والرَّجلُ المبعوث فينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فيقولان له: انظر مقعدك من النار قد أبدلك الله به مقعدا في الجنة فيراهما جميعاً. وأما المنافق أو الكافر فيقول : لا أدري فيقولان له: «لا دريت ولا تليت»، ويضرب بمطراق من حديد في يد أحدهما، فيصيح صيحة يسمعها من يليه غير الثقلين. ويَتَرفّقان بالمؤمن، ويَنْهران الكافر والمنافق. ويسألان كل أحد بلسانه [؟] لآخر؛ فلا يسئل إلَّا في القبر الذي يبعث منه . قوله : (ويعيد الله الرُّوح فيه تمامه) هذا هو قول الجمهور لظاهر الأحاديث المتواترة، ولذا قال السيوطي: [ من الرجز] وكلُّـه يـحـيـا لـدى الـجـمـهـور لا جزؤه لـظـاهـر الـمـأثـور قوله : (ويترفَّقان بالمؤمن) : أي : ولو عاصياً بحسب تفاوت مراتب المؤمنين.
And Allah returns the spirit into it completely, and it is said: into half of it. And they (the two angels) ask him: 'Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What do you say about the man who was sent among you?' So the believer says: 'My Lord is Allah, my religion is Islam, and the man sent among us is the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace.' So they say to him: 'Look at your seat in the Fire; Allah has replaced it for you with a seat in Paradise,' so he sees both of them. As for the hypocrite or the disbeliever, he says: 'I do not know.' So they say to him: 'You do not know and you did not learn.' And they strike him with an iron hammer between his ears, and he screams a scream that is heard by whoever is near him except the two weighty ones (jinn and humans). And they are gentle with the believer, and they are harsh with the disbeliever and the hypocrite. And they ask everyone in their [؟] tongue to the other; so no one is asked except in the grave from which he will be raised. His saying: (And Allah returns the spirit into it completely) — this is the opinion of the majority due to the apparent meaning of the mutawatir hadiths, and thus al-Suyuti said [in rajaz]: 'It is all revived according to the majority, not a part, due to the manifest transmitted reports.' His saying: (And they are gentle with the believer) — i.e., even with a disobedient one, according to the difference in ranks of the believers.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the text of the Sharh al-Kharidah, explaining the resurrection of the spirit and the details of the grave questioning. It begins by stating the majority view that Allah returns the entire spirit into the body, not just part of it, with a minority opinion that it is only half. Then it presents the standard narrative of the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) questioning the deceased. The believer correctly answers the three questions about his Lord, religion, and prophet, and is shown his former place in Hell replaced by Paradise. The hypocrite or disbeliever fails to answer and is struck painfully. The commentary then notes that the angels treat the believer gently, even if he was sinful, according to his rank. The final line notes that every person is asked in the grave from which he will be raised, implying that the questioning is universal. The author cites al-Suyuti's poetic summary affirming the majority view of complete resurrection.

منكر ونكير
الجمهور

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the believer see after answering correctly?
A) Only Paradise
B) Only Hell
C) Both his seat in Hell and his seat in Paradise
D) The angels' faces

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is universal: every person is asked about their Lord, religion, and Prophet, and believers are shown their reward while disbelievers are punished.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are alone in your grave and Munkar and Nakir ask you 'Who is your Lord?', will your answer be a confident declaration of faith or a hesitant guess? What are you doing today to make that answer certain?
?
The believer is shown both his former punishment seat in Hell (which he escaped) and his reward in Paradise. Look at your own life: Are you living in a way that you will be shown a reward, or a punishment? What needs to change starting now?
?
The disbeliever is told 'You do not know and you did not learn'. Are you learning what is necessary for your grave—or are you filling your mind with things that will be useless in that moment? Commit to one concrete action this week to learn about your Lord, religion, and Prophet as if your grave depends on it.

The Ruling and Exceptions of the Grave Questioning
Sawi affirms the grave questioning's universality and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the grave questioning occurs regardless of bodily destruction and that prophets, angels, and the siddeeqoon are exempt.

Core Idea
Grave questioning happens whether the body is intact or destroyed.

In this passage, al-Sawi defends the orthodox view that the grave questioning is real and universal, even if the body is completely obliterated. He then notes the exceptions to this rule, showing that not everyone undergoes the same interrogation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on universality
Read the Arabic passage noticing the strong affirmation of the questioning even after complete physical destruction. The author uses extreme examples to stress that nothing prevents it.
The phrase 'even if his limbs are torn apart' sets the tone.
2
Identify the variations in questioning
Notice that the questioning differs: some are asked by two angels, some by one, and the questions vary. This is based on the person's state.
Al-Qurtubi's citation explains the diversity.
3
Understand the exceptions
The passage states that prophets, angels, and siddeeqoon are not questioned. This is a crucial exception.
The siddeeqoon will be defined in a later lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم سؤال القبر على الصحيح، ولو تمزّقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السِّباعُ أو حُرِق وسُحِق وذُرِّي في الهواء، إذ لا يبعد أن يخلق الله تعالى الحياة فيه. وأحوال المسؤولين مختلفة : فمنهم من يسأله الملكان، ومنهم من يسأله أحدهما ، قال القرطبي : اختلفت الأحاديث في كيفية السُّؤال، والجواب : وذلك بحسب الأشخاص، فمنهم مَنْ يُسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومنهم مَن يُسأل عن كلّها) انتهى واختلف في اختصاصه بهذه الأُمَّة، ولا يُسأل الأنبياء ولا الملائكة ولا الصِّدِّيقون . قوله : (على الصحيح) أي : كما هو ظاهر الأحاديث وأقوال السلف، وقيل بالعربيَّة، وقيل: بالسِّريانيَّة (۲) ، والمعتمد : أنَّ السُّؤال مرَّة واحدة للمسلم والمنافق والكافر . وذهب أكثر العلماء إلى أنَّه ثلاث مرات في ساعة واحدة عقب نزوله (۳) وذهب السُّيوطي إلى أنَّه يتكرّر على المؤمن سبعة أيَّام المرَّة الأولى عقب نزوله، والباقي بعد الفجر له (٤) . قوله: (ولا الصِّدِّيقون صديق، ، وهو من صدق الله ورسوله،
The ruling of the grave questioning: on the correct view, even if his limbs are torn apart or beasts eat him or he is burned, crushed, and scattered in the air, since it is not improbable that Allah creates life in it. And the conditions of those questioned are different: among them are those whom the two angels ask, and among them are those whom only one of them asks. Al-Qurtubi said: 'The hadiths differ concerning the manner of the questioning, and the answer [is]: that is according to persons; some are asked about some of their beliefs, and some are asked about all of them.' End. And they differed concerning its being specific to this nation, and prophets, angels, and the siddeeqoon are not asked. His saying: (on the correct view) — i.e., as is apparent from the hadiths and the statements of the Salaf. And it was said [it is] in Arabic, and it was said in Syriac, and the relied-upon [view] is that the questioning is once for the Muslim, the hypocrite, and the disbeliever. And the majority of scholars hold that it is three times in one hour after his descent. And al-Suyuti held that it is repeated for the believer for seven days: the first time after his descent, and the remaining [times] after dawn for him. His saying: (nor the siddeeqoon) — siddeeq is one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the grave questioning, now focusing on its ruling and secondary details. The author first affirms that the questioning occurs even if the body is completely destroyed, as Allah can create life in it. Then he notes that the conditions of the questioned differ: some are asked by both angels, some by only one, and the questions vary according to the individual's state, as cited from al-Qurtubi. The author then mentions a disagreement over whether this questioning is specific to this nation (Ummah), and notes the exception: prophets, angels, and the siddeeqoon are not questioned. Following this, he explains the meaning of the phrase 'on the correct view' in the original text, affirming it is based on hadith and Salaf. He then presents three opinions on the language of the questioning (Arabic, Syriac, or the relied-upon view that it is once) and three opinions regarding the number of times: once (the relied-upon view), three times in one hour (majority), or repeated for seven days (al-Suyuti). Finally, he briefly defines siddeeq as one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger, explaining why they are not questioned.

Key Terms
سؤال القبر
الصِّدِّيقون
القرطبي
الملكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the grave questioning only occurs if the body is intact and not if destroyed or cremated.
Correction: The text explicitly states that it happens even if the body is torn, eaten, burned, crushed, and scattered in the air, because Allah can create life in it.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true according to this passage?
A) The grave questioning only occurs if the body is intact.
B) The grave questioning occurs even after complete bodily destruction.
C) The grave questioning only occurs for Muslims.
D) The grave questioning does not apply to prophets.

Key Takeaway
Grave questioning is universal and occurs even after bodily destruction, but prophets, angels, and siddeeqoon are not questioned.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says prophets, angels, and siddeeqoon are exempt from questioning. You are not among them. How does that reality settle in your soul right now? What change must you make before you face the questioning?
?
The questioning varies according to the person. If you were to be asked only about some of your beliefs, would that be a mercy or a judgment? Examine your own heart: which belief are you least confident in? What will you do about it starting today?

Language, Frequency, and Meaning of Siddeeq
Sawi presents opinions on language and frequency and defines siddeeq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing opinions on the language and frequency of the grave questioning, and the definition of siddeeq.

Core Idea
After affirming its occurrence, scholars debate the language and number of times.

Al-Sawi continues by explaining the phrase 'on the correct view,' then presents the various opinions on whether the questioning occurs in Arabic or Syriac, and how many times it happens—once, thrice, or over seven days. He then defines siddeeq as one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger.

Guided Path
1
Understand the clarification of 'on the correct view'
The phrase is explained as being based on hadith and the statements of the Salaf, indicating the orthodox position.
This grounds the ruling in tradition.
2
Examine the language opinions
Two minority views suggest the questioning is in Arabic or Syriac, but the relied-upon view does not specify a language.
The footnote numbers indicate additional references.
3
Compare the three views on frequency
The text presents three opinions: once, three times in one hour (majority), and seven days (al-Suyuti). The relied-upon view is once.
Notice that the majority opinion is not the relied-upon one.
4
Learn the definition of siddeeq
Siddeeq is defined as one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger, explaining why they are exempt from the questioning.
This complements the exception from Lesson 1.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم سؤال القبر على الصحيح، ولو تمزّقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السِّباعُ أو حُرِق وسُحِق وذُرِّي في الهواء، إذ لا يبعد أن يخلق الله تعالى الحياة فيه. وأحوال المسؤولين مختلفة : فمنهم من يسأله الملكان، ومنهم من يسأله أحدهما ، قال القرطبي : اختلفت الأحاديث في كيفية السُّؤال، والجواب : وذلك بحسب الأشخاص، فمنهم مَنْ يُسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومنهم مَن يُسأل عن كلّها) انتهى واختلف في اختصاصه بهذه الأُمَّة، ولا يُسأل الأنبياء ولا الملائكة ولا الصِّدِّيقون . قوله : (على الصحيح) أي : كما هو ظاهر الأحاديث وأقوال السلف، وقيل بالعربيَّة، وقيل: بالسِّريانيَّة (۲) ، والمعتمد : أنَّ السُّؤال مرَّة واحدة للمسلم والمنافق والكافر . وذهب أكثر العلماء إلى أنَّه ثلاث مرات في ساعة واحدة عقب نزوله (۳) وذهب السُّيوطي إلى أنَّه يتكرّر على المؤمن سبعة أيَّام المرَّة الأولى عقب نزوله، والباقي بعد الفجر له (٤) . قوله: (ولا الصِّدِّيقون صديق، ، وهو من صدق الله ورسوله،
The ruling of the grave questioning: on the correct view, even if his limbs are torn apart or beasts eat him or he is burned, crushed, and scattered in the air, since it is not improbable that Allah creates life in it. And the conditions of those questioned are different: among them are those whom the two angels ask, and among them are those whom only one of them asks. Al-Qurtubi said: 'The hadiths differ concerning the manner of the questioning, and the answer [is]: that is according to persons; some are asked about some of their beliefs, and some are asked about all of them.' End. And they differed concerning its being specific to this nation, and prophets, angels, and the siddeeqoon are not asked. His saying: (on the correct view) — i.e., as is apparent from the hadiths and the statements of the Salaf. And it was said [it is] in Arabic, and it was said in Syriac, and the relied-upon [view] is that the questioning is once for the Muslim, the hypocrite, and the disbeliever. And the majority of scholars hold that it is three times in one hour after his descent. And al-Suyuti held that it is repeated for the believer for seven days: the first time after his descent, and the remaining [times] after dawn for him. His saying: (nor the siddeeqoon) — siddeeq is one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the grave questioning, now focusing on its ruling and secondary details. The author first affirms that the questioning occurs even if the body is completely destroyed, as Allah can create life in it. Then he notes that the conditions of the questioned differ: some are asked by both angels, some by only one, and the questions vary according to the individual's state, as cited from al-Qurtubi. The author then mentions a disagreement over whether this questioning is specific to this nation (Ummah), and notes the exception: prophets, angels, and the siddeeqoon are not questioned. Following this, he explains the meaning of the phrase 'on the correct view' in the original text, affirming it is based on hadith and Salaf. He then presents three opinions on the language of the questioning (Arabic, Syriac, or the relied-upon view that it is once) and three opinions regarding the number of times: once (the relied-upon view), three times in one hour (majority), or repeated for seven days (al-Suyuti). Finally, he briefly defines siddeeq as one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger, explaining why they are not questioned.

الجمهور
السيوطي

A) Once

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon view is that the questioning occurs once, but other views exist, and siddeeqoon are spared due to their truthfulness.

The Reality and Frequency of the Grave Questioning
Affirms the grave questioning and discusses its scope and frequency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of the questioning in the grave, including its universality, the exemption of certain individuals, and the differing scholarly opinions on its frequency.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is real for all but prophets, angels, and the siddiqun.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary affirms the reality of the grave questioning even for bodies that have been destroyed. It addresses who is questioned, by whom, and how many times, while noting that the prophets, angels, and the siddiqun are exempt. The author presents the relied-upon view and also records the differing opinions of scholars on the number of times the questioning occurs.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full translation. This allows the author's own rhythm and argument to come through.
Notice the strong opening statement affirming the ruling.
2
Identify the central affirmation
Note that the questioning is affirmed even for bodies that have been completely destroyed. This shows the power of Allah to recreate life.
This addresses a common doubt about how questioning can occur after disintegration.
3
Note the exemptions
The passage explicitly states that prophets, angels, and the siddiqun are not questioned. Understand that this exemption is a special honor.
4
Compare the opinions on frequency
Three views are presented: once for all, three times in one hour, and seven days for the believer. Identify each view and note which is the relied-upon one.
The relied-upon view is that it occurs once for everyone.
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
Consider why this doctrine matters for Islamic eschatology. It affirms accountability and divine justice even after death.
Connect to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم سؤال القبر على الصحيح، ولو تمزّقت أعضاؤه أو أكلته السِّباعُ أو حُرِق وسُحِق وذُرِّي في الهواء، إذ لا يبعد أن يخلق الله تعالى الحياة فيه. وأحوال المسؤولين مختلفة : فمنهم من يسأله الملكان، ومنهم من يسأله أحدهما ، قال القرطبي : اختلفت الأحاديث في كيفية السُّؤال، والجواب : وذلك بحسب الأشخاص، فمنهم مَنْ يُسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومنهم مَن يُسأل عن كلّها) انتهى واختلف في اختصاصه بهذه الأُمَّة، ولا يُسأل الأنبياء ولا الملائكة ولا الصِّدِّيقون. قوله : على الصحيح) أي : كما هو ظاهر الأحاديث وأقوال السلف، وقيل بالعربيَّة، وقيل: بالسِّريانيَّة ، والمعتمد : أنَّ السُّؤال مرَّة واحدة للمسلم والمنافق والكافر . وذهب أكثر العلماء إلى أنَّه ثلاث مرات في ساعة واحدة عقب نزوله. وذهب السُّيوطي إلى أنَّه يتكرّر على المؤمن سبعة أيَّام المرَّة الأولى عقب نزوله، والباقي بعد الفجر له.
The ruling on the questioning of the grave is correct; even if his limbs are torn apart or beasts eat him or he is burned and ground and scattered in the air, since it is not improbable that Allah the Exalted creates life in it. And the conditions of those questioned vary: among them are those whom the two angels question, and among them are those whom only one of them questions. Al-Qurtubi said: The hadiths differ concerning the manner of the questioning, and the answer is that it is according to the persons, so among them are those who are asked about some of his beliefs, and among them are those who are asked about all of them. He ended. And there is disagreement concerning its being specific to this ummah. And the prophets, angels, and the siddiqun are not questioned. His saying: 'on the correct view' means as is apparent from the hadiths and the statements of the salaf, and it was said in Arabic, and it was said in Syriac. And the relied-upon view is that the questioning is one time for the Muslim, the hypocrite, and the disbeliever. And most scholars went that it is three times in one hour after his descent. And al-Suyuti went that it is repeated for the believer seven days: the first time after his descent, and the remaining after dawn for him.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the ruling on the questioning of the grave, affirming it as correct. It then addresses a potential objection: how can a body that has been destroyed be questioned? The author says that even if the body is completely disintegrated, God can recreate life in it. Then it discusses the varying conditions of those questioned, quoting al-Qurtubi that the nature of the questioning depends on the person. It then mentions disagreement on whether the questioning is specific to this ummah, and lists those who are exempt: prophets, angels, and the siddiqun. The commentary on the phrase 'on the correct view' explains that this is the apparent meaning of hadiths and the salaf, and notes differing opinions on the language of the questioning (Arabic vs Syriac). The relied-upon view is that the questioning occurs once for everyone (Muslim, hypocrite, disbeliever). Then two further opinions are given: most scholars say it occurs three times in one hour after burial; al-Suyuti says it is repeated for the believer over seven days, with the first time immediately after burial and the rest after dawn. The passage thus presents the correct view and acknowledges differences among scholars.

Correction: The passage explicitly states that the questioning occurs for the Muslim, the hypocrite, and the disbeliever.

The Siddiqun and the Murabitun: Truth and Guarding
Defines siddiqun and murabitun as exempted groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two categories of people exempted from the grave questioning: the siddiqun (truthful ones) and the murabitun (frontier guards), and why they are exempt.

Core Idea
Truthfulness and guarding the frontier exempt one from the grave questioning.

Al-Sanusi begins by listing several groups who will not be questioned in the grave. Among the first are the siddiqun, those who are absolutely truthful to Allah and His Messenger, and the murabitun, who dedicate themselves to protecting the Muslim borders. These two categories highlight that both inner sincerity and outer service to the community can earn divine protection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the definitions of siddiq and murabit in Arabic. Notice the concise style of the commentary.
2
Understand the definitions
Siddiq is one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger. Murabit is one who guards the frontier against disbelievers.
3
Reflect on the commonality
Both categories involve extreme devotion: inner truthfulness and outer sacrifice. Why might these exempt from grave questioning?
They represent complete faith and service.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا الصِّدِّيقون) جمع صديق، وهو من صدق الله ورسوله. والمرابطون والشُّهداء وملازم قراءة تبارك كل ليلة، والمبطون، ومن مات في أيام الطاعون ولو لم يُطعن، والمجنون والأبله، وجَزَم الجلال السيوطي بعدم سؤال وأخلص لله ظاهراً وباطناً. قوله : (والمرابطون) جمع مرابط، وهو الملازم طرف بلاد المسلمين لحفظهم من الكفَّار . قوله : (والشُّهداء) : أي : قتلى المعركة أو شهداء الآخرة، وهم فرق كثيرة؛ منهم المبطون الآتي. قوله : (وملازم قراءة تبارك كل ليلة ) : أي : بعد غروب الشمس إلى طلوع الفجر، ويدخل وقتها بالزَّوال، ومثله ملازم قراءة سورة (السجدة). قوله : (والمبطون) : أي : الذي مات بإسهال بطنه، لما ورد : «من قتله بطنه لم يعذَّب في قبره . قوله :(والمجنون) أي: إن جنَّ قبل البلوغ أو بعده وهو مسلم، واستمرَّ به الجنون إلى الموت. قوله : ( والأبله) : هو الذي له عقل لا يصل إلى حدّ تدبير دينه أو دنياه، وهو المغفّل.
His saying: (and the siddiqun) plural of siddiq, and he is the one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger. And the murabitun, and the martyrs, and the one who persists in reciting Tabarak every night, and the one who dies of stomach illness, and the one who dies in the days of plague even if he is not afflicted, and the insane, and the simple-minded. And al-Jalal al-Suyuti asserted the absence of questioning for one who is sincere to Allah outwardly and inwardly. His saying: (and the murabitun) plural of murabit, and he is the one who resides at the frontier of the lands of the Muslims to protect them from the disbelievers. His saying: (and the martyrs) meaning those killed in battle or martyrs of the Hereafter, and they are many types; among them is the one who dies of stomach illness mentioned later. His saying: (and the one who persists in reciting Tabarak every night) meaning after sunset until dawn, and its time enters at noon, and similarly the one who persists in reciting Surah al-Sajdah. His saying: (and the one who dies of stomach illness) meaning the one who dies from diarrhea of his stomach, due to the hadith: 'Whoever is killed by his stomach will not be punished in his grave.' His saying: (and the insane) meaning if he became insane before puberty or after while being Muslim, and the insanity continued until death. His saying: (and the simple-minded) is the one who has intellect that does not reach the level of managing his religion or his worldly affairs, and he is the heedless one.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and definition of those exempt from the questioning in the grave. It begins by commenting on the line 'and the siddiqun', defining a siddiq as one who is truthful to God and His Messenger. Then it lists additional categories: the murabitun (those stationed at frontiers), the martyrs (shuhada'), those who regularly recite Surah Tabarak (al-Mulk) every night, those who die of stomach illness, those who die during a plague even if not infected, the insane, and the simple-minded. It also mentions al-Suyuti's assertion that one who is wholly sincere to God is exempt. The commentary then defines each term: 'murabit' is one who guards the Muslim borders; 'shuhada' includes battlefield martyrs and other types, including those who die of stomach illness; 'persistent recitation of Tabarak' is from sunset to dawn, and similarly for Surah al-Sajdah; 'al-mabtun' is one who dies from diarrhea, citing a hadith that such a person will not be punished in the grave; 'al-majnun' is the insane, whether before or after puberty, as long as the insanity persists to death; 'al-ablah' is the simple-minded, lacking sufficient intellect to manage his affairs. The passage thus provides a detailed list of exemptions based on status, actions, or conditions.

Key Terms
صديق
مرابط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think only major prophets and angels are exempt from grave questioning.
Correction: The passage shows that even ordinary believers can be exempt through specific actions like truthfulness and guarding the frontier.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of a siddiq?
A) One who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger
B) One who guards the frontier
C) One who dies in battle
D) One who recites Surah al-Mulk every night

Key Takeaway
The siddiqun and murabitun are exempt from grave questioning because of their profound truthfulness and selfless service.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you truthfully living up to the level of a siddiq? Reflect on a recent situation where you compromised on truth. Will you commit to being truthful even when it costs you?
?
The murabitun guard the frontiers of Islam. In what ways are you guarding the boundaries of your faith—against doubts, sins, or neglect? What is one step you will take today to strengthen your spiritual vigilance?
?
If you were to face the grave questioning tonight, would you hope to be among the exempted? What evidence in your life supports that hope? Make a firm intention to pursue the qualities of the siddiqun and murabitun starting now.

The Martyrs and Reciters of Tabarak

The passage continues with two more groups: the martyrs (shuhada') and those who steadfastly recite Surah Tabarak every night. Both categories involve extraordinary devotion—either through sacrificing one's life in the path of Allah or through consistent nightly worship.

Martyrs and those who regularly recite Surah al-Mulk and al-Sajdah at night are exempt from grave questioning.

?

Stomach Illness, Plague, and Mental Conditions: Exemptions
Defines exemptions for stomach illness, plague, insanity, simple-mindedness, and sincerity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the exemptions for those who die of stomach illness, plague victims, the insane, the simple-minded, and those who are wholly sincere to Allah.

Core Idea
Death from specific illnesses or mental conditions, as well as complete sincerity, can grant exemption from the grave questioning.

The final part of the list includes several physical and mental conditions that exempt one from the grave trial. From fatal stomach illness to plague, insanity, and simple-mindedness, and concluding with the general category of absolute sincerity mentioned by al-Suyuti, these exemptions show the mercy of Allah in various circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definitions
Read the definitions of mabtun, insane, simple-minded, and the addition by al-Suyuti.
2
Note the hadith for stomach illness
The exemption for stomach illness is supported by a hadith: 'Whoever is killed by his stomach will not be punished in his grave.'
3
Understand conditions for insanity
Insanity must be before or after puberty, the person must be Muslim, and insanity must persist until death.
4
Reflect on al-Suyuti's addition
Absolute sincerity outwardly and inwardly is a general exemption that encompasses many.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا الصِّدِّيقون) جمع صديق، وهو من صدق الله ورسوله. والمرابطون والشُّهداء وملازم قراءة تبارك كل ليلة، والمبطون، ومن مات في أيام الطاعون ولو لم يُطعن، والمجنون والأبله، وجَزَم الجلال السيوطي بعدم سؤال وأخلص لله ظاهراً وباطناً. قوله : (والمرابطون) جمع مرابط، وهو الملازم طرف بلاد المسلمين لحفظهم من الكفَّار . قوله : (والشُّهداء) : أي : قتلى المعركة أو شهداء الآخرة، وهم فرق كثيرة؛ منهم المبطون الآتي. قوله : (وملازم قراءة تبارك كل ليلة ) : أي : بعد غروب الشمس إلى طلوع الفجر، ويدخل وقتها بالزَّوال، ومثله ملازم قراءة سورة (السجدة). قوله : (والمبطون) : أي : الذي مات بإسهال بطنه، لما ورد : «من قتله بطنه لم يعذَّب في قبره . قوله :(والمجنون) أي: إن جنَّ قبل البلوغ أو بعده وهو مسلم، واستمرَّ به الجنون إلى الموت. قوله : ( والأبله) : هو الذي له عقل لا يصل إلى حدّ تدبير دينه أو دنياه، وهو المغفّل.
His saying: (and the siddiqun) plural of siddiq, and he is the one who is truthful to Allah and His Messenger. And the murabitun, and the martyrs, and the one who persists in reciting Tabarak every night, and the one who dies of stomach illness, and the one who dies in the days of plague even if he is not afflicted, and the insane, and the simple-minded. And al-Jalal al-Suyuti asserted the absence of questioning for one who is sincere to Allah outwardly and inwardly. His saying: (and the murabitun) plural of murabit, and he is the one who resides at the frontier of the lands of the Muslims to protect them from the disbelievers. His saying: (and the martyrs) meaning those killed in battle or martyrs of the Hereafter, and they are many types; among them is the one who dies of stomach illness mentioned later. His saying: (and the one who persists in reciting Tabarak every night) meaning after sunset until dawn, and its time enters at noon, and similarly the one who persists in reciting Surah al-Sajdah. His saying: (and the one who dies of stomach illness) meaning the one who dies from diarrhea of his stomach, due to the hadith: 'Whoever is killed by his stomach will not be punished in his grave.' His saying: (and the insane) meaning if he became insane before puberty or after while being Muslim, and the insanity continued until death. His saying: (and the simple-minded) is the one who has intellect that does not reach the level of managing his religion or his worldly affairs, and he is the heedless one.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and definition of those exempt from the questioning in the grave. It begins by commenting on the line 'and the siddiqun', defining a siddiq as one who is truthful to God and His Messenger. Then it lists additional categories: the murabitun (those stationed at frontiers), the martyrs (shuhada'), those who regularly recite Surah Tabarak (al-Mulk) every night, those who die of stomach illness, those who die during a plague even if not infected, the insane, and the simple-minded. It also mentions al-Suyuti's assertion that one who is wholly sincere to God is exempt. The commentary then defines each term: 'murabit' is one who guards the Muslim borders; 'shuhada' includes battlefield martyrs and other types, including those who die of stomach illness; 'persistent recitation of Tabarak' is from sunset to dawn, and similarly for Surah al-Sajdah; 'al-mabtun' is one who dies from diarrhea, citing a hadith that such a person will not be punished in the grave; 'al-majnun' is the insane, whether before or after puberty, as long as the insanity persists to death; 'al-ablah' is the simple-minded, lacking sufficient intellect to manage his affairs. The passage thus provides a detailed list of exemptions based on status, actions, or conditions.

Categories of Those Spared from the Questioning of the Grave
Al-Sawi lists and defines groups exempt from the questioning of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific categories of people who are exempt from the questioning of the grave according to the Ash'ari tradition, as enumerated by al-Sawi.

Core Idea
Several groups are spared grave questioning due to their special circumstances.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary on al-Kharidat identifies those who will not face the questioning in the grave. It lists various categories and provides definitions based on hadith. Let's explore each group and understand why they are exempt.

Guided Path
1
Read the list of exempt categories
Carefully read the initial enumeration of groups: murabitun, shuhada, those who recite Tabarak, etc. Note that the list includes both specific actions and conditions.
The list is comprehensive but each item is explained later.
2
Understand the definitions and conditions
For each category, examine the definition provided by al-Sawi. Notice the conditions that must be met, such as constancy in recitation or the nature of the illness.
Some definitions are tied to hadith evidence cited in the footnotes.
3
Reflect on the hadith evidence
Review the hadith cited for the stomach disease exemption and note that other categories are supported by general principles. Consider how these exceptions demonstrate Allah's mercy.
The hadith for the stomach disease is directly mentioned; other categories have scriptural backing.

والمرابطون والشُّهداء وملازم قراءة تبارك كل ليلة، ومن قرأ في مرض موته الإخلاص ثلاثاً، والمبطون، ومن مات مات في أيام الطاعون ولو لم يُطعن، والمجنون والأبله، وجَزَم الجلال السيوطي بعدم سؤال وأخلص لله ظاهراً وباطناً.

(1) أخرجه الترمذي (۲۸۹۰) عن ابن عباس
(۲) أخرجه الترمذي (١٠٦٤) ، والنسائي في السنن الكبرى (۲۱۹۰) عن سليمان بن صرد وخالد بن عرفطة لها
And those who guard the frontiers, and the martyrs, and the one who constantly reads 'Tabarak' every night, and the one who recites 'al-Ikhlas' three times in his deathbed illness, and the one who dies of a stomach disease, and the one who dies in the days of plague even if not struck by it, and the insane person, and the imbecile; and al-Jalal al-Suyuti asserted that there is no questioning for one who is sincere to God outwardly and inwardly. He said: (Al-Murabitun) plural of murabit, who is the one who stays at the border of Muslim lands to protect them from the disbelievers. He said: (Al-Shuhada) i.e., the killed in battle or the martyrs of the afterlife, and they are many categories; among them is the one who dies of a stomach disease mentioned later. He said: (And the one who constantly reads 'Tabarak' every night) (1): i.e., after sunset until dawn, and its time enters at midday, and similarly the one who constantly reads Surah al-Sajdah. He said: (And the one who dies of a stomach disease): i.e., the one who dies from diarrhoea of his stomach, because it is reported: 'Whoever is killed by his stomach will not be punished in his grave' (2). He said: (And the insane person): i.e., if he goes insane before puberty or after and is Muslim, and the insanity continues until death. He said: (And the imbecile): he who has intellect that does not reach the level of managing his religion or his worldly affairs, and he is the heedless one. (1) Reported by al-Tirmidhi (2890) from Ibn Abbas. (2) Reported by al-Tirmidhi (1064) and al-Nasa'i in al-Sunan al-Kubra (2190) from Sulayman ibn Surad and Khalid ibn 'Urfuta.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that lists categories of people who are exempt from the questioning in the grave, as established by the base text of al-Kharidat. The author begins by enumerating these groups: the murabitun (those stationed at borders), the shuhada (martyrs), those who consistently recite Surah al-Mulk (Tabarak) every night, those who recite Surah al-Ikhlas three times on their deathbed, those who die from a stomach disease, those who die during a plague even if not directly infected, the insane, and the imbecile. He also mentions that Jalal al-Suyuti asserted that those who are sincere to God outwardly and inwardly are not questioned. Then he provides definitions for each term: 'murabitun' means those who guard the borders; 'shuhada' means those killed in battle or martyrs of the afterlife, and they include various types; the one who constantly reads Tabarak does so after sunset until dawn, and its time begins at midday; the one who dies from a stomach disease is spared punishment; the insane person is excused if insanity persists from before or after puberty; the imbecile has insufficient intellect to manage his affairs. The footnotes cite hadith sources for these rulings.

Definition and Locus of the Grave's Bliss and Punishment
Al-Sawi defines the grave's bliss/punishment as barzakh and locates it in soul and body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the bliss and punishment of the grave actually refer to the barzakh state, and that both the soul and body experience it.

Core Idea
The grave's reward and punishment involve both soul and body, even if unseen.

Al-Sawi begins by clarifying that the terms 'bliss of the grave' and 'punishment of the grave' refer to the intermediate state (barzakh) and apply even to those not buried. He then explains that the locus of this experience is both the soul and the body, as Allah can create a partial life in the body to perceive pain or pleasure. This passage establishes the reality of the grave's experience as a spiritual-physical event.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how al-Sawi defines the terms and addresses the locus.
2
Understand the barzakh concept
The passage equates grave punishment with barzakh punishment. Understand that 'grave' is used generally; it applies to everyone in the intermediate state.
The barzakh is the period between death and resurrection.
3
Identify the locus
The author states the locus is both soul and body. Note the proof: Allah can create life in body parts to enable perception without visible signs.
This counters the view that only the soul experiences it.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this doctrine matters: it affirms the reality of punishment/reward in the grave as a sensory experience for the whole person.
It also explains how those eaten by beasts or cremated can still be punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعيم القبر وعذابه
-
أدلَّة السؤال .
نعيم القبر وعذابه
- وكنعيم القبر وعذابه، والمراد عذابُ البرزخ ونعيمه، ولو لم يُقبر، والتّعبير بالقبر جَرْي على الغالب، ومحله الرُّوح والجسد جميعاً، إذ لا مانع أن يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو بعضها نوعاً من الحياة قَدْرَ ما يُدرك ألَمَ العذاب أو لَذَّة النَّعيم، وهذا لا يستلزم أن يتحرَّك أو يضطرب أو يُرى أثر العذاب عليه، حتى إنَّ من أكلته السِّباعُ أو صُلب في الهواء يُعذَّب وإن لم نطلع على ذلك، وقيل : مختص بالرُّوح .
والنّعيم يكون للمؤمنين، والعذاب للكافرين ولعصاة المؤمنين من هذه الأُمَّة وغيرها، وهو قسمان :
دائم، وهو للكفار وبعض العصاة.
- ومنقطع، وهو لبعض العُصاة ممَّن خفت جرائمهم، وانقطاعه : إِما بسب سبب كصدقة أو دعاء، أو بلا سبب بل بمجرَّد العَفْو .
ومن عذاب القبر ضغطتُه : وهي التقاء حافتيه حتّى تختلف أضلاعُ الميت، ويختلف باختلاف العمل، حتى إنّ الصَّالح يضمُّه ضمَّةَ الأمّ
The bliss of the grave and its punishment. Evidence of the questioning. The bliss of the grave and its punishment — and what is meant is the punishment of the barzakh and its bliss, even if he is not buried, and the expression 'grave' is used according to the prevalent case. Its location is both the soul and the body together, for there is no prevention that Allah Most High creates in all the parts or some of them a kind of life to the extent that he perceives the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. This does not necessitate that he moves or is agitated or that the effect of punishment is seen, such that even the one eaten by beasts or crucified in the air is punished even if we are not aware of that. It is said: it is specific to the soul. Bliss is for the believers, and punishment for the disbelievers and for the disobedient believers from this nation and others. It is of two types: eternal, and it is for the disbelievers and some of the disobedient; and temporary, and it is for some of the disobedient whose crimes are light. Its cessation is either due to a cause such as charity or supplication, or without cause but simply by forgiveness. Among the punishment of the grave is its pressure: it is the meeting of its two sides until the ribs of the dead become dislocated, and it varies according to action, such that the righteous person is pressed with the embrace of a mother.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the nature of the bliss and punishment of the grave, which is actually the punishment and bliss of the barzakh (the intermediate state). The author clarifies that the term 'grave' is used because it is the most common case, but it applies even to those not buried. The locus of this experience is both the soul and the body, as Allah can create a partial life in the body parts to perceive pain or pleasure. This does not require visible movement or agitation. He then states that bliss is for believers and punishment for disbelievers and disobedient believers. Punishment is of two types: eternal (for disbelievers and some disobedient) and temporary (for light sinners). Temporary punishment ends either through a cause (charity, supplication) or through mere forgiveness. Finally, he mentions the pressure of the grave (dammat al-qabr), which is a squeezing that dislocates ribs and varies with one's deeds, with the righteous experiencing a gentle embrace.

عذاب القبر
البرزخ

Correction: This passage affirms both soul and body experience it, as Allah creates life in the body parts for perception.

A) Only the soul
B) Only the body
C) Both the soul and the body
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The grave's bliss and punishment are barzakh experiences that involve both the soul and the body, demonstrating Allah's power to create perception without visible signs.

Types of Punishment and the Pressure of the Grave
Al-Sawi classifies grave punishment into eternal/temporary and defines the pressure of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of punishment in the grave (eternal and temporary) and the nature of the grave's pressure (dammat al-qabr).

Core Idea
Punishment in the grave is either eternal for disbelievers or temporary for light sinners, and includes the pressure of the grave varying with deeds.

In the second part of this passage, Al-Sawi categorizes the punishment of the grave: eternal punishment for disbelievers and some disobedient believers, and temporary punishment for those with lighter sins. He then describes the pressure of the grave (dammat al-qabr), a physical squeezing that dislocates the ribs, and notes that it varies according to one's actions. This lesson clarifies the scope and nature of post-mortem punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Pay attention to the two divisions of punishment.
2
Identify the two types
Find where the author divides punishment into 'dā'im' (eternal) and 'munqaṭiʻ' (temporary). Note who each applies to.
Eternal is for disbelievers and some disobedient; temporary is for light sinners.
3
Understand cessation of temporary punishment
Temporary punishment ends either by a cause (charity, supplication) or by mere forgiveness. Reflect on the mercy of Allah.
4
Analyze the pressure of the grave
Learn what dammat al-qabr is: the meeting of the grave's sides causing rib dislocation. Note that it varies based on deeds, with the righteous experiencing a gentle embrace.
This shows punishment is proportional to sin.

It is of two types: eternal, and it is for the disbelievers and some of the disobedient; and temporary, and it is for some of the disobedient whose crimes are light. Its cessation is either due to a cause such as charity or supplication, or without cause but simply by forgiveness. Among the punishment of the grave is its pressure: it is the meeting of its two sides until the ribs of the dead become dislocated, and it varies according to action, such that the righteous person is pressed with the embrace of a mother.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage defines and explains the nature of the bliss and punishment of the grave, which is actually the punishment and bliss of the barzakh (the intermediate state). The author clarifies that the term 'grave' is used because it is the most common case, but it applies even to those not buried. The locus of this experience is both the soul and the body, as Allah can create a partial life in the body parts to perceive pain or pleasure. This does not require visible movement or agitation. He then states that bliss is for believers and punishment for disbelievers and disobedient believers. Punishment is of two types: eternal (for disbelievers and some disobedient) and temporary (for light sinners). Temporary punishment ends either through a cause (charity, supplication) or through mere forgiveness. Finally, he mentions the pressure of the grave (dammat al-qabr), which is a squeezing that dislocates ribs and varies with one's deeds, with the righteous experiencing a gentle embrace.

Key Terms
العذاب الدائم
العذاب المنقطع
ضغطة القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think all punishment in the grave is eternal.
Correction: This passage teaches that punishment is of two types: eternal for disbelievers and some, temporary for light sinners, and can end.

Checkpoint

A) Only by charity
B) Only by supplication
C) Either by a cause (charity/supplication) or by mere forgiveness
D) It never ends

Key Takeaway
Punishment in the grave is not uniform; it is eternal for disbelievers and some sinners, temporary for light sinners, and the pressure of the grave varies with deeds.

The passage says temporary punishment ends by charity or supplication from the living. Name one person who has passed away whom you have not prayed for or given charity on their behalf. Will you set a reminder to do this daily or weekly?
?
If your grave pressure were based on your deeds right now, would you expect a painful dislocation or a loving embrace? What is the first step you will take tonight to tip the balance toward mercy?

The Reality and Locus of Grave Punishment and Bliss
Defines grave punishment and bliss and explains its locus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment and bliss of the grave refer to the barzakh, affect both soul and body, and do not require visible signs.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is real, occurs in the barzakh, and impacts body and soul invisibly.

This lesson clarifies what is meant by grave punishment and bliss, emphasizing that the term 'grave' is a general expression for the intermediate state (barzakh), and that both soul and body are involved. The author dispels the misconception that punishment must be visibly observable.

Guided Path
1
Understand the terminology
Note that 'grave' is used generally for the barzakh; punishment occurs even without burial.
The author explains this in the first sentence.
2
Identify the locus
The punishment and bliss affect both soul and body together, as Allah can create a limited life in body parts.
3
Recognize no visible signs required
The one punished may not move or show outward signs, even if eaten by beasts or crucified.
This refutes those who deny punishment due to lack of visible evidence.
4
Consider the alternative opinion
Some say punishment is specific to the soul only. Note this minority view.
The author presents it but does not endorse it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعيم القبر وعذابه
وكنعيم القبر وعذابه، والمراد عذابُ البرزخ ونعيمه، ولو لم يُقبر، والتّعبير بالقبر جَرْي على الغالب، ومحله الرُّوح والجسد جميعاً، إذ لا مانع أن يخلق الله تعالى في جميع الأجزاء أو بعضها نوعاً من الحياة قَدْرَ ما يُدرك ألَمَ العذاب أو لَذَّة النَّعيم، وهذا لا يستلزم أن يتحرَّك أو يضطرب أو يُرى أثر العذاب عليه، حتى إنَّ من أكلته السِّباعُ أو صُلب في الهواء يُعذَّب وإن لم نطلع على ذلك، وقيل : مختص بالرُّوح . والنّعيم يكون للمؤمنين، والعذاب للكافرين ولعصاة المؤمنين من هذه الأُمَّة وغيرها، وهو قسمان : دائم، وهو للكفار وبعض العُصاة. - ومنقطع، وهو لبعض العُصاة ممَّن خفت جرائمهم، وانقطاعه : إِما بسبب كصدقة أو دعاء، أو بلا سبب بل بمجرَّد العَفْو . ومن عذاب القبر ضغطتُه : وهي التقاء حافتيه حتّى تختلف أضلاعُ الميت، ويختلف باختلاف العمل، حتى إنّ الصَّالح يضمُّه ضمَّةَ الأمّ الشفوقة على ولدها .
قوله : (والمراد عذاب البرزخ) : أي : وإِنَّما أضيف إلى القبر لأنَّه الغالب، وإلا فكل ميت أراد الله تعذيبه عذب قبر أو لم يقبر.
And concerning the bliss of the grave and its punishment: what is meant is the punishment of the Barzakh (intermediary state) and its bliss, even if one is not buried. The expression 'grave' is used as a general rule. Its locus is the soul and the body together, for there is no impediment to Allah Most High creating in all parts or some of them a type of life to the extent that one perceives the pain of punishment or the pleasure of bliss. This does not necessitate that one moves, is agitated, or that the effect of punishment is seen upon him, even to the extent that one devoured by beasts or crucified in the air is punished even if we do not witness that. And it is said it is specific to the soul. Bliss is for the believers, and punishment for the disbelievers and for sinful believers of this nation and others. It is of two types: permanent, which is for the disbelievers and some of the sinners; and temporary, which is for some sinners whose crimes are light. Its cessation is either due to something like charity or supplication, or without cause but merely by pardon. And among the punishments of the grave is its pressure: the meeting of its two sides until the ribs of the dead become interlaced, and it varies according to deeds, to the extent that the righteous person is pressed with the pressing of a compassionate mother upon her child. His saying: 'What is meant is the punishment of the Barzakh' means: it is only attributed to the grave because that is the general rule, otherwise every deceased person whom Allah wills to punish is punished whether buried or not.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage discusses the punishment and bliss of the grave (ʿadhāb al-qabr wa naʿīmuh). It begins by clarifying that the term 'grave' is a general expression for the intermediate state (barzakh); the punishment occurs even if one is not buried. The locus of this experience is both the soul and the body, as Allah can create a limited life in some or all parts to enable perception of pain or pleasure. The author stresses that this does not require visible movement or agitation. He then states that bliss is for believers and punishment for disbelievers and sinful believers. Punishment is divided into permanent (dāʾim) for disbelievers and some sinners, and temporary (munqaṭiʿ) for sinners with light sins, which may cease due to charity, supplication, or sheer pardon. Finally, the passage describes 'pressure of the grave' (ḍaghṭ al-qabr), where the grave's sides meet and interlock the ribs, varying with one's deeds—even the righteous are pressed, akin to a mother's affectionate embrace.

نعيم القبر
البرزخ

Correction: The author states that both soul and body are affected, as Allah can create life in body parts for perception.

Types of Grave Punishment and the Pressure of the Grave
Explains types of grave punishment and the pressure of the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two types of grave punishment (permanent and temporary) and the concept of grave pressure (ḍaghṭ al-qabr) and how it varies by deeds.

Core Idea
Grave punishment varies: permanent for disbelievers, temporary for some sinners; even the righteous experience pressure.

This lesson explores the classification of grave punishment into permanent and temporary, explaining how temporary punishment may cease. It then describes the pressure of the grave, a physical compression that differs according to one's deeds, showing that even the righteous are pressed gently like a mother's embrace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of punishment
Permanent punishment is for disbelievers and some sinners; temporary is for light-sinning believers.
2
Understand how temporary punishment ends
It ceases due to charity, supplication, or sheer pardon from Allah.
No specific reason needed for cessation.
3
Learn about grave pressure
The grave's sides meet, interlocking ribs; it varies with deeds.
Even the righteous experience it, but gently.
4
Connect to the broader principle
The author reiterates that punishment is not limited to burial; it is general for the barzakh.
The final sentence reinforces earlier point.

Martyrs: Alive in Their Graves
Defines martyrs' special life, sustenance, and name meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the special life of martyrs in the grave, their sustenance, the meaning of their name, and the intention required for their complete reward.

Core Idea
Martyrs enjoy a hidden life with Allah, beyond human comprehension.

This lesson examines the Quranic declaration that martyrs are not dead but alive. It clarifies who qualifies as a martyr, what their life entails, and why they are called shuhadā’. The passage also distinguishes between worldly and spiritual rulings based on intention.

Guided Path
1
Define the martyr
The passage begins by identifying martyrs as those killed in jihad to elevate Allah's word. Note the important condition of sincere intention.
Intention matters: fighting for worldly gain gives only worldly rulings.
2
Understand their life
Read the Quranic verse (3:169) which affirms they are alive and provided for. The modality of this life is unknown and beyond human perception.
This life includes eating, drinking, and delighting in Paradise.
3
Learn the etymology
The passage gives two possible reasons for the name 'shahīd': they witness Paradise, or Allah and angels witness their final state.
This explains the special status of martyrs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشهداء أحياء في قبورهم
وكحياة الشُّهداء، وهم من قتلوا في جهاد الكفَّار لإعلاء كلمة الله تعالى، حتى إنهم يأكلون ويشربون ويتنعمون في الجنَّة قال تعالى (وَلَا تَحْسَبَنَّ الَّذِينَ قُتِلُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ أَمْوَتَّاً بَلْ أَحْيَاءٌ عِندَ رَبِّهِمْ يُرْزَقُونَ )) وإن لم تُعلّم كيفية هذه الحياة، إذ هي غير معقولة لأكثر البشر. وسُمُّوا شهداء لأنَّ أرواحهم شَهِدت دارَ السَّلام؛ أي: حضرتها ودخلتها، بخلاف غيرهم فإنَّه لا يدخلها إلا يوم القيامة، أو لأنّ الله وملائكته شهدوا له بالموافاة.
قوله : (في جهاد الكفَّار مثله من قتل على الحقِّ؛ كقتال البغاة، وقطَّاع الطريق، وإقامة الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر. قوله : (الإعلاء كلمة الله : أخرج به من قاتل لا لإعلاء كلمة الله، بل للغنيمة، أو لإظهار الشَّجاعة ؛ فإنَّ له حكم شهداء الدُّنيا من عدم غسلهم والصَّلاة عليهم لا ثوابهم الكامل.
And concerning the life of the martyrs: they are those who were killed in jihad against the disbelievers to elevate the word of Allah Most High, such that they eat, drink, and delight in Paradise. He says: 'Do not consider those who were killed in the way of Allah as dead; rather, they are alive with their Lord, receiving provision' (Q.3:169). Even if the modality of this life is not known, for it is incomprehensible to most humans. They are called 'martyrs' (shuhadāʾ) because their souls witnessed (shahidat) the Abode of Peace (Dār al-Salām), i.e., they attended and entered it, unlike others who do not enter it until the Day of Resurrection; or because Allah and His angels bore witness (shahidū) to his final state. His saying: 'In jihad against the disbelievers' – similarly, anyone killed for the truth, such as fighting against rebels, highway robbers, and establishing commanding good and forbidding evil. His saying: 'To elevate the word of Allah' excludes one who fights not to elevate Allah's word but for booty or to show courage; such a person has the worldly ruling of the martyrs (not to be washed or prayed upon) but not their complete reward.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage explains the life of martyrs (shuhadāʾ) in the grave. It begins by identifying martyrs as those killed in jihad against disbelievers with the sincere intention of elevating Allah's word. It then describes their state: they eat, drink, and enjoy Paradise, citing Quran 3:169. The author notes that the modality of this life is unknown and beyond human comprehension. He then explains the etymology of 'shuhadāʾ': they witness the Abode of Peace, entering it before others, or because Allah and angels witness their final state. The marginal commentary clarifies that the category extends to anyone killed for the truth (e.g., fighting rebels, highway robbers, or in enjoining good). It also distinguishes intention: those fighting for worldly gain receive the worldly rulings of martyrs (no washing, no prayer) but not the full spiritual reward.

The Taking of Records on the Day of Judgment
Enumerates recipients of records and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that all accountable beings (humans and jinn) receive their record of deeds from guardian angels on the Day of Judgment, except the prophets and a special group who enter Paradise without account.

Core Idea
Every accountable soul receives its book of deeds, but some are exempt from the reckoning.

On the Day of Judgment, every accountable being will be given a record of their deeds, written by the guardian angels. However, divine mercy has singled out the prophets and a blessed seventy thousand who will enter Paradise without any account. This passage introduces this foundational belief and sets the stage for understanding the broader scene of the Hereafter.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the brief, dense style typical of creedal summaries.
The passage cuts off at 'bil-aymān', likely describing distribution by right/left hand.
2
Identify the general rule and its exceptions
The passage states that all accountable beings (the 'two heavy ones'—jinn and humans) take their records. Then it excludes the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account.
These exceptions show that not everyone undergoes the same accounting process.
3
Reflect on the role of the guardian angels
The guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓa) are the ones who recorded every deed in the world. Their records are the basis for the books given on Judgment Day.
This underscores the perfection of divine justice: every deed is preserved.
4
Consider the significance of the exceptions
Why are prophets and these seventy thousand exempt? This teaches us about Allah's mercy and the high station of prophethood.
It also encourages believers to strive for that blessed group.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذ العباد الصحف - وكأخذ العباد المكلَّفين من الثَّقلين في المحشر، ما عدا الأنبياء والسَّبعين ألفاً كتبت فيها الذين يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب، كتبهم . الملائكةُ الحَفَظَةُ أعمالهم التي صدرت عنهم في الدُّنيا، بالأيمان
The taking of the records - And like the taking by the accountable servants from the two heavy ones (jinn and humans) in the gathering place, except the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account, their records. The guardian angels [record] their deeds that issued from them in the world, with the right hands [or oaths].
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage discusses the event of receiving records (ṣuḥuf) on the Day of Judgment. It states that all accountable beings—both humans and jinn—will receive their records in the gathering place (maḥshar). An exception is made for the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account: they do not undergo this accounting. The records are written by the guardian angels (al-ḥafaẓa), who recorded all deeds performed in the world. The final word 'bil-aymān' is ambiguous; it likely means 'with the right hands' (i.e., the righteous receive their records in their right hand) or 'oaths' (as in confirmation). The passage is cut short, but it clearly asserts the doctrine that every accountable being will be given their book of deeds.

Key Terms
الصحف
المحشر
الملائكة الحفظة
الحساب
الثقلين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everyone will be held to account and receive a record of deeds.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that prophets and seventy thousand are exempt from taking records, showing that some are honored by being spared the accounting.

Checkpoint

B) The prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account
C) Only the prophets
D) No one is exempt

Key Takeaway
On Judgment Day, all accountable beings receive their books of deeds, but Allah exempts the prophets and seventy thousand from this accounting as a special mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that every deed you do—every thought, word, and action—is being recorded by the guardian angels right now. If your book were handed to you today, would you be pleased or terrified? What one deed will you change today so that your record holds something you are proud to present?
?
The seventy thousand enter Paradise without any account, yet the prophets—the best of creation—are also exempt. Do you long for that exemption? What have you done today that shows you are striving to be among those who are saved from the reckoning?
?
You will stand before Allah with your book open. The prophets and the seventy thousand are exempt, but you are not guaranteed that. Are you living as though you will be called to account for every moment? What will you do before you sleep tonight to prepare for that day?
