The Giving of Records on Judgment Day
Al-Sawi describes the process of record distribution on Judgment Day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed Islamic belief regarding the distribution of records on Judgment Day, including the process, the exceptions, the first recipients, and the nature of the book.

Core Idea
Your record of deeds finds you on Judgment Day — and its brightness mirrors your faith.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary describes one of the dramatic scenes of the Hereafter: the giving of the books of deeds. It explains how every accountable soul receives a scroll containing their life's record, how it reaches them, and who are the first to receive theirs. The details reinforce the justice and mercy of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the English translation to get the overall flow of the narrative.
Notice the sequence of events described.
2
Identify the exceptions
Find who does not receive a book in this manner: the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account. Understand their special status.
This highlights Allah's mercy.
3
Trace the process step by step
Outline the process: deeds compiled into one sheet, stored under the Throne, a wind sends each sheet to its owner's neck, angels take them and hand them out according to faith.
The process ensures everyone gets their own record.
4
Learn the first recipients
Memorize the names: Umar ibn al-Khattab is the absolute first to receive his book in his right hand, Abu Bakr is chief of the seventy thousand, and others follow.
The first to receive in the left hand is al-Aswad.
5
Reflect on the first line of the book
Consider the meaning of the verse: 'Read your book; sufficient is yourself against you today.' How does this demand self-accountability?
This is a direct address to the soul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكأخذ العباد المكلَّفين من الثَّقلين في المحشر، ما عدا الأنبياء والسَّبعين ألفاً الذين يدخلون الجنة بغير حساب، كتبهم الملائكةُ الحَفَظَةُ أعمالهم التي صدرت عنهم في الدُّنيا، بالأيمان. وحاصل ما قيل في ذلك : أنّ صحائف الأيام والليالي توصل حتى تكون صحيفة واحدة، وقيل : يُنسخ ما في جميعها في صحيفة واحدة، فإذا مات العبد جُعِلَت في خزانة تحت العرش، حتّى إذا كان يوم القيامة والنَّاسُ في الموقف بعث الله تعالى ريحاً فتطيرُها من تلك الخزانة، فلا تخطئ صحيفةٌ عُنق صاحبها . ثمَّ تأخذها الملائكة من الأعناق فيعطونها لهم في أيديهم على حسب حالهم من إيمان أو كفر ، فالمؤمن يُعطى كتابه بيمينه والكافرُ بشماله، ويُثقب صدرُه فَيُدخِل يده اليسرى فيه ويأخذ كتابه من وراء ظهره . وأوَّلُ من يأخذ كتابه بيمينه على الإطلاق عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله عنه وله شعاعٌ كالشَّمس، وأما أبو بكر فهو رئيس السبعين ألفاً الذين يدخلون الجَنَّة بغير حساب، وبعد عمر أبو سلمة عبد بن عبد الأسد المخزومي له ، وأوَّلُ من يأخذه بشماله أخوه الأسود بن عبد الأسد المخزومي. ثمَّ إذا أخذ العبد كتابه وَجَدَ حروفَه نَيّرَةً أو مُظلمةً على حسب الأعمال الحسنة أو القبيحة، وأوَّلُ خطّ فيها اقْرَأْ كِتَبَكَ كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ
And like the taking of the records of the obligated servants from the two weighty (jinn and humans) in the gathering place, except for the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account. Their books are taken by the guardian angels of their deeds that issued from them in the world, by the right hands. The summary of what is said about that is: the sheets of days and nights are joined until they become one sheet, or it is said: what is in all of them is copied into one sheet. When the servant dies, it is placed in a treasury under the Throne. Then on the Day of Resurrection when people are in the standing place, Allah sends a wind that makes them fly from that treasury, and no sheet misses the neck of its owner. Then the angels take them from the necks and give them to them in their hands according to their state of faith or disbelief. The believer is given his book in his right hand, and the disbeliever in his left, and his chest is pierced so he inserts his left hand into it and takes his book from behind his back. The very first to take his book in his right hand is Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, and he has a radiance like the sun. As for Abu Bakr, he is the chief of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account. After Umar is Abu Salama Abd ibn Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi. And the first to take it in his left hand is his brother al-Aswad ibn Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi. Then when the servant takes his book, he finds its letters bright or dark according to good or bad deeds. The first line in it is: 'Read your book; sufficient is yourself against you.'
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage explains the process of the taking of records (suhuf) on Judgment Day. It begins by stating that the books of deeds are given to all accountable servants (jinn and humans) except the prophets and the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning. The guardian angels (al-mala'ika al-hafaza) present the books in their right hands. Then, al-Sawi summarizes the tradition: the daily and nightly deeds are combined into one scroll, or copied into one scroll, which is kept in a treasury beneath the Throne. On Judgment Day, a wind from Allah sends each scroll to its owner's neck. Angels then take the scrolls from the necks and hand them out according to the person's faith: the believer receives it in his right hand, the disbeliever in his left, and his chest is pierced so he takes it from behind. Next, the author mentions the first recipients: Umar ibn al-Khattab is the absolute first to take his book in his right hand, with a radiant light like the sun. Abu Bakr is the chief of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account. After Umar comes Abu Salama al-Makhzumi. The first to receive his book in his left hand is al-Aswad ibn Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi (Umar's brother from the mother's side). Finally, the passage describes that the letters of the book are either bright or dark according to the person's deeds, and the first line they read is 'Read your book; sufficient is yourself against you today' (referring to Quran 17:14 or similar).

Key Terms
صحف
أخذ الكتاب
يمين
شمال
عمر بن الخطاب
أبو بكر
أبو سلمة
الأسود بن عبد الأسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think all believers receive their books first, but this passage specifies that Umar is the absolute first.
Correction: While all believers receive their book in the right hand, Umar ibn al-Khattab is the first to do so, and he has a special radiance.

Checkpoint
Who is the very first person to take his book of deeds in his right hand according to this passage?
A) Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
B) The Prophet Muhammad
C) Umar ibn al-Khattab
D) Abu Salama

Key Takeaway
On Judgment Day, everyone receives their personal record of deeds, and the first to receive his in the right hand is Umar ibn al-Khattab.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your record were given to you right now, would the first letter be bright or dark? What specific sin would you be most terrified to see illuminated? Before you sleep tonight, repent from that sin with a commitment never to return.
?
The first line you will read is 'Read your book; sufficient is yourself against you.' Your own deeds will testify. What is one habit you are neglecting today that will make that reading painful? Decide now to change it starting this week.
?
Umar ibn al-Khattab received his book with radiance like the sun. What quality of his faith do you lack that would make your own record bright? Ask Allah tonight to grant you that quality and act on it tomorrow.

The Giving of the Books: Process and Recipients
Al-Sawi explains the process of giving the books on Judgment Day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the process by which the scrolls of deeds are given to people on Judgment Day, including the combining of scrolls and the roles of angels.

Core Idea
Every deed is recorded, and on Judgment Day, each soul receives its scroll directly.

Al-Sawi begins by quoting Quranic verses about receiving the book in the right hand or behind the back. Then he summarizes scholarly opinions on how the scrolls of days and nights are combined into one scroll per person, kept under the Throne until Judgment Day, when a wind brings each scroll to its owner. This lesson covers the general process.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses
Read the opening verses (84:7-12) quoted in the Arabic passage. Notice the contrast between receiving the book in the right hand vs. behind the back.
This sets the scriptural foundation.
2
Understand the scroll combination
Study how the daily and nightly scrolls are combined into one, either by connecting or copying. This is based on scholarly interpretation.
3
Trace the journey of the scroll
Follow the path: after death, the scroll is stored under the Throne; on Judgment Day, Allah sends a wind that brings each scroll to its owner's neck; angels then place it in the person's hand.
Notice the precise sequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذ العباد الصحف والشَّمائل فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَبَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا وَسَنقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُورًا وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَبَهُ وَرَآءَ ظَهْرِهِ فَسَوْفَ يَدْعُوا ثُبُورًا وَيَصْلَى سَعِيرًا (١) وحاصل ما قيل في ذلك : أنّ صحائف الأيام والليالي توصل حتى تكون صحيفة واحدة، وقيل : يُنسخ ما في جميعها في صحيفة واحدة، فإذا مات العبد جُعِلَت في خزانة تحت العرش، حتّى إذا كان يوم القيامة والنَّاسُ في الموقف بعث الله تعالى ريحاً فتطيرُها من تلك الخزانة، فلا تخطئ صحيفةٌ عُنق صاحبها . ثمَّ تأخذها الملائكة من الأعناق فيعطونها لهم في أيديهم على حسب حالهم من إيمان أو كفر ، فالمؤمن يُعطى كتابه بيمينه والكافرُ بشماله، ويُثقب صدرُه فَيُدخِل يده اليسرى فيه ويأخذ كتابه من وراء ظهره . وأوَّلُ من يأخذ كتابه بيمينه على الإطلاق عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله وله شعاعٌ كالشَّمس، وأما أبو بكر فهو رئيس السبعين ألفاً الذين يدخلون الجَنَّة بغير حساب، وبعد عمر أبو سلمة عبد بن عبد الأسد عبد الله المخزومي له ، وأوَّلُ من يأخذه بشماله أخوه الأسود بن عبد الأسد المخزومي. ثمَّ إذا أخذ العبد كتابه وَجَدَ حروفَه نَيّرَةً أو مُظلمةً على حسب الأعمال الحسنة أو القبيحة، وأوَّلُ خطّ فيها اقْرَأْ كِتَبَكَ كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ حَسِيبًا ) فإذا قرأه ابيض وجهه إن كان مؤمناً، واسود إن كان كافراً، وذلك قوله تعالى : يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوةٌ ... الآية . ويخلق الله تعالى له عِلْمَ القراءة وإن لم يكن يقرأ في الدُّنيا والصَّحيحُ : أنّ عصاة المؤمنين يأخذون صحائفهم بأيمانهم، ويكون علامة على دخولهم الجنَّة، ولو بعد دخولهم النار .
The people take the scrolls and the qualities. So as for one who is given his book in his right hand, he will be judged an easy judgment and return to his family joyful. And as for one who is given his book behind his back, he will call out for destruction and burn in a blaze (Quran 84:7-12). The summary of what has been said about that: that the scrolls of days and nights are connected until they become one scroll, and it is said: what is in all of them is copied into one scroll. When the servant dies, it is placed in a treasure under the Throne, until when the Day of Resurrection comes and the people are at the standing place, Allah sends a wind that flies them from that treasure, and no scroll misses the neck of its owner. Then the angels take them from the necks and give them to them in their hands according to their state of faith or disbelief. So the believer is given his book in his right hand, and the disbeliever in his left, and his chest is pierced and he inserts his left hand into it and takes his book from behind his back. And the first to take his book in his right hand unconditionally is Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, and he has a radiance like the sun. As for Abu Bakr, he is the leader of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning. After Umar is Abu Salama Abd bin Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi. And the first to take it with his left hand is his brother al-Aswad bin Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi. Then when the servant takes his book, he finds its letters luminous or dark according to good or evil deeds. And the first line in it is: 'Read your book! Sufficient is your soul today as a reckoner against you' (Quran 17:14). So when he reads it, his face becomes white if he is a believer, and black if he is a disbeliever. And that is the word of Allah: 'On the day when faces become white and faces become black...' (Quran 3:106). And Allah creates for him knowledge of reading even if he did not read in the world. And the correct view: that the sinful believers take their scrolls in their right hands, and it is a sign of their entry into Paradise, even if after entering the Fire.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage explains the process of giving the books (suhuf) to people on Judgment Day. It begins by quoting Quranic verses about receiving the book in the right hand versus behind the back. Then it summarizes scholarly opinions: the daily and nightly scrolls are combined into one, or their contents are copied into one scroll. After death, the scroll is kept in a treasury under the Throne until the Day of Resurrection, then a wind brings each scroll to its owner's neck. Angels then give the scrolls to people based on faith or disbelief: the believer receives it in his right hand, the disbeliever in his left, and the disbeliever's chest is pierced to take it from behind. Then it mentions the first person to receive his book in his right hand unconditionally is Umar ibn al-Khattab, while Abu Bakr is the leader of the 70,000 who enter Paradise without reckoning. Others follow. The first to receive with his left hand is al-Aswad ibn Abd al-Aswad al-Makhzumi. Then the passage describes that letters appear luminous or dark based on deeds. Upon reading, the face becomes white for believers and black for disbelievers. Allah creates knowledge of reading for them. The correct view is that sinful believers receive their scrolls in their right hands, indicating eventual entry into Paradise even if they enter Hell first.

Key Terms
صحف
كتاب
يمين
شمال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the scrolls are only given to the righteous.
Correction: The passage clearly states that everyone receives their scroll—believers and disbelievers alike, but in different hands.

Checkpoint
What happens to the scroll after a person dies according to the passage?
A) It is destroyed.
B) It is placed in a treasury under the Throne.
C) It is given to the family.
D) It is kept with the angels.

Key Takeaway
The giving of the book on Judgment Day is a precise, divinely orchestrated process where each soul receives its own scroll according to faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew that every moment of your day is being recorded and will be presented to you as one scroll, would you change anything about how you spend your time starting today?
?
The believer receives the book in the right hand with joy. Do you live your life in a way that would give you confidence in that moment, or do you avoid thinking about it?
?
The disbeliever's chest is pierced to take the book from behind. What does that image evoke in you about the consequences of neglecting faith, and what will you do today to ensure you are not among them?

First Recipients of the Scrolls
Al-Sawi names the first individuals to receive their scrolls on Judgment Day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the specific individuals mentioned as the first to receive their scrolls on Judgment Day and their ranks.

Core Idea
Among all people, Umar ibn al-Khattab is the first to receive his scroll in the right hand unconditionally.

After describing the general giving process, Al-Sawi highlights specific individuals who are the first to receive their scrolls. He mentions Umar ibn al-Khattab as the first unconditionally, and Abu Bakr as the leader of those who enter Paradise without reckoning. He also notes the first person to receive with the left hand. This lesson focuses on these named examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first on the right
Find the part where Al-Sawi says 'the first to take his book in his right hand unconditionally is Umar.' Note the qualification 'unconditionally' (ʿalā al-iṭlāq).
This distinguishes Umar from others who might be first in a restricted sense.
2
Understand Abu Bakr's unique rank
Read that Abu Bakr is the leader of the 70,000 who enter Paradise without reckoning. This is a separate honor, not directly about being first to receive the scroll.
Thus Abu Bakr's status is different from Umar's in this context.
3
Note the first on the left
Al-Sawi also mentions the first to receive with the left hand: al-Aswad ibn Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi.
This shows that even the disbelievers have a 'first' in terms of receiving.

The correct view is that sinful believers receive their scrolls in their right hands, indicating eventual entry into Paradise even if they enter Hell first.

Signs of the Scroll: Luminous Letters and Faces
Al-Sawi describes the appearance of the scroll and the faces, and the ruling for sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the signs that appear on the scrolls and on the faces of people when they receive their books on Judgment Day, and the ruling on sinful believers.

Core Idea
The letters on the scroll shine or darken based on deeds, and faces reflect the state of faith when the scroll is read.

After describing the giving process and the first recipients, Al-Sawi explains the internal signs of the scroll itself. He states that the letters appear luminous or dark according to good or evil deeds. The first line of every scroll is the Qur'anic verse 'Read your book!'. Then, upon reading, the face of a believer becomes white and that of a disbeliever becomes black. Finally, he clarifies the correct view: sinful believers also receive their scrolls in the right hand, indicating eventual Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Observe the condition of the letters
Read that when the servant takes his scroll, he finds the letters either luminous or dark, corresponding to his deeds.
This shows that the scroll itself contains visible evidence of one's actions.
2
Note the first line of the scroll
The first line written is the command: 'Read your book! Sufficient is your soul today as a reckoner against you.'
This emphasizes self-accountability.
3
Understand the transformation of faces
Upon reading, the believer's face becomes white, the disbeliever's black. This is a physical sign of inner state.
Connected to Quran 3:106.
4
Learn the ruling on sinful believers
Al-Sawi states the correct view: sinful believers (ʿuṣāt al-muʾminīn) take their scrolls in their right hands as a sign they will eventually enter Paradise, even if they enter Hell first.
This clarifies a common point of confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذ العباد الصحف والشَّمائل فَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَبَهُ بِيَمِينِهِ فَسَوْفَ يُحَاسَبُ حِسَابًا يَسِيرًا وَسَنقَلِبُ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ مَسْرُورًا وَأَمَّا مَنْ أُوتِيَ كِتَبَهُ وَرَآءَ ظَهْرِهِ فَسَوْفَ يَدْعُوا ثُبُورًا وَيَصْلَى سَعِيرًا (١) وحاصل ما قيل في ذلك : أنّ صحائف الأيام والليالي توصل حتى تكون صحيفة واحدة، وقيل : يُنسخ ما في جميعها في صحيفة واحدة، فإذا مات العبد جُعِلَت في خزانة تحت العرش، حتّى إذا كان يوم القيامة والنَّاسُ في الموقف بعث الله تعالى ريحاً فتطيرُها من تلك الخزانة، فلا تخطئ صحيفةٌ عُنق صاحبها . ثمَّ تأخذها الملائكة من الأعناق فيعطونها لهم في أيديهم على حسب حالهم من إيمان أو كفر ، فالمؤمن يُعطى كتابه بيمينه والكافرُ بشماله، ويُثقب صدرُه فَيُدخِل يده اليسرى فيه ويأخذ كتابه من وراء ظهره . وأوَّلُ من يأخذ كتابه بيمينه على الإطلاق عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله وله شعاعٌ كالشَّمس، وأما أبو بكر فهو رئيس السبعين ألفاً الذين يدخلون الجَنَّة بغير حساب، وبعد عمر أبو سلمة عبد بن عبد الأسد عبد الله المخزومي له ، وأوَّلُ من يأخذه بشماله أخوه الأسود بن عبد الأسد المخزومي. ثمَّ إذا أخذ العبد كتابه وَجَدَ حروفَه نَيّرَةً أو مُظلمةً على حسب الأعمال الحسنة أو القبيحة، وأوَّلُ خطّ فيها اقْرَأْ كِتَبَكَ كَفَى بِنَفْسِكَ الْيَوْمَ عَلَيْكَ حَسِيبًا ) فإذا قرأه ابيض وجهه إن كان مؤمناً، واسود إن كان كافراً، وذلك قوله تعالى : يَوْمَ تَبْيَضُ وُجُوهٌ وَتَسْوَدُّ وُجُوةٌ ... الآية . ويخلق الله تعالى له عِلْمَ القراءة وإن لم يكن يقرأ في الدُّنيا والصَّحيحُ : أنّ عصاة المؤمنين يأخذون صحائفهم بأيمانهم، ويكون علامة على دخولهم الجنَّة، ولو بعد دخولهم النار .
The people take the scrolls and the qualities. So as for one who is given his book in his right hand, he will be judged an easy judgment and return to his family joyful. And as for one who is given his book behind his back, he will call out for destruction and burn in a blaze (Quran 84:7-12). The summary of what has been said about that: that the scrolls of days and nights are connected until they become one scroll, and it is said: what is in all of them is copied into one scroll. When the servant dies, it is placed in a treasure under the Throne, until when the Day of Resurrection comes and the people are at the standing place, Allah sends a wind that flies them from that treasure, and no scroll misses the neck of its owner. Then the angels take them from the necks and give them to them in their hands according to their state of faith or disbelief. So the believer is given his book in his right hand, and the disbeliever in his left, and his chest is pierced and he inserts his left hand into it and takes his book from behind his back. And the first to take his book in his right hand unconditionally is Umar ibn al-Khattab, may Allah be pleased with him, and he has a radiance like the sun. As for Abu Bakr, he is the leader of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning. After Umar is Abu Salama Abd bin Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi. And the first to take it with his left hand is his brother al-Aswad bin Abd al-Asad al-Makhzumi. Then when the servant takes his book, he finds its letters luminous or dark according to good or evil deeds. And the first line in it is: 'Read your book! Sufficient is your soul today as a reckoner against you' (Quran 17:14). So when he reads it, his face becomes white if he is a believer, and black if he is a disbeliever. And that is the word of Allah: 'On the day when faces become white and faces become black...' (Quran 3:106). And Allah creates for him knowledge of reading even if he did not read in the world. And the correct view: that the sinful believers take their scrolls in their right hands, and it is a sign of their entry into Paradise, even if after entering the Fire.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage explains the process of giving the books (suhuf) to people on Judgment Day. It begins by quoting Quranic verses about receiving the book in the right hand versus behind the back. Then it summarizes scholarly opinions: the daily and nightly scrolls are combined into one, or their contents are copied into one scroll. After death, the scroll is kept in a treasury under the Throne until the Day of Resurrection, then a wind brings each scroll to its owner's neck. Angels then give the scrolls to people based on faith or disbelief: the believer receives it in his right hand, the disbeliever in his left, and the disbeliever's chest is pierced to take it from behind. Then it mentions the first person to receive his book in his right hand unconditionally is Umar ibn al-Khattab, while Abu Bakr is the leader of the 70,000 who enter Paradise without reckoning. Others follow. The first to receive with his left hand is al-Aswad ibn Abd al-Aswad al-Makhzumi. Then the passage describes that letters appear luminous or dark based on deeds. Upon reading, the face becomes white for believers and black for disbelievers. Allah creates knowledge of reading for them. The correct view is that sinful believers receive their scrolls in their right hands, indicating eventual entry into Paradise even if they enter Hell first.

The First Intercession: Relief from the Standing
Al-Sawi describes the first type of intercession and its unique status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first type of the Prophet's intercession, its specificity, and the events surrounding it on Judgment Day.

Core Idea
The first intercession relieves all of creation from the hardship of waiting.

This passage from al-Sawi explains the first and most universal intercession of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ). Unlike other forms of intercession, this one is specific to him and brings relief to every soul on the Day of Judgment. As we read, pay attention to the dramatic narrative of how people seek help from the prophets until they finally approach the Prophet, who accepts the task.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation. Notice the key terms: الشفاعة, المقام المحمود, لواء, ذؤابة.
The passage contains a narrative of events on Judgment Day.
2
Identify the first type of intercession
Find the definition of the first type: it is for relief from the standing. Understand that it is specific to the Prophet by consensus.
3
Follow the narrative of the prophets
Trace the sequence: people go to Adam, Noah, etc., each excuses themselves, until they reach Muhammad. Notice each prophet's response.
This shows the unique status of the Prophet.
4
Understand the Praised Station and the banner
The Praised Station is the moment when the Prophet intercedes and the banner with three peaks is set up. Reflect on the symbolism of the three peaks.
The banner signifies the universality of his message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكالشَّفاعة وهي أنواع: الأوّل: شفاعته له في فضل القضاء لإراحة الخَلْق من طول الوقوف ومشقّته، وهي مختصة به صالة . قوله: (وهي مختصة به ) : أي : إجماعاً؛ وذلك لأنَّ النَّاس في ذلك الوقت يذهبون إلى الرُّسل من آدم إلى عيسى فرداً فرداً يسألونهم الشَّفاعة في الانصراف من ذلك الموقف، فكل يبدي حجة إلى أن يذهبوا إليه الله يسألونه الشَّفاعة فيقول: «أنا لها أنا لها، فيسجد تحت العرش، فيقول الله له : ارفع رأسك واشفع تشفّع » (۳) ، فيرفع رأسه ، وهذا هو المقام المحمود ؛ لأنَّه من حينها يكثر حمد النَّاس له، فينصب له لواء له ثلاث ذؤابات ؛ ذؤابة بالمشرق، وأخرى بالمغرب، وأخرى بالوسيط
And like intercession, and it has types: the first: his intercession for him in the matter of the judgment (faḍl al-qaḍā') to relieve the creation from the length of the standing and its hardship, and it is specific to him, peace be upon him. His statement: 'And it is specific to him' means: by consensus; and that is because the people at that time go to the messengers from Adam to Jesus, one by one, asking them for intercession to depart from that standing, and each one offers an excuse until they go to him, [i.e.,] to Allah [?], asking him for intercession, and he says: 'I am for it, I am for it.' Then he prostrates under the Throne, and Allah says to him: 'Raise your head and intercede, and you will be granted intercession.' Then he raises his head, and this is the Praised Station (al-maqam al-mahmud); because from that time the people's praise of him increases. Then a banner is set up for him with three peaks: a peak in the east, another in the west, and another in the middle.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage defines the first type of intercession (shafa'ah) of the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ) on Judgment Day. It is his intercession 'in the matter of the judgment' (fi faḍl al-qaḍā') to relieve the creation from the long standing and its hardship. This type is specific to him by consensus. The explanation: people go to various prophets from Adam to Jesus, each excusing themselves, until they come to Muhammad (ﷺ), who says 'I am for it' and prostrates under the Throne, and Allah tells him to raise his head and intercede, and he will be granted intercession. This is the Praised Station (al-maqam al-mahmud), because from that point people praise him much. Then a banner is set up for him with three peaks: one in the east, one in the west, and one in the middle.

المقام المحمود
لواء
ذؤابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession only forgives sins or is for a specific group.
Correction: This first intercession is universal: it relieves all of creation from the hardship of the standing, not just believers or sinners.

Checkpoint

?
The Prophet's intercession relieves all of creation from the agony of waiting. How does this knowledge affect your preparation for that day? Are you living as if you truly believe the standing is real and that you need his intercession?

The First Type of Intercession: The Great Intercession for Judgment
Al-Sawi defines the first type of intercession and describes its exclusive nature and accompanying honors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first type of intercession specific to the Prophet Muhammad and its significance as the Praiseworthy Station.

Core Idea
The great intercession is the Prophet's exclusive role to relieve creation from the hardship of judgment.

Al-Sawi begins by listing the types of intercession, focusing on the first: the Prophet's intercession to initiate judgment. This intercession is unique to him and is the basis of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqam al-mahmud) and the banner with three fringes. In this lesson, we explore how this intercession unfolds and why it is so important.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the narrative of the prophets seeking intercession come through.
Notice the phrase 'I am for it, I am for it' showing the Prophet's eagerness.
2
Identify the type and its exclusivity
The passage states this first type is 'specific to him' by consensus. Ask why this exclusivity matters in kalam.
3
Understand the narrative of the prophets
The passage traces how people go from Adam to Jesus, each declining. This shows the special status of Muhammad.
Compare with hadith of intercession (e.g., Sahih Bukhari).
4
Learn the Praiseworthy Station and the banner
The prostration under the Throne and the command to intercede lead to the Praiseworthy Station. The banner with three fringes symbolizes his universal honor.
The three fringes (east, west, middle) suggest covering all directions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكالشَّفاعة وهي أنواع: الأول: شفاعته له في فضل القضاء لإراحة الخَلْق من طول الوقوف ومشقّته، وهي مختصة به قوله: (وهي مختصة به) : أي : إجماعاً؛ وذلك لأنَّ النَّاس في ذلك الوقت يذهبون إلى الرُّسل من آدم إلى عيسى فرداً فرداً يسألونهم الشَّفاعة في الانصراف من ذلك الموقف، فكل يبدي حجة إلى أن يذهبوا إليه الله يسألونه الشَّفاعة فيقول: «أنا لها أنا لها، فيسجد تحت العرش، فيقول الله له : ارفع رأسك واشفع تشفّع » (۳) ، فيرفع رأسه ، وهذا هو المقام المحمود ؛ لأنَّه من حينها يكثر حمد النَّاس له، فينصب له لواء له ثلاث ذؤابات ؛ ذؤابة بالمشرق، وأخرى بالمغرب، وأخرى بالوسيط
And like intercession, and it has types: the first: his intercession for the excellence of judgment to give rest to creation from the length of standing and its hardship, and it is specific to him. His statement: (And it is specific to him) i.e., by consensus; because the people at that time go to the messengers from Adam to Jesus one by one asking them for intercession to depart from that standing-place, and each one offers an excuse until they go to Allah asking him for intercession, and he says: 'I am for it, I am for it,' then he prostrates under the Throne, and Allah says to him: 'Raise your head and intercede, and you will be interceded' (3), so he raises his head. And this is the praiseworthy station because from that time the people's praise of him increases. And a banner is set up for him with three fringes: a fringe on the east, another on the west, and another in the middle.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage defines the first type of intercession (shafa'ah) of the Prophet Muhammad (s) and describes its unique features. It begins by stating that intercession has types, and the first is his intercession for the advantage of the judgment (qada') to relieve creation from the long standing and hardship of the Day of Resurrection. Then it explains that this type is specific to him by consensus. The reason is that when people seek intercession from earlier prophets, each declines until they come to the Prophet Muhammad, who accepts. He prostrates under the Throne, and Allah commands him to raise his head and intercede. This is the praiseworthy station (al-maqam al-mahmud) because from then on people praise him abundantly. As a sign of honor, a banner is set up for him with three fringes extending east, west, and the middle.

الشفاعة
المقام المحمود
الذؤابات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All intercessions are equally shared among prophets.
Correction: This passage clarifies that the great intercession for judgment is exclusive to Prophet Muhammad.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Five Special Types of Intercession
Al-Sawi lists five more types of intercession and explains the scholarly consensus and differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various types of intercession beyond the first, including which are specific to the Prophet and which are shared.

Core Idea
Intercession is multidimensional: from entering Paradise to lightening Hell's punishment.

Al-Sawi continues his discussion of intercession by enumerating five more types, each with different rulings on whether the Prophet has exclusive privilege. This passage clarifies disputed points and shows the breadth of prophetic intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the list of five intercession types.
Notice the structure: each type is introduced with a number (second through sixth).
2
Identify the five types
List the five types: entering Paradise without account, preventing entry into Hell, exiting Hell, increasing ranks, and lightening punishment for the eternally damned.
The first type (general intercession) was covered earlier.
3
Examine the scholarly disputes
For type three (preventing Hell entry), note that 'Iyad says it is not specific, while al-Nawawi hesitated. For type five (increasing ranks), al-Nawawi allowed specificity. Understand the reliance on textual evidence.
The commentary says the relied-upon view for type three is non-specificity.
4
Focus on shared intercession
Type four (exiting Hell) is shared by prophets, angels, and righteous believers. Reflect on the inclusivity.
Even a master can intercede for a person who said the shahada with no good deeds.
5
Reflect on the Abu Talib example
The sixth type (lightening punishment) is exemplified by Abu Talib. Consider the implications for those destined to remain in Hell.
The hadith 'I am the first intercessor' supports this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشفاعة وأنواعها (وهي الثاني : شفاعته في إدخال قوم الجنَّة بغير حساب، قال النووي: مختصة به) (۱) . الثَّالث: الشَّفاعة فيمن استحقَّ دخول النَّار أن لا يدخلها، قال عياض: (وليست مختصة به)(۲)، وتردَّد النّوويُّ؛ أي: لأنَّه لم يرد تصريح بذلك . الرّابع : الشَّفاعة في إخراج قوم من النَّار، ويشاركه فيها الأنبياء والملائكة وصالحو المؤمنين . الخامس : الشّفاعة في زيادة الدرجات، وجوز النووي اختصاصها به عليه الصلاة السلام (۳). السادس : الشَّفاعة في تخفيف العذاب عمَّن استحق الخلود في النَّار، كما في حقّ أبي طالب ففي الصحيح: «أنا أوّل شافع وأوّل والأنبياء ومن دونهم تحت ذلك اللواء (٤). قوله : (قال عياض وليست مختصة به) : أي : وهو المعتمد. قوله : (وصالحو المؤمنين) : أي : والأطفال، بل والمولى يشفع أيضاً فيمن قال : لا إله إلَّا الله ، ولم يعمل خيراً قط .
Intercession and its types: And the second: his intercession for entering some people into Paradise without account. Al-Nawawi said it is specific to him. The third: intercession for one who deserves to enter Hellfire that he should not enter it. 'Iyad said it is not specific to him, and al-Nawawi hesitated; because no explicit text came to that effect. The fourth: intercession for taking people out of Hellfire, and prophets, angels, and righteous believers share with him in it. The fifth: intercession for increasing ranks, and al-Nawawi allowed its specificity to him (peace and blessings be upon him). The sixth: intercession for lightening the punishment for one who deserves eternal abiding in Hellfire, as in the case of Abu Talib, for in the Sahih: 'I am the first intercessor and the first... and the prophets and those below them are under that banner.' His statement: ( 'Iyad said it is not specific to him ) means that is the relied-upon view. His statement: ( and righteous believers ) means including children, and even a master intercedes for one who said 'There is no god but Allah' and never did any good deed.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage enumerates five more types of intercession (shafa'ah) after the first. For each, it states the ruling on whether it is specific to the Prophet. The second type (entering Paradise without account) is specific by Nawawi's view. The third (preventing Hellfire entry) is disputed: 'Iyad says not specific, Nawawi hesitated. The fourth (exiting Hellfire) is shared with prophets, angels, and righteous believers. The fifth (increasing ranks) is possibly specific. The sixth (lightening punishment for the eternally damned) is exemplified by Abu Talib. The passage then provides a gloss confirming that the relied-upon view for the third type is that it is not specific, and explains that 'righteous believers' in the fourth type includes children and even a master can intercede for someone who said the shahada with no good deeds.

شفاعة
حساب
خلود
أبو طالب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is only for exiting Hell.
Correction: Intercession includes many forms: entering Paradise without account, preventing Hell entry, increasing ranks, and even lightening punishment for those who remain in Hell.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the fourth type of intercession (exiting Hellfire) is shared by whom?
A) Only the Prophet
B) Prophets and angels only
C) Prophets, angels, and righteous believers
D) Only righteous believers

Key Takeaway
Intercession comprises multiple forms, from entering Paradise without account to lightening punishment for the eternally damned, and only some are exclusive to the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's intercession lightened Abu Talib's punishment even though he died upon disbelief. Think of someone in your life who does not share your faith—what does this teach you about your duty of da'wah and compassion towards them? How can you act on this today?
?
The passage shows that even a person who said 'La ilaha illa Allah' but did no good deeds can receive intercession. Does this make you complacent in your own deeds, or does it increase your hope and urgency to act? Spend a few moments reflecting on one good deed you have been neglecting, and commit to doing it tomorrow.
?
Some intercessions are exclusive to the Prophet, and some are shared. Which of these types do you personally need most right now? How does that shape your reliance on the Prophet versus your own deeds?

The Five Types of Intercession (Types 2–6)
Lists types 2–6 of prophetic intercession with rulings on exclusivity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the five types of prophetic intercession (types 2–6) and whether each is exclusive to the Prophet or shared.

Core Idea
Intercession is a spectrum: some types are unique to the Prophet, others are shared.

The concept of intercession (shafa'ah) is often misunderstood as being a single event. In fact, scholars distinguish multiple types with different rulings. This lesson presents five specific types of the Prophet's intercession, from the second to the sixth, highlighting which are exclusive to him and which are shared with other prophets, angels, and believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get a clear overview of the five types.
2
Identify each type and its ruling
For each of the five types (second through sixth), note the description and the ruling on exclusivity mentioned by scholars like al-Nawawi and Qadi 'Iyad.
Pay special attention to the differences of opinion.
3
Reflect on the case of Abu Talib
The sixth type is illustrated by the Prophet's intercession for his uncle Abu Talib. Consider what this teaches about the scope of intercession.
The hadith shows that even a person destined for eternal punishment can have their torment lightened.
4
Understand shared intercession
Notice that some types are not exclusive to the Prophet; prophets, angels, and even righteous believers can intercede. This shows the widespread mercy of Allah.

الشفاعة وأنواعها
(وهي
الثاني : شفاعته في إدخال قوم الجنَّة بغير حساب، قال النووي: مختصة به.
الثَّالث: الشَّفاعة فيمن استحقَّ دخول النَّار أن لا يدخلها، قال عياض: (وليست مختصة به)، وتردَّد النّوويُّ؛ أي: لأنَّه لم يرد تصريح بذلك .
الرّابع : الشَّفاعة في إخراج قوم من النَّار، ويشاركه فيها الأنبياء والملائكة وصالحو المؤمنين .
الخامس : الشّفاعة في زيادة الدرجات، وجوز النووي اختصاصها به عليه الصلاة السلام.
السادس : الشَّفاعة في تخفيف العذاب عمَّن استحق الخلود في النَّار، كما في حقّ أبي طالب ففي الصحيح: «أنا أوّل شافع وأوّل مشفّع، وإنَّه ذُكِر عنده عمه أبو طالب فقال: «لعله تنفعه شفاعتي فَيُجْعَل في ضَحْضَاح من النار».

Intercession and its types. (And it) The second: his intercession in admitting some people to Paradise without reckoning. Al-Nawawi said: exclusive to him. The third: intercession for one who deserves to enter the Fire not to enter it. 'Iyad said: (not exclusive to him), and al-Nawawi hesitated; meaning because no explicit text came regarding that. The fourth: intercession in bringing out some people from the Fire, and the prophets, angels, and righteous believers share with him in it. The fifth: intercession in increasing ranks, and al-Nawawi allowed its exclusivity to him, peace be upon him. The sixth: intercession in lightening the punishment for one who deserves eternal stay in the Fire, as in the case of Abu Talib, for in the Sahih: 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted, and his uncle Abu Talib was mentioned before him, and he said: Perhaps my intercession will benefit him so that he is placed in a shallow patch of Fire.' And the prophets and those below them are under that banner. His saying: ('Iyad said: and it is not exclusive to him) meaning: and it is the relied-upon view. His saying: (and righteous believers) meaning: and children; indeed, even a master intercedes for one who said 'There is no god but Allah' and did not do any good deed at all. His saying: ('so he is placed in a shallow patch of Fire') meaning: because it has come that he is the least of the people of the Fire in punishment, for in the hadith: 'The least of the people of the Fire in punishment is a man who wears two sandals of Fire, from which his brain boils.'
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage enumerates the types of intercession (al-shafa'ah) of the Prophet Muhammad, specifically from the second to the sixth type. The first type is not mentioned here, likely having been covered earlier. The second type is his intercession to admit a group into Paradise without accountability; al-Nawawi states this is exclusive to him. The third is intercession for those who deserve to enter the Fire that they not enter it; Qadi 'Iyad said it is not exclusive, and al-Nawawi hesitated due to lack of explicit text. The fourth is intercession to remove people from the Fire, and he is joined by prophets, angels, and righteous believers. The fifth is intercession to increase ranks, with al-Nawawi allowing its exclusivity. The sixth is intercession to lighten punishment for those deserving eternity in the Fire, like Abu Talib, with a hadith that the Prophet will intercede so that Abu Talib is placed in a shallow fire (dahdah). The commentator then clarifies that the view of Qadi 'Iyad is the relied-upon one, and that 'righteous believers' includes children, and even a master may intercede for one who said 'La ilaha illa Allah' without any good deeds. Finally, the commentator explains the hadith about the least punished person in Hell having two soles of fire, making his brain boil, connecting it to Abu Talib's punishment.

Misconception: All types of intercession are exclusive to the Prophet.
Correction: Some types, like intercession to remove people from the Fire, are shared with other prophets, angels, and righteous believers.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet’s intercession encompasses multiple distinct acts, some unique to him and some in which others participate, reflecting the depth of divine mercy.

The First Major Sign: Al-Dajjal and His Name
Defines the five major signs and introduces the first, al-Dajjal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first major sign of the Hour—the emergence of al-Dajjal—and the linguistic and theological reasons for his name as presented in the text.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is the first major sign; his name reveals his role and deformity.

The signs of the Last Day are many, but scholars agree on five major signs that precede the Hour. The first and most discussed is the emergence of al-Masih al-Dajjal. In this lesson, we explore the agreed-upon signs and then focus on the Dajjal's name, spelling, and the reasons he is called 'Masih'—a name that points to his unique characteristics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Notice how the author introduces the five signs and then focuses on the first one.
The Arabic includes a parenthetical comment about the spelling.
2
Understand the five agreed-upon signs
The passage states that there are five agreed-upon major signs of the Hour. Only the first is mentioned here. Understand that these are the major signs (al-kubrā).
The other four signs are not listed in this passage.
3
Examine the reasons for the name 'Masih'
The author gives three explanations for why al-Dajjal is called 'Masih': (1) because he will traverse the earth quickly, (2) because he is flat-footed (mamsūḥ al-qadam), and (3) a reference to a hadith about the left eye. Identify each reason.
The phrase 'as the left eye' is likely a textual error; the intended meaning may be 'as will come in the hadith about the left eye'.
4
Note the spelling clarification
The passage clarifies that the correct spelling is with the unpointed ḥā' (ḥā' muhmalah), not with khā'. The alternative with khā' is mentioned but rejected.
This shows the care scholars take in preserving correct terminology.

أولها : خروج المسيح الدَّجَّال - بالحاء المهملة - على الصحيح، سمّي مسيحاً لِمَسْحه الأرض في أَمَد يسير ؛ أي: مدة أربعين يوماً كما العين اليسرى، وقيل: لأنه ممسوح سيأتي في الحديث، وقيل: لأنه ممسوح القدم ؛ أي: لأنه لا أخمص له .

Signs of the Day of Resurrection. And from the conditions of the Hour: the five agreed-upon; i.e., its signs; i.e., the signs indicating its proximity: The first of them: the emergence of al-Masih al-Dajjal – with the unpointed ha (ḥā') – according to the correct view. Commentary
This passage discusses the signs of the Day of Resurrection, specifically the five agreed-upon signs (al-'alamāt al-muttafaq 'alayhā) that indicate the proximity of the Hour. It states that these are the major signs (al-kubrā). The first of these signs is the emergence of al-Masih al-Dajjal. The correct spelling is with the unpointed ḥā' (ḥā' muhmalah), though some pronounce it with khā' mu'jama because he is deformed (mamsūkh) in form. Several explanations are given for why he is called 'Masih': he will traverse the earth quickly in a short time—forty days—as will come in the hadith; another reason is that he is flat-footed (mamsūḥ al-qadam), meaning he has no arch. The passage includes a comment that these signs are the major ones.

Correction: The correct spelling is with the unpointed ḥā' (ح) as in 'ḥā', according to the passage. The alternative with khā' is mentioned but not accepted as correct.

The First Major Sign: The Emergence of Al-Dajjal
Al-Sawi defines the five signs and explains the first sign: al-Dajjal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Dajjal is called 'Masih' and 'Dajjal', and how his title distinguishes him from Prophet Jesus.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is called Masih because he traverses the earth swiftly, but he is the anti-Christ.

This passage by Al-Sawi opens the discussion of the major signs of the Hour. After briefly listing the five agreed-upon signs, he dives into the first sign: the emergence of al-Dajjal. He clarifies the correct pronunciation of 'Dajjal' and explains the meanings behind his two titles: 'Masih' and 'Dajjal', carefully distinguishing him from Prophet Jesus. Understanding these names is key to recognizing this fitna.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get the flow. Notice the structure: it first mentions the five signs, then focuses on the first sign with its linguistic explanations.
The passage uses a lot of 'qīla' (it is said) for variant opinions.
2
Identify the two titles
Find where the passage explains why he is called 'Masih' and why 'Dajjal'. Note the two different reasons for 'Masih' and the one reason for 'Dajjal'.
The reasons for 'Masih' include traversing the earth and being flat-footed.
3
Compare with Prophet Jesus
The passage also explains why Prophet Jesus is called 'Masih'. Compare the reasons: one shared reason (traversing the earth) but different emphases.
Jesus is called Masih because of his healing by wiping or because he is blessed.
4
Reflect on the significance
Think about why such detail is given to names. In Islamic theology, names often reflect attributes. Knowing the Dajjal's names helps in recognizing him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامات يوم القيامة وكشرائط الساعة الخَمْسة المتَّفَق عليها أي علاماتها أي العلامات الدالة على قربها : أولها : خروج المسيح الدَّجَّال - بالحاء المهملة - على الصحيح وقيل بالخاء المعجمة لأنـَّه ممسوخ الصورة. سمي مسيحاً لِمَسْحه الأرض في أَمَد يسير أي مدة أربعين يوما كما سيأتي في الحديث وقيل لأنه ممسوح القدم أي لأنه لا أخمص له . ووُصِف بالدَّجَّال أي الكذاب للفرق بينه وبين المسيح عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام. وسُمِّي عيسى مسيحاً لِمَسحه الأرض أي سياحته فيها وقيل لأنَّه ما مسح على ذي عاهة إلا بَرِئ بإذن الله تعالى وقيل لأنَّه ممسوح بالبركة.
Signs of the Day of Resurrection: And among the conditions of the Hour are the five agreed-upon signs, i.e., its signs, i.e., the signs indicating its nearness: The first of them: the emergence of al-Masīḥ al-Dajjāl – with the unpointed ḥā’ – according to the correct view, and it is said with the pointed khā’ because he is distorted in form. He is called Masīḥ because of his traversing the earth in a short period, i.e., a duration of forty days as will come in the hadith, and it is said because he is flat-footed, i.e., he has no arch. And he is described as al-Dajjāl, i.e., the great liar, to distinguish him from the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace be upon him. And Jesus is called Masīḥ because of his traversing the earth, i.e., his travelling in it, and it is said because he used to wipe over any affliction and it would heal by God’s permission, and it is said because he is blessed.

Commentary
This passage enumerates the five major signs of the Hour and then defines the first sign: the emergence of al-Masīḥ al-Dajjāl. It begins by stating that the signs are the conditions of the Hour that indicate its nearness. The first sign is the appearance of the Dajjāl. The author clarifies the pronunciation of 'Dajjāl': the correct view is with an unpointed ḥā’ (i.e., with the letter ح), but some say it is written with a pointed khā’ (خ) because the Dajjāl is distorted in form (mamsūkh al-ṣūrah). Then he explains why the Dajjāl is called 'Masīḥ': because he traverses the earth quickly in forty days, and also because he is flat-footed (mamsūḥ al-qadam), lacking an arch. The Dajjāl is described as 'al-Dajjāl' (the great liar) to differentiate him from Jesus, who is also called Masīḥ. Jesus is called Masīḥ because he traversed the earth in his travels, or because he used to wipe (yamsaḥ) over the sick and heal them, or because he is blessed. The passage thus clarifies the shared title and the distinct meanings.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the title 'Masīḥ' (Messiah) applies exclusively to Prophet Jesus and that the Dajjāl is never called Masīḥ.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the Dajjāl is also called Masīḥ, but for different reasons: he is called Masīḥ because he traverses the earth quickly (or because he is flat-footed). The Dajjāl is further described as 'al-Dajjāl' (the great liar) to distinguish him from Jesus.

Key Takeaway

The Second Sign: Descent of Jesus and Killing the Dajjal
Al-Sawi describes the second sign: Jesus's descent and his destruction of the Dajjal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second major sign of the Hour: the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) and his role in killing the Dajjal, as described in authentic hadiths from al-Sahih and Musnad Ahmad.

Core Idea
Jesus will descend to defeat the Dajjal and restore pure Islam.

This lesson presents the second sign of the Hour: the descent of Jesus son of Mary. Through two hadiths, we learn that Jesus will return as a just judge, break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya. The Dajjal's appearance and deception are also described, along with explanatory notes. Let's examine the textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once, then the English translation to get an overview of the content.
Notice the two hadiths embedded in the passage.
2
Identify the two hadiths
The passage quotes two hadiths: one from al-Sahih about Jesus's actions, and one from Musnad Ahmad about the Dajjal. Identify their key points.
3
Explore the commentary
Al-Sawi explains key terms: 'khifqa' (scarcity), 'idbār' (turning away), and clarifies which days of the Dajjal are longer.
The commentary helps understand the hadiths better.
4
Reflect on the jizya issue
Understand the common misunderstanding about jizya: Jesus will not accept it but only offer Islam or the sword.
This corrects a potential misconception.

The second of them: the descent of the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace and blessings be upon him, from heaven and his killing of the Dajjāl. For in al-Ṣaḥīḥ: 'The son of Mary will certainly descend as a just judge; he will break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya...' the hadith. And in Musnad Aḥmad from the hadith of Jābir: 'The Dajjāl will appear in a period of decline in religion and withdrawal of knowledge, and he will have forty nights to traverse the earth, a day like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, then the rest of his days like your days. He will have a donkey he rides, the width between its ears being forty cubits. He will say to the people: I am your Lord, but he is one-eyed, and your Lord is not one-eyed.' His statement: 'and he will place the jizya' – meaning he will not accept it, rather either Islam or the sword. His statement: 'in a decline (khifqa)' – meaning scarcity. His statement: 'and withdrawal (idbār)' – meaning turning away. His statement: 'a day like a year' – meaning the first day. His statement: 'and a day like a month' – meaning the second. His statement: 'and a day like a week' – meaning the third.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents the second major sign of the Hour: the descent of Jesus (ʿĪsā ibn Maryam) from heaven and his killing of the Dajjāl. It supports this with two hadiths. The first hadith (from al-Ṣaḥīḥ, likely Bukhari and Muslim) states that Jesus will descend as a just judge (ḥakaman ʿadlan), break the cross, kill the pig, and abolish the jizya (the poll tax). This indicates that he will establish pure Islam, removing corruptions and not accepting tribute from non-Muslims – rather they must either accept Islam or face the sword. The second hadith (from Musnad Aḥmad via Jābir) describes the Dajjāl's appearance during a time of religious decline and ignorance. He will have forty days to travel the earth, with the first day lasting a year, the second a month, the third a week, and the rest normal. He will ride a donkey with huge ears and claim to be God, but he is one-eyed, whereas God is not one-eyed. The commentary then explains key phrases: 'khifqa' means scarcity (of faith), 'idbār' means turning away (from knowledge), and the variations in day lengths refer to the first, second, and third days respectively. The overall message is that Jesus's return will defeat the Dajjāl and restore true religion.

Correction: The commentary clarifies that Jesus will not accept jizya; rather he will offer only Islam or the sword, meaning he will compel conversion or fight.

Why Dajjal is Called Liar and Isa is Called Masih
Defines why Dajjal is called liar and Isa is called Masih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and theological reasons why Dajjal is called 'Dajjal' and why Jesus is called 'Masih' according to Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
Names in Islamic eschatology carry deep meanings that reveal the roles of key figures.

This brief passage from a classical commentary explains the etymologies behind two central eschatological titles. By understanding why the Antichrist is called 'Dajjal' (the liar) and why Jesus is called 'Masih' (the Messiah), we gain insight into their respective missions and significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to get the author's meaning.
Notice the concise style of the commentary.
2
Identify Dajjal's meaning
The text says 'dajjal' means 'kadhdhab' (liar). Understand that this is to distinguish him from the truthful Messiah.
This sets up a contrast between falsehood and truth.
3
List the three reasons for Masih
The passage gives three possible etymologies for 'Masih': (1) because of his travels, (2) because he healed by wiping, (3) because he was wiped with blessing.
Each reason highlights a different aspect of Jesus's role.
4
Reflect on the contrast
Compare the single negative epithet for Dajjal (liar) with the multiple positive attributes of Jesus. This underscores the theological distinction.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and try the activity to reinforce the lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووُصِف بالدَّجَّال؛ أي: الكذاب؛ للفرق بينه وبين المسيح عيسى بن مريم عليه الصلاة والسلام. وسُمِّي عيسى مسيحاً لِمَسحه الأرض؛ أي: سياحته فيها، وقيل: لأنَّه ما مسح على ذي عاهة إلا بَرِئ بإذن الله تعالى، وقيل: لأنَّه ممسوح بالبركة.
And he was described as al-Dajjal, i.e., the liar, to distinguish between him and the Messiah, Jesus son of Mary, peace be upon him. And Jesus was named Messiah because of his traversing the earth, i.e., his traveling in it, and it is said because he did not wipe (مسح) over any afflicted person except that he was cured by the permission of Allah, and it is said because he was wiped with blessing.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage defines two key eschatological figures: al-Dajjal (the Antichrist) and al-Masih (the Messiah, Jesus). It explains why al-Dajjal is called 'dajjal' — meaning 'kadhdhab' (liar) — to distinguish him from the truthful Messiah. Then it gives three explanations for why Jesus is called 'Masih': first, because of his extensive travels (masaha al-ard); second, because he used to wipe (yamsahu) over ailments and heal them by Allah's permission; third, because he is 'mamsuh' (wiped) with blessing. Each etymology reinforces the unique station of Jesus.

Key Terms

المسيح
الكذاب
مسح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The one-eyed
B) The liar
C) The traveller
D) The blessed

Key Takeaway
The names 'Dajjal' and 'Masih' are not arbitrary; they reveal the essential natures of the figures they describe — falsehood versus truth and blessing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The name 'Dajjal' means 'the liar'. In your own life, where are you most vulnerable to self-deception — the lies you tell yourself about your faith, your intentions, or your priorities? Will you commit to identifying one such lie today and replacing it with the truth from this lesson?
?
Jesus was called 'Masih' partly because he would wipe over the afflicted and they would be healed. You have been given the opportunity to be a source of healing to those around you — through your words, your presence, or your prayers. Who in your life is suffering, and what specific act of 'wiping' — of kindness, forgiveness, or intercession — can you offer them this week?
?
The passage distinguishes between the liar (Dajjal) and the truthful one (Masih). In your daily interactions, do your words and actions align more with deception or with truth? What would it cost you to be completely truthful in a situation where a small lie would be easier? Are you willing to pay that price?

The Descent of Jesus and the Dajjal's Appearance
Presents the second major sign with two hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second major sign of the Hour: the descent of Jesus and his killing of the Dajjal, and the hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
Jesus will descend as a just judge, break the cross, and offer only Islam or the sword.

This lesson presents the second major sign: the descent of Jesus and his confrontation with the Dajjal. The author provides two authentic hadiths that detail these events, including the extraordinary signs of the Dajjal's advent. Understanding these signs is crucial for eschatological belief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the hadith excerpts. Then review the literal translation.
2
Examine the first hadith from Sahih
Identify the actions Jesus will perform: breaking the cross, killing the pig, and imposing jizyah. Note the commentary on jizyah.
The commentary clarifies that 'imposing jizyah' means he will not accept it, only Islam or the sword.
3
Examine the second hadith from Musnad Ahmad
Read the description of the Dajjal's emergence, his unusual journey, and his claim to divinity. Notice the commentary on the terms 'khifqa' and 'idbar'.
The Dajjal is one-eyed, while Allah is not one-eyed.

ثانيها : نزول المسيح عيسى بن مريم عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام من السَّماء وقَتْلُه للدَّجَّال، ففي الصَّحيح : «لينزِلَنَّ ابنُ مريم حَكَماً عدلاً فلَيَكْسِرَنَّ الصَّليب، ولَيَقْتُلَنَّ الخنزير ، ولَيَضَعَنَّ الجزية ... الحديث، وفي مسند أحمد» من حديث جابر: «يخرج الدَّجَّالُ في خفقة من الدين وإدبار من العلم وله أربعون ليلة يسيحها في الأرض، اليوم منها كالسَّنة، واليوم منها كالشَّهر ، واليوم منها كالجُمعة، ثمَّ سائر أيامه كأيامكم هذه وله حمار يركبه عَرْضُ جانب أذنيه أربعون ذراعاً، فيقول للنّاس : أنا ربّكم، وهو أعور، وإن ربكم ليس بأعور، قوله : ( وليضعن الجزية أي لا يقبلها بل إمَّا الإسلام أو السيف خفقة قوله : (في من الدِّين: أي: قلَّة. قوله : (وإدبار) : أي : إعراض. قوله : (اليوم) منها كالسَّنة) : أي : وهو أول يوم منها . وقوله : ( واليوم منها كالشَّهر) : أي : الثَّاني . وقوله: (واليوم منها كالجمعة) : أي : الثالث.
The second: The descent of the Messiah Jesus son of Mary, peace and blessings be upon him, from heaven and his killing of the Dajjal. In Sahih: 'Ibn Maryam will certainly descend as a just judge, and he will break the cross, and kill the pig, and impose the jizyah...' and in Musnad Ahmad from the hadith of Jabir: 'The Dajjal will come out during a decline in religion and a turning away from knowledge, and he will have forty nights wandering the earth, a day of which is like a year, a day like a month, a day like a week, then the rest of his days are like your days. He has a donkey that he rides, the width between its ears is forty cubits. He will say to the people: I am your Lord, and he is one-eyed, and your Lord is not one-eyed.' His saying: 'and he will impose the jizyah' means he will not accept it, but rather either Islam or the sword. 'During a decline' meaning scarcity. 'Turning away' meaning aversion. 'A day like a year' meaning it is the first day of them. 'A day like a month' meaning the second. 'A day like a week' meaning the third.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage defines the second major sign of the Hour: the descent of Jesus and his killing of the Dajjal. It provides two hadiths as evidence. The Sahih hadith shows Jesus will descend as a just judge, breaking the cross (symbol of Christianity), killing pigs (forbidden food), and imposing jizyah, but the commentary explains this means he will not accept jizyah — he offers only Islam or the sword. The Musnad hadith from Jabir describes the Dajjal's emergence during a 'khifqa' (scarcity) in religion and 'idbar' (turning away) from knowledge. He will have forty nights of unusual lengths: the first day like a year, the second like a month, the third like a week, then the rest like normal days. He will ride a huge donkey, and he will claim divinity while being one-eyed—contrary to Allah who is not one-eyed. The commentary clarifies each term: 'khifqa' means scarcity, 'idbar' means aversion, and the three stages of the first three days are explained.

Correction: The commentary clarifies that 'impose jizyah' means he will not accept it, but rather offer only Islam or the sword. Jizyah is not an option during his rule.

The Mark of the Dajjal
Describes the writing 'Kafir' on the Dajjal's forehead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Dajjal bears a clear, readable mark of disbelief ('Kafir') between his eyes, which every believer can recognize regardless of literacy.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's forehead openly declares his disbelief.

Among the many deceptive signs of the Dajjal, the most straightforward is the word 'Kafir' written between his eyes. This passage establishes that the mark is readable by all believers—literate or not—as a divine sign to protect the faithful.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic text
Read the short Arabic phrase: 'مكتوب بين عينيه : كافر، يقرؤه كلُّ مؤمن كاتب وغير كاتب'.
Notice the emphasis on 'كل مؤمن' (every believer).
2
Reflect on the significance
Why would this mark be readable by all? It shows that recognition of falsehood does not require worldly learning; faith itself grants insight.
This contrasts with the Dajjal's other deceptive miracles.
3
Connect to modern understanding
Consider how this sign serves as an absolute criterion: no matter how convincing the Dajjal appears, his true nature is openly displayed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكتوب بين عينيه : كافر، يقرؤه كلُّ مؤمن كاتب وغير كاتب، يرد كلَّ ماء ومَنْهَل إلا المدينة ومكَّةَ حرَّمهما الله عليه، وأقامت الملائكة بأبوابهما، ومعه جبال من خُبز، والنَّاسُ في جَهد إِلَّا مَنْ تَبِعه، ومعه تهران أنا أعلم بهما منه، نهر يقول : الجنَّة، ونهر يقول : النَّار، فمَنْ أُدخل الذي يسميه الجنَّةَ فهوَ في النَّار، ومن أُدخل الذي يسميه النَّار فهوَ في الجنَّة، قال : وتبعث معه شياطين تلكم، ومعه فتنة عظيمة، يأمر السّماءَ تُمطر فيما يرى النّاس، ويَقتُل نفساً ثم يُحييها فيما يرى النَّاس، فيقول للنَّاس : أيُّها النَّاس ؛ فهل يفعل مثل هذا إلا الرَّبُّ؟ فيفِرُّ النَّاسُ إلى جبل الدُّخان بالشَّام، فيأتيهم فيحاصرهم، فيشتد حصارهم ويُجهدهم جهداً شديداً ، ثم ينزل عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام قوله: (ومعه نهران . . . إلخ) : هو معنى قوله في بعض الروايات: (ومعه جنَّة ونار) (۱). قوله : شياطين) (تلكم هو اسم موضع . حين قوله : ( ويقتل نفساً ثمَّ يحييها ) : أي : وهو الخضر ، ورد أنَّه يحييه يقول له : أولم تؤمن بي؟ فيقول له : والله ؛ ما ازددت فيك إلَّا بصيرة، ثمَّ بعد إحيائه تمسك يده فلا يقتل أحداً (٢). قوله : ( فيفرُّ النَّاس) : أي : مع المهدي. (1) أخرجه مسلم (١٠٤/۲۹۳٤) عن حذيفة لله (۲) أخرجه مسلم (۱۱۳/۲۹۳۸) عن أبي سعيد الخدري الله الله
Written between his eyes: 'Kafir'. Every believer, literate or illiterate, reads it. He (Dajjal) seeks every source of water except Medina and Mecca, for Allah has forbidden them to him, and angels stand at their gates. With him are mountains of bread, and the people are in hardship except those who follow him. He has two rivers, I know them more than him: a river saying 'Paradise' and a river saying 'Hell'. Whoever enters what he calls Paradise will be in Hell, and whoever enters what he calls Hell will be in Paradise. He said: and with him are sent devils of Talakum, and with him is a great trial. He commands the sky to rain, in what the people see. He kills a soul then revives it, in what the people see. He says to the people: O people, does anyone do such things except the Lord? So the people flee to the mountain of smoke in Syria. He comes to them and besieges them, the siege tightens and he severely stresses them. Then Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, descends. His saying: 'And with him are two rivers...' is the meaning of his saying in some narrations: 'With him is a garden and a fire.' His saying: 'devils' Talakum is a place name. His saying: 'And he kills a soul then revives it' means it is al-Khidr. It is narrated that he revives him and says: Did you not believe in me? He says: By Allah, I have only increased in certainty about you. Then after his revival, he takes hold of his hand and does not kill anyone. His saying: 'So the people flee' means with the Mahdi. (1) Muslim (2934/104) from Hudhayfah. (2) Muslim (2938/113) from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage details the deceptions and trials of the Dajjal as derived from authentic hadith. It describes the writing 'Kafir' on his forehead, readable by all believers regardless of literacy—a clear sign for believers to recognize him. He cannot enter Mecca or Medina, as angels guard them. He brings mountains of bread to attract followers, while others suffer. He has two rivers that he mislabels as Paradise and Hell to mislead people. The commentary clarifies that these are actually a garden and a fire, a test. The Dajjal also performs apparent miracles: commanding rain and reviving a dead person. The commentary identifies the revived person as al-Khidr, who, when revived, affirms his faith in Islam and then grabs the Dajjal's hand so he cannot kill anyone else. This shows the Dajjal's power is illusion. The people flee to the mountain of smoke (Jabal al-Dukhan) in Syria, where the Dajjal besieges them. Finally, Jesus descends to save them. The commentary adds that the flight is with the Mahdi.

مكتوب بين عينيه كافر

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The hadith explicitly says both literate and illiterate believers read it, showing it is a matter of faith-based recognition.

Dajjal's Limitations and False Paradise
Describes Dajjal's inability to enter Mecca/Medina and his deceptive rivers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Dajjal cannot enter Mecca or Medina due to angelic protection, and that his so-called 'paradise' and 'hell' are deceptive trials.

Core Idea
The Dajjal is powerless before sacred cities and his paradise is actually hell.

The hadith details two crucial defenses against the Dajjal: the sanctity of Mecca and Medina, and the reality behind his two rivers. This lesson explains how Allah protects His sanctuaries and how the Dajjal's deception is inverted.

Guided Path
1
Locate the two rivers
Read the passage describing the two rivers—one claiming to be Paradise, one Hell.
Note that the Dajjal's claims are false: what he calls Paradise leads to Hell, and vice versa.
2
Understand the protection of Mecca and Medina
The text says angels guard the gates of these cities, preventing Dajjal's entry.
This shows the special status of these cities.
3
Reflect on the deception
Why would the Dajjal offer mountains of bread? He uses worldly allurements to attract followers.

مكتوب بين عينيه : كافر، يقرؤه كلُّ مؤمن كاتب وغير كاتب، يرد كلَّ ماء ومَنْهَل إلا المدينة ومكَّةَ حرَّمهما الله عليه، وأقامت الملائكة بأبوابهما، ومعه جبال من خُبز، والنَّاسُ في جَهد إِلَّا مَنْ تَبِعه، ومعه تهران أنا أعلم بهما منه، نهر يقول : الجنَّة، ونهر يقول : النَّار، فمَنْ أُدخل الذي يسميه الجنَّةَ فهوَ في النَّار، ومن أُدخل الذي يسميه النَّار فهوَ في الجنَّة، قال : وتبعث معه شياطين تلكم، ومعه فتنة عظيمة، يأمر السّماءَ تُمطر فيما يرى النّاس، ويَقتُل نفساً ثم يُحييها فيما يرى النَّاس، فيقول للنَّاس : أيُّها النَّاس ؛ فهل يفعل مثل هذا إلا الرَّبُّ؟ فيفِرُّ النَّاسُ إلى جبل الدُّخان بالشَّام، فيأتيهم فيحاصرهم، فيشتد حصارهم ويُجهدهم جهداً شديداً ، ثم ينزل عيسى عليه الصلاة والسلام قوله: (ومعه نهران . . . إلخ) : هو معنى قوله في بعض الروايات: (ومعه جنَّة ونار) (۱). قوله : شياطين) (تلكم هو اسم موضع . حين قوله : ( ويقتل نفساً ثمَّ يحييها ) : أي : وهو الخضر ، ورد أنَّه يحييه يقول له : أولم تؤمن بي؟ فيقول له : والله ؛ ما ازددت فيك إلَّا بصيرة، ثمَّ بعد إحيائه تمسك يده فلا يقتل أحداً (٢). قوله : ( فيفرُّ النَّاس) : أي : مع المهدي. (1) أخرجه مسلم (١٠٤/۲۹۳٤) عن حذيفة لله (۲) أخرجه مسلم (۱۱۳/۲۹۳۸) عن أبي سعيد الخدري الله الله
Written between his eyes: 'Kafir'. Every believer, literate or illiterate, reads it. He (Dajjal) seeks every source of water except Medina and Mecca, for Allah has forbidden them to him, and angels stand at their gates. With him are mountains of bread, and the people are in hardship except those who follow him. He has two rivers, I know them more than him: a river saying 'Paradise' and a river saying 'Hell'. Whoever enters what he calls Paradise will be in Hell, and whoever enters what he calls Hell will be in Paradise. He said: and with him are sent devils of Talakum, and with him is a great trial. He commands the sky to rain, in what the people see. He kills a soul then revives it, in what the people see. He says to the people: O people, does anyone do such things except the Lord? So the people flee to the mountain of smoke in Syria. He comes to them and besieges them, the siege tightens and he severely stresses them. Then Jesus, peace and blessings be upon him, descends. His saying: 'And with him are two rivers...' is the meaning of his saying in some narrations: 'With him is a garden and a fire.' His saying: 'devils' Talakum is a place name. His saying: 'And he kills a soul then revives it' means it is al-Khidr. It is narrated that he revives him and says: Did you not believe in me? He says: By Allah, I have only increased in certainty about you. Then after his revival, he takes hold of his hand and does not kill anyone. His saying: 'So the people flee' means with the Mahdi. (1) Muslim (2934/104) from Hudhayfah. (2) Muslim (2938/113) from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage details the deceptions and trials of the Dajjal as derived from authentic hadith. It describes the writing 'Kafir' on his forehead, readable by all believers regardless of literacy—a clear sign for believers to recognize him. He cannot enter Mecca or Medina, as angels guard them. He brings mountains of bread to attract followers, while others suffer. He has two rivers that he mislabels as Paradise and Hell to mislead people. The commentary clarifies that these are actually a garden and a fire, a test. The Dajjal also performs apparent miracles: commanding rain and reviving a dead person. The commentary identifies the revived person as al-Khidr, who, when revived, affirms his faith in Islam and then grabs the Dajjal's hand so he cannot kill anyone else. This shows the Dajjal's power is illusion. The people flee to the mountain of smoke (Jabal al-Dukhan) in Syria, where the Dajjal besieges them. Finally, Jesus descends to save them. The commentary adds that the flight is with the Mahdi.

Key Terms
يرد كل ماء ومنهل
الملائكة
جبال من خبز
نهر
الجنَّة
النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where can the Dajjal NOT go?
A) Any city with water
B) Mecca and Medina
C) The mountain of smoke
D) The Levant

Key Takeaway
The Dajjal's protection is limited by Allah's command, and his rivers are a deceptive test.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you saw a person offering you 'paradise' right now—something that feels like success, comfort, or pleasure—how would you test whether it is from Allah or from the Dajjal? What specific signs from this lesson would you apply?
?
The Dajjal cannot enter Mecca and Medina because angels guard them. Do you truly honor these cities in your heart? When was the last time you felt their sacredness and turned your soul toward them in devotion?
?
The Prophet's warning about the inverted rivers means you cannot trust your senses when appearances clash with divine truth. In your own life, what worldly 'paradise' have you been chasing that might actually be burning your soul? Will you turn away from it starting today?

Dajjal's Apparent Miracles and Al-Khidr
Describes Dajjal's miracles and al-Khidr's response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Dajjal's apparent miracles (causing rain and reviving the dead) are illusions, as shown by the story of al-Khidr who, after being revived, affirms his faith and restrains the Dajjal.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's miracle of reviving a dead person is exposed by al-Khidr's steadfast faith.

The Dajjal performs astonishing acts: he commands the sky to rain and even kills a man then revives him. But the commentary in this passage identifies the revived man as the prophet al-Khidr, who upon revival declares increased faith in Allah and physically grabs the Dajjal's hand, preventing further killing. This lesson reveals the true nature of these 'miracles'.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the miracles
Read how the Dajjal makes it rain and revives a dead person.
Note the phrase 'فيما يرى الناس' (in what the people see) – an important qualifier.
2
Identify al-Khidr's role
The commentary identifies the revived person as al-Khidr. Read his response to the Dajjal.
Al-Khidr's faith increases, and he physically restrains the Dajjal.
3
Understand the lesson
The Dajjal uses these signs to claim divinity, but the true believers are not deceived.
This shows that apparent power is not proof of truth.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the Dajjal can truly resurrect the dead, proving his divinity.
Correction: The passage shows that the revived person is al-Khidr, who does not worship the Dajjal but instead affirms his faith and restrains him, exposing the act as a trial, not a true miracle.

?
