?
The Dajjal's 'resurrection' appeared real 'in what the people see' (فيما يرى الناس). What apparent 'miracles' or successes in your life—wealth, status, relationships—might be deceptive trials rather than signs of divine favor? How can you distinguish between the two?
?
Al-Khidr's immediate response upon being revived was to affirm faith and physically resist the Dajjal. If you were given a second chance in a situation where you had previously compromised your faith, would you have the courage to stand firm and reject the deception? What is holding you back from that steadfastness now?

Flight to the Mountain of Smoke and Descent of Jesus
Describes the believers' flight to Jabal al-Dukhan and the descent of Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the believers will flee to Jabal al-Dukhan (Mountain of Smoke) in Syria, be besieged by the Dajjal, and then be saved by the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him), with the Mahdi leading the flight.

Core Idea
The believers' refuge is Jabal al-Dukhan, and their deliverance is through Jesus and the Mahdi.

As the Dajjal's persecution intensifies, the believers, led by the Mahdi, flee to a mountain called Jabal al-Dukhan in Syria. The Dajjal besieges them, causing severe hardship. Then, at the height of their distress, Jesus descends from heaven to save them. This lesson covers the final stages of the Dajjal's trial.

Guided Path
1
Read the flight to the mountain
Read how the people flee to Jabal al-Dukhan and are besieged.
Note the location: Syria.
2
Understand the Mahdi's role
The commentary adds that the flight is with the Mahdi.
The Mahdi is the leader of the believers at that time.
3
Learn about the descent of Jesus
The siege ends with the descent of Jesus, who will defeat the Dajjal.
Jesus' descent is a major event in Islamic eschatology.

The Dajjal Narrative and the Descent of Jesus
Al-Sawi explains the Dajjal's signs and the descent of Jesus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the signs of the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus as described in the hadith, and the caution against being deceived by false miracles.

Core Idea
The Dajjal's deception includes false signs, but true believers see through them by Allah's guidance.

This passage takes us into one of the major eschatological events: the appearance of the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus. Al-Sawi expounds on the hadith narrative, highlighting the Dajjal's deceptive miracles and the ultimate defeat by Jesus. Let's explore the details.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the hadith's own flow come through before you interpret the gloss.
Notice the vivid imagery of the Dajjal's mark and rivers.
2
Examine the commentary notes
Al-Sawi inserts brief clarifications. Pay special attention to his explanation of the two rivers and the identity of the revived man (al-Khidr).
These notes show how scholars resolve apparent contradictions in narrations.
3
Reflect on the descent of Jesus
Consider how Jesus's arrival turns the tide. He refuses to lead prayer out of respect for the Mahdi, then kills the Dajjal. Notice the cosmic call of trees and stones.
This highlights the thoroughness of the Dajjal's defeat.
4
Connect to eschatological lessons
Ask yourself: What does this narrative teach about faith and trials? Why are these details preserved in the tradition?
The passage strengthens belief in the unseen and warns against false messiahs.

قوله : ( فيفرُّ النَّاس) : أي : مع المهدي.
علامات يوم القيامة
فيأتي في السَّحَر فيقول : أيُّها النّاس ؛ ما يمنعكم أن تخرجوا إلى هذا الكذاب الخبيث، فينطلقون فإذا هم بعيسى فتقام الصَّلاة، فيقال له : تقدم يا روح الله ، فيقول : ليتقدَّم إمامُكُم فليصل بكم، فإذا صلوا صلاةَ الصُّبح خرجوا إليه، فحين يراه الكذَّابُ فينماع – أي : يذوب – كما ينماع الملح في الماء، فيقتلُه حَتَّى إِنَّ الشَّجر والحَجَر يُنادي : يا الله ؛ هذا يهودي، فلا يترك ممَّن كان يتّبعه أحداً إلا قتله»(۱) روح أحاديث بمعنى ذلك. انتهى، ذكره السيوطي الصحيح وفي
قوله : (فيأتي في السَّحر ) : أي : في وقته .
قوله : ( ليتقدَّم إمامكم) : أي : وهو المهدي.
Written between his eyes: 'disbeliever', which every believing reader, literate or illiterate, reads; he turns away from every water and watering-place except Madinah and Makkah, which Allah has forbidden to him, and the angels are stationed at their gates; with him are mountains of bread, and people are in hardship except those who follow him; with him are two rivers, I know more about them than he does: a river says 'Paradise' and a river says 'Hellfire'; whoever enters what he calls Paradise is in the Fire, and whoever enters what he calls Fire is in Paradise. He said: 'And with him are sent devils of Taklam, and with him is a great trial; he commands the sky to rain in what people see, and he kills a soul then revives it in what people see, and he says to the people: 'O people! Can anyone do such things except the Lord?' So the people flee to the Mountain of Smoke in Syria, and he comes to them and besieges them, and his siege becomes severe and he puts them to great hardship, then Jesus (peace and blessings be upon him) descends.'
His saying: '(And with him are two rivers... etc.)' means his saying in some narrations: 'With him are a Paradise and a Fire' (1).
His saying: 'devils' – Taklam is the name of a place.
His saying: '(And he kills a soul then revives it)' means: and he is al-Khidr; it is narrated that he revives him and says to him: 'Have you not believed in me?' So he says to him: 'By Allah, I have only increased in insight concerning you.' Then after his revival, he seizes his hand and does not kill anyone (2).
His saying: '(So the people flee)' means: with the Mahdi.
Signs of the Day of Judgment:
'He comes at dawn and says: 'O people! What prevents you from going out to this wicked liar?' So they set out, and suddenly they are with Jesus, and the prayer is established, and it is said to him: 'Come forward, O Spirit of Allah.' He says: 'Let your imam come forward and lead you in prayer.' So when they pray the dawn prayer, they go out to him. When the liar sees him, he melts – i.e., dissolves – as salt dissolves in water, and he kills him until even the tree and stone call out: 'O Allah, this is a Jew!' So he leaves not one of those who followed him except he kills him.' (1) Narrations with that meaning. End. Mentioned by al-Suyuti, the authentic, and in...
His saying: '(He comes at dawn)' means: at its time.
His saying: '(Let your imam come forward)' means: and he is the Mahdi.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the hadith describing the Dajjal (the Antichrist) and the subsequent descent of Jesus (peace be upon him). It combines the main text from al-Kharida with the gloss of al-Sawi. The commentary begins by quoting the main text: 'Written between his eyes: disbeliever, which every believing reader reads...' This describes the Dajjal's mark. Then it explains that the Dajjal will have two rivers, one appearing as Paradise but being Fire, and vice versa. The commentator clarifies that this is the meaning of other narrations mentioning a 'Paradise' and a 'Fire' with him. The Dajjal also has devils from a place called Taklam. He performs false miracles: commanding rain and reviving the dead (specifically al-Khidr, who after revival refuses to follow him and is protected). People flee to the Mountain of Smoke in Syria, and then Jesus descends. The narrative continues with Jesus coming in the early morning, leading prayer, and then killing the Dajjal. The commentator notes that 'at dawn' means at that time, and 'your imam' refers to the Mahdi. The passage concludes with a note that such narrations are found in authentic sources, citing al-Suyuti.

Correction: They are deceptions; what appears as Paradise leads to Hell and vice versa.

Ya'juj and Ma'juj: Their Identity and Origins
Al-Sawi defines Ya'juj and Ma'juj and explains their genealogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ya'juj and Ma'juj are two historical tribes from the lineage of Yafith, son of Noah, and that their names are foreign proper nouns with two canonical Quranic pronunciations.

Core Idea
Ya'juj and Ma'juj are real tribes from Noah's son Yafith.

The third major sign of the Day of Judgment is the emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj. Before we can grasp their prophetic role, we must first know who they are. This lesson clarifies their lineage, the origin of their names, and their vast numbers as reported by Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic source passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: definition, then linguistic notes, then genealogy.
The passage is in three parts: identity, name explanation, lineage.
2
Understand the name 'Ya'juj and Ma'juj'
Note that the names are foreign proper nouns with no Arabic derivation. They are indeclinable. The two pronunciations (with and without hamz) are both valid Quranic readings.
This shows the Quranic authenticity of both forms.
3
Trace the lineage from Noah
Learn the three sons of Noah: Sam, Ham, Yafith. Each is the ancestor of different peoples. Yafith is the father of Turks, Berbers, Sicily, and Ya'juj and Ma'juj.
This genealogy places Ya'juj and Ma'juj firmly within human history.
4
Reflect on Ibn Abbas's statement
Ibn Abbas says they are ten parts of humanity while all others are one part. This emphasizes their enormous number and their disbelief.
This underscores the scale of their emergence as a sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله : (يأجوج ومأجوج ) : اسمان أعجميَّان لا اشتقاق لهما، ومنعا من الصَّرف للعلمية والعجمة .
قوله : (بالهمز ودونه :أي: فهما لغتان وقراءتان سبعيتان.

His saying: (Ya'juj and Ma'juj): two foreign names with no derivation, and they are prevented from declension due to being proper nouns and foreign.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the third major sign of the Day of Judgment: the emergence of Ya'juj and Ma'juj. The main text states that they are two tribes from the children of Yafith son of Noah, and thus from the progeny of Adam, without any disagreement. The commentator then explains the name: 'Ya'juj and Ma'juj' are foreign proper names with no etymological derivation, and they are indeclinable because of being proper nouns and foreign. The variant 'with hamz and without' means there are two pronunciations, both of which are canonical Quranic readings. Then the commentator expands on the genealogy: Noah had three sons: Sam, Ham, and Yafith. Sam is the ancestor of the Persians, Arabs, and Byzantines; Ham of the Abyssinians, Zanj, and Nubians; Yafith of the Turks, Berbers, and Sicily, and also Ya'juj and Ma'juj. A quote from Ibn Abbas is given: 'They are ten parts, and the rest of Adam's children are one part, all of them disbelievers.' This emphasizes their immense number and their disbelief.

?

The Dajjal and the Descent of Jesus
Hadith on Dajjal and Jesus's descent with hashia commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of events surrounding the Dajjal's appearance and Jesus's descent, as described in a prophetic hadith and its commentary.

Core Idea
The Dajjal melts like salt when he sees Jesus, who destroys him utterly.

This lesson presents a hadith describing one of the major signs of the Hour: the coming of the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him). We will read the report, notice the miraculous events, and see how the commentary clarifies key details about the imam and the timing.

Guided Path

This shows the divine power at work.
3
Understand the commentary

The commentary ties the hadith to the figure of al-Mahdi.
4

Commentary
This passage is a hadith combined with commentary from the hashia. It describes one of the major signs of the Hour: the coming of the Dajjal and the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him). The hadith begins with the Dajjal appearing at dawn and addressing the people, accusing them of not going out to the 'lying wicked one' (i.e., the Dajjal himself). The people then find themselves with Jesus, who is asked to lead the prayer. Jesus declines, saying the imam (al-Mahdi) should lead. After the morning prayer, they go out to the Dajjal, and when the Dajjal sees Jesus, he melts like salt. Jesus then kills him, with even the trees and stones calling out to warn that a Jew is hiding behind them, leading to the killing of all the Dajjal's followers. The commentary then clarifies two points: (1) 'comes at dawn' means in its time, and (2) 'your imam' refers to al-Mahdi. The passage concludes by noting that al-Suyuti mentioned this hadith in his Sahih collection.

The Lineage and Linguistic Notes of Gog and Magog
Definition and lineage of Gog and Magog, with linguistic and numerical details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the lineage of Gog and Magog as descendants of Japheth, the linguistic features of their names, and their immense numbers as reported by Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are two tribes from the progeny of Adam, descendants of Japheth, and they outnumber the rest of humanity.

This lesson begins with the identification of Gog and Magog as the third major sign of the Hour. We explore their lineage from Japheth son of Noah, and the linguistic peculiarities of their names. The passage also highlights the vast population of these tribes, emphasizing their significance in eschatological events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on lineage
Read the Arabic passage describing the origin of Gog and Magog. Notice that they are from the children of Japheth bin Noah, placing them in the lineage of Adam.
The text emphasizes that there is no disagreement about this descent.
2
Understand the linguistic notes
The names 'Yajuj and Majuj' are foreign, indeclinable, and have two pronunciations (with and without hamzah). Learn that these are canonical Quranic readings.
The commentary clarifies that these are proper nouns with no derivation.
3
Explore Noah's three sons
The passage lists the peoples descending from Shem, Ham, and Japheth. Note that Gog and Magog are from Japheth, along with Turks, Berbers, and Sicilians.
This helps situate Gog and Magog among known genealogies.
4
Reflect on the vast numbers
Ibn Abbas is quoted saying that Gog and Magog constitute ten parts of humanity, while all other humans are one part. All of them are disbelievers.
This shows their enormous population and sets the stage for their role in end-times.

Commentary
This passage is a combination of definition, lineage, and a detailed hadith about Gog and Magog (Yajuj and Majuj). It begins by identifying the emergence of Gog and Magog as the third sign of the Hour. It explains their lineage: they are two tribes from the children of Japheth (Yafith) son of Noah, thus descendants of Adam. The commentary then provides linguistic notes: the names are non-Arabic, indeclinable, and have two readings with and without hamzah. It expands on Noah's three sons and the peoples descending from each, noting that Gog and Magog are from Japheth. Ibn Abbas's statement that they are ten parts of humanity, all disbelievers, underscores their vast number.

The passage then presents the hadith from Muslim, narrated by al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an. After Jesus kills the Dajjal, Allah commands him to retreat to Mount Tur because He has released Gog and Magog, whom no one can fight. They emerge rapidly in huge numbers, passing by the Lake of Tiberias and drinking it dry. They besiege Jesus and his companions so severely that an ox head becomes extremely valuable. Jesus and his companions supplicate, and Allah sends maggots that kill them all instantly. Then their corpses fill the earth, causing stench. Jesus and his companions supplicate again, and Allah sends huge birds to carry the corpses away. The hadith also notes that the Prophet called Gog and Magog to faith on the Night of Isra, but they refused. The commentary explains: 'supplicates' means prays and pleads; 'their corpses' means their dead bodies causing stench; with regard to 'wherever Allah wills', some narrations specify the sea. Finally, it mentions that Gog and Magog will not enter Mecca, Medina, or Jerusalem.

?

The Divine Destruction of Gog and Magog
Hadith of Gog and Magog's destruction, including the siege of Jesus and divine punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed hadith about the destruction of Gog and Magog after the Dajjal, including their rapid emergence, the siege of Jesus, the divine punishment by maggots, and the removal of their corpses by birds.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog will be destroyed by divine punishment (maggots), not by human armies, and their corpses will be removed by giant birds.

This lesson presents the lengthy hadith from Muslim narrated by al-Nawwas ibn Sam'an. It describes the events following Jesus's victory over the Dajjal: the release of Gog and Magog, their vast numbers, the siege of Jesus and his followers, and their miraculous destruction through maggots sent by Allah. The hadith concludes with the removal of their bodies by birds, and a note that they will not enter certain holy cities.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith from Muslim
Read the hadith carefully from the point where Allah commands Jesus to retreat to Mount Tur until the end.
Notice the detailed sequence of events.
2
Identify the key events
Outline the stages: release of Gog and Magog, their drinking of Lake Tiberias, siege of Jesus, supplication, death by maggots, filling of earth with corpses, and removal by birds.
Each event is a distinct stage of the narrative.
3
Reflect on the divine intervention
Note that the destruction is entirely by Allah's power: maggots kill them, birds remove corpses. No human effort is involved.
This emphasizes Allah's absolute control over creation.
4
Consider the additional notes
The commentary adds that the Prophet called them to faith on the Night of Isra but they refused, and that they will not enter Mecca, Medina, or Jerusalem.
These details enrich the eschatological picture.

Commentary

The Hadith of Gog and Magog from Muslim
Al-Sawi transmits the hadith of Gog and Magog with explanatory glosses on key phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the events surrounding the emergence and destruction of Gog and Magog as described in Sahih Muslim, as well as al-Sawi's explanatory glosses.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog's destruction is a divine intervention after the believers' prayer.

This lesson presents a hadith from Sahih Muslim that details the appearance of Gog and Magog after Jesus kills the Dajjal. Al-Sawi's commentary clarifies key phrases, helping us understand the narrative's details and the miraculous purification of the earth.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the Arabic passage once for rhythm, then the translation to understand the narrative flow.
Notice the parentheses in the Arabic - they mark al-Sawi's explanatory glosses.
2
Identify the major events
List the sequence: Jesus commanded to go to Mount Sinai, Gog and Magog emerge, they drink Lake Tiberias, besiege believers, believers pray, worms kill Gog and Magog, stench fills earth, birds remove corpses, rain purifies earth.
This sequence shows the pattern of calamity followed by divine relief.
3
Examine al-Sawi's glosses
Focus on his explanations of 'beseech' (يرغب) as supplication and 'their stench' (زهمتهم) as putrid bodies. These clarify the Arabic idioms.
Al-Sawi also notes that the Prophet called Gog and Magog to faith on the Night of Ascension, but they refused.
4
Reflect on the theological lesson
Consider how the hadith teaches reliance on Allah through supplication in times of extreme trial, and the certainty of divine justice.
This reinforces the importance of dua (supplication) in Islamic eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
روى مسلم من حديث النّوّاس بن سمعان : إنّ الله تعالى يوحي إلى عيسى عليه السلام بعد قتله الدَّجَّال : أنّي قد أخرجتُ عباداً لي لا يَدانِ لأحد بقتالهم فَحَرِّزْ عبادي إلى الطور، ويبعث الله يأجوج ومأجوج وهم من كلِّ حَدَب يَنْسِلون - أي من كل نشز يمشون مسرعين – فيمرّ أوائلهم على بحيرة طبرية، فيشربون ماءها – وهي بالشّام، طولها عشرة أميال – ويمرُّ آخرهم فيقولون: لقد كان بهذا أَثَرُ ماء، ويحصرون عيسى وأصحابه حتى يكون رأسُ الثَّور لأحدهم خيراً من مئة دينار لأحدكم، فيرغَبُ نبيُّ الله وأصحابه إلى الله تعالى، فيرسل الله عليهم النَّغَفَ في رقابهم، فيصبحون فرسى كموت نفس واحدة ثم يهبط الله عيسى وأصحابه في الأرض فلا يجدون في الأرض موضع شبر إلا ملأته زهمتهم فيرغب إلى الله نبي الله وأصحابه، فيرسل الله طيراً كأعناق البُخْت، فتحملهم فتطرحهم حيث شاء الله، دعاهم النَّبِيُّ الله إلى الإيمان ليلة الإسراء فلم يجيبوا (۱) . قوله : (فيرغب نبي الله ) : أي : يدعو ويتضرّع قوله :(زهمتهم) : أي جيفتهم فتنتن الأرض منهم . قوله: (فتطرحهم حيث شاء الله ) : في بعض الروايات : فتطرحهم في البحر ) (۲) ، ولا يدخلون مكَّة ولا المدينة ولا بيت المقدس(۳)، ولا ثم يرسل الله تعالى مطراً لا يكن منه بيت مدر ولا وبر، فيغسل الأرض حتى يتركها كالزَّلَفَة، ثم يقال للأرض : أنبتي ثمرك . . . » الحديث (۱).
Muslim narrated from the hadith of al-Nuwwas ibn Sam'an: Indeed Allah Most High reveals to Jesus peace be upon him after he kills the Dajjal: 'I have brought out servants of Mine whom no one has the power to fight, so move My servants to the Mount.' And Allah sends Gog and Magog, and they are from every hill rushing forth - i.e., from every elevation walking quickly. So their first ones pass by the Lake of Tiberias, they drink its water - and it is in Syria, its length ten miles - and their last ones pass and they say: 'There used to be water here.' And they besiege Jesus and his companions until the head of an ox for one of them is better than a hundred dinars for one of you. So the Prophet of Allah and his companions beseech Allah Most High, so Allah sends upon them worms in their necks, and they become like a single dead person. Then Allah brings down Jesus and his companions to the earth, and they do not find on the earth a handspan but it is filled with their stench. So the Prophet of Allah and his companions beseech Allah, so Allah sends birds like the necks of Bactrian camels, and they carry them and throw them where Allah wills. The Prophet of Allah called them to faith on the Night of Ascension but they did not respond (1). His statement: 'so the Prophet of Allah beseeches' means he supplicates and humbles himself. His statement: 'their stench' means their corpses, so the earth stinks from them. His statement: 'and throws them where Allah wills' in some narrations: and throws them into the sea (2), and they do not enter Mecca, nor Medina, nor Jerusalem (3), nor. Then Allah Most High sends rain which no house of clay or hair can keep out, and it washes the earth until it leaves it like a mirror. Then it is said to the earth: Bring forth your fruit... the hadith (1).
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a hadith report from Sahih Muslim about the appearance and destruction of Gog and Magog in the end times. The commentator (al-Sawi) inserts explanatory notes within the hadith. The hadith begins with Allah revealing to Jesus after he kills the Dajjal to take the believers to Mount Sinai because of the emergence of Gog and Magog. They are described as numerous, rushing from every high place. They pass the Lake of Tiberias and drink all its water, astonishing later arrivals. They besiege Jesus and his followers until cattle become more valuable than gold. Jesus and his companions pray, and Allah sends a worm-like creature that kills them all at once. Then the earth becomes filled with their corpses. Jesus and his companions pray again, and Allah sends large birds that remove the corpses to the sea (according to one version). A comment notes that the Prophet called Gog and Magog to faith on the Night of Ascension but they refused. The commentator also clarifies the meanings of 'beseech' (يرغب) as supplication and pleading, and 'their stench' (زهمتهم) as their putrid bodies. After their removal, Allah sends a heavy rain that cleans the earth completely, then commands the earth to produce its fruit. The hadith ends with the phrase 'the hadith'. This passage conveys the calamity of Gog and Magog and the divine intervention to save the believers and purify the earth.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
الدَّجَّال
الطور
النَّغَف
زهمتهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith is a continuous narrative without commentary, but the text includes al-Sawi's explanatory glosses.
Correction: The parentheses in the Arabic text indicate al-Sawi's own clarifications of key phrases, such as 'beseech' and 'stench'. Recognizing this helps distinguish the original hadith from the commentary.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What specific situation are you holding back from bringing before Him today, and what will it cost you to keep relying on your own strength alone?

?
After the destruction, Allah cleanses the earth with rain, leaving it pure and fruitful. What spiritual 'stench' in your heart—like pride, envy, or attachment to sin—needs to be washed away? Will you humble yourself today in sincere repentance, asking Allah to restore you to purity, and what will you change starting now?

The Immense Multitudes of Gog and Magog
Al-Sawi cites reports on the huge numbers and sizes of Gog and Magog.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extraordinary numbers and physical descriptions of Gog and Magog as reported in an additional tradition from al-Tha'labi.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are described as massive nations with astonishing reproductive rates and giant sizes.

This passage from al-Tha'labi supplements the earlier discussion of Gog and Magog with vivid details about their population and physical characteristics. The Prophet's response to Hudhayfa's question paints a picture of immense multitudes and prodigious offspring. As you read, note how these descriptions underscore the scale of the eschatological events.

Read the passage and translation

These numbers emphasize the overwhelming scale of Gog and Magog.
3
Reflect on the genre

Commentary
This passage is an additional report from al-Tha'labi's commentary, citing a hadith from Hudhayfa. It describes the immense numbers and physical characteristics of Gog and Magog. The Prophet answers that they are many nations (أمم), each nation numbering four hundred thousand. They are prolific: a man does not die until he sees a thousand offspring from his loins. They are descendants of Adam. The commentator notes a variant that they are two mountains containing 4,000 nations each. Another variant says each individual sees a thousand male descendants carrying weapons. The passage also mentions that they come in different types, with one type being 120 cubits tall. This material reinforces the extraordinary magnitude of these eschatological figures.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadith describes each man of Gog and Magog seeing a thousand offspring from his loins. What does this extreme fecundity teach you about the scale of the trials that will come? How does it change your view of the importance of preparing for the Hour, knowing that such multitudes will appear?
?
If Gog and Magog include giants of 120 cubits, this challenges our assumptions about normal human size. How does this make you reconsider what is possible in Allah's creation? Does your heart tremble at the power of Allah to create such beings? What should you do today to strengthen your faith in the unseen?
?
The Prophet gave precise numbers about these nations. Do you treat these reports with the same certainty as other matters of faith? If you truly believed such multitudes are coming, how would it change your priorities in life? What is one concrete action you can take this week to live with more awareness of the Last Day?

Hadith about the Rain that Cleans the Earth on the Day of Judgment
Presents a hadith about rain that cleans the earth on the Day of Judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand one of the major signs of the Day of Judgment as described in a prophetic hadith, specifically the rain that cleanses the earth.

Core Idea
The rain on Judgment Day will cleanse the earth completely, making it smooth and ready for resurrection.

This lesson presents a hadith that describes a remarkable event on the Day of Judgment: a rain that no shelter can escape, which washes the earth until it becomes like a smooth, flat surface. This is one of the signs that precede the resurrection and the command for the earth to bring forth its fruit. The passage is concise but rich in imagery and theological significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the literal meaning. Notice the key terms like 'مطر' (rain) and 'زلفة' (smooth surface).
The hadith is part of a longer narration; we focus on this segment.
2
Understand the imagery
The hadith describes a rain that penetrates all shelters, washing the earth until it is like 'الزَّلَفَة' — a smooth, clean surface. Visualize this cleansing process.
This imagery emphasizes the thoroughness of divine action.
3
Connect to the Day of Judgment context
This rain is one of the signs preceding the resurrection. After cleansing, the earth is commanded to produce its fruit, indicating the renewal of life.
This hadith is often cited as a minor sign or a precursor to major events.
4
Reflect on the theological meaning
The hadith highlights Allah's absolute power over the earth and the certainty of resurrection. The cleansing rain symbolizes purification before the final judgment.
Consider how this aligns with Islamic eschatology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامات يوم القيامة. ثم يرسل الله تعالى مطراً لا يكن منه بيت مدر ولا وبر، فيغسل الأرض حتى يتركها كالزَّلَفَة، ثم يقال للأرض : أنبتي ثمرك . . . » الحديث (۱).
Signs of the Day of Judgment. Then Allah the Exalted sends rain from which no house of mud or hair can shelter, so it washes the earth until it leaves it like a smooth surface, then it is said to the earth: bring forth your fruit... the hadith.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a hadith about one of the major signs of the Day of Judgment. It describes a rain that will cover the entire earth, cleansing it until it becomes smooth and flat like a mirror (كالزَّلَفَة). Then the earth is commanded to bring forth its fruit, indicating the resurrection. The hadith is cited with a footnote reference.

Key Terms

علامات يوم القيامة

Checkpoint

A) It floods it
B) It cleans it until it becomes smooth like a mirror
C) It destroys it
D) It brings forth vegetation

Key Takeaway
The hadith teaches that one of the signs of the Day of Judgment is a universal rain that cleanses the earth completely, leaving it smooth and ready for the command to bring forth new life.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Knowing that one day the earth will be stripped bare by a rain that no shelter can protect you from, how does that affect your attachment to your home and possessions? Will you be ready to face that day?
?
The hadith shows that even the earth is commanded to bring forth its fruit. What fruit (good deeds) will you have brought forth on that day when you stand before your Lord?
?
This rain is unavoidable and will cleanse the earth completely. What are you depending on for shelter from Allah's judgment? Is it your deeds, your status, or your wealth? Are they any more able to shield you than a house of mud or hair?

The Nations of Gog and Magog: Numbers and Origin
Hudhayfah's hadith on the numbers and origin of Gog and Magog.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the enormous numbers of Gog and Magog as described in the hadith, and their descent from Prophet Adam.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are countless nations from Adam's offspring.

The hadith from Hudhayfah provides foundational details about Gog and Magog: they are numerous nations, each consisting of 400,000 individuals, and they are human descendants of Adam. This lesson unpacks the numbers and lineage from the source.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith from Hudhayfah
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the question and answer.
2
Focus on the numbers
Note that each 'ummah' (nation) consists of 400,000, and there are many such nations. Also note the phrase 'two mountains' with 4,000 nations each.
The numbers are immense beyond ordinary imagination.
3
Understand their lineage
The hadith explicitly says 'they are from the children of Adam'. This corrects any misconception that they are not human.
This is important for theological discussions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التَّعلبي من حديث حذيفة قلت يا رسول الله ؛ ما يأجوج ومأجوج ؟ قال : أمم كلُّ أمة أربع مئة ألف، لا يموت الرَّجل حتّى عين تطوف بين يديه من صلبه وهم من ولد آدم، فيسيرون ألف یری يصلون إلى من تحصّن بورد أو ذكر . قوله : (أمم) : في بعض الروايات : إنَّهما جبلان، كلُّ جبل مشتمل على أربعة آلاف أمة . قوله : حتَّى يرى ألف عين ... إلخ) في رواية: لا يموت الواحد منهم حتّى يرى ألف ذكر من صلبه كلُّهم صلبه كلُّهم قد حمل السلاح؛ وهم أصناف، صنف منهم طوله عشرون ومئة ذراع في السَّماء، وصنف منهم طوله إلى خَراب الدُّنيا، فيكون مقدَّمتُهم بالشَّام، وساقتهم بالعراق، فيمرون بأنهار الدنيا فيشربون الفرات ودجلة وبحيرة طبريَّة، حتّى يأتون بيت المقدس، فيقولون قد قتلنا أهل الدنيا، فقاتلوا من في السَّماء، فيرمون نُشَّابهم إلى السَّماء، فيردُّ الله تعالى نشابهم محمّراً دماً(۱) وقد ورد أنَّ الدَّجَّال يقتله عيسى بن مريم فيخرج بعده يأجوج ومأجوج فيقتلون من اتَّبَع الدَّجَّال الذي قتله عيسى، وينحصر عيسى وعرضه سواء عشرون ومئة ذراع، وصنف منهم يفترش أحدهم إحدى أذنيه ويلتحف بالأخرى لا يمرُّون بفيل ولا وحش ولا خنزير إلّا أكلوه ومن أكلوه (٢) مات منهم
And in al-Tha'labi from the hadith of Hudhayfah: I said, O Messenger of Allah, what are Gog and Magog? He said: Nations, each nation four hundred thousand. A man does not die until a thousand eyes parade before him from his loins, and they are from the children of Adam. They march, a thousand [?] they reach whoever takes refuge in a fortress or remembrance. His saying: (Nations): in some narrations: they are two mountains, each mountain containing four thousand nations. His saying: Until he sees a thousand eyes... etc. in a narration: Not one of them dies until he sees a thousand males from his loins, all of them from his loins, all of them carrying weapons; and they are types: a type whose height is one hundred twenty cubits in the sky, and a type whose height extends to the ruin of the world, so their vanguard is in Syria and their rear in Iraq. They pass by the rivers of the world and drink the Euphrates, the Tigris, and the Sea of Tiberias until they come to Jerusalem. They say: we have killed the people of the earth, so fight those in the sky. They shoot their arrows to the sky, and Allah returns their arrows red with blood. And it has been narrated that the Dajjal is killed by Jesus son of Mary, then Gog and Magog emerge after him and kill those who followed the Dajjal whom Jesus killed, and Jesus is besieged [?]. And its width is the same: one hundred twenty cubits. And a type of them spread one of their ears and wrap themselves with the other. They pass by no elephant, wild beast, or pig but they eat it, and whoever eats it dies.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage collects several narrations about Gog and Magog (يأجوج ومأجوج). It begins with a hadith from Hudhayfah where the Prophet describes them as countless nations, each consisting of 400,000 individuals. They are from the children of Adam. Their reproduction rate is so high that each man sees a thousand of his offspring before dying. Additional details from other narrations mention their enormous size, with some reaching 120 cubits tall. Their destructive march across the world includes drinking up great rivers and advancing to Jerusalem. In their arrogance, they shoot arrows at the sky, which Allah returns bloodied. Another narration links them to the Dajjal: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and kill the Dajjal's followers. Physical descriptions include giant ears used as bedding. Their hunger is insatiable, devouring every animal. These descriptions underscore their monstrous nature and the divine power that will eventually destroy them.

Key Terms
يأجوج ومأجوج
أمم
ولد آدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Gog and Magog are not human but monsters or demons.
Correction: The hadith explicitly states 'they are from the children of Adam', confirming their humanity.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith from Hudhayfah, how many are in each nation (أمة) of Gog and Magog?
A) 40,000
B) 400,000
C) 4,000
D) 4 million

Key Takeaway
Gog and Magog are enormous human nations from the lineage of Adam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Gog and Magog are real, physical human nations, or does your heart subtly doubt because your eyes have not seen them? How does this affect your certainty in everything else the Prophet has told us about the unseen? What can you do today to strengthen that certainty?
?
The hadith describes their numbers as enormous and their lineage from Adam like yours. When you consider that these are your own relatives from a distant time, does it make you feel any urgency to prepare for the Hour? What is one concrete step you can take this week to live with that awareness?
?
If you were among the people who will see Gog and Magog in their lifetime, what would be different about your faith today? Are you living as though that day could come at any moment, or do you treat it as a distant story? Ask yourself: what would change if you knew you had only one year before they appear?

The Physical Attributes and Destructive March of Gog and Magog
Descriptions of Gog and Magog's size, march, and arrow-shooting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical descriptions of Gog and Magog, including their gigantic size and their destructive actions as they march across the earth.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are giants who devastate land and sea, defying even the sky.

Following the initial hadith about their numbers, additional narrations describe Gog and Magog in vivid physical detail: some are 120 cubits tall, they drink entire rivers, and even shoot arrows at the heavens. This lesson examines these extraordinary attributes and actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of their size
Focus on the two types: some are 120 cubits tall, others extend to the ruin of the world. Notice the contrast.
2
Trace their march
Follow their path from Syria to Iraq, drinking rivers and reaching Jerusalem. Note their boastful speech.
3
Analyze the arrow incident
They shoot arrows at the sky, and Allah returns them bloodied. This shows their arrogance and Allah's power.
This is a sign of their delusion.

Gog and Magog in the End Times: Dajjal, Jesus, and the Final Battle
The eschatological role of Gog and Magog after the Dajjal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Gog and Magog in the end times, including their emergence after the death of the Dajjal at the hands of Jesus, and their eventual destruction.

Core Idea
After Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog emerge and wreak havoc until Allah destroys them.

The final portion of the source links Gog and Magog to the eschatological sequence: after Jesus kills the Dajjal, Gog and Magog appear and attack the followers of the Dajjal. This lesson also includes their bizarre physical description of using ears as bedding and their insatiable appetite.

Guided Path
1
Understand the sequence
Note the order: Dajjal killed by Jesus, then Gog and Magog emerge and kill Dajjal's followers. Jesus is besieged.
2
Examine the physical oddity
Some of them use one ear as a mattress and wrap with the other. This emphasizes their grotesque nature.
3
Reflect on their feeding
They eat every animal they encounter, including elephants and pigs, and then die. This shows their voraciousness and eventual demise.
The phrase 'whoever eats it dies' might refer to them dying from overconsumption or a divine plague.

Gog and Magog and the Dam of Dhul-Qarnayn
The author narrates the story of Gog and Magog, the building of the dam, and their destruction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narrative of Gog and Magog as described in the text, including their emergence after the Dajjal, the building of the dam by Dhul-Qarnayn, the daily digging and divine restoration, and their final destruction by a disease.

Core Idea
Gog and Magog are contained by a physical dam, but ultimately destroyed by Allah's command.

This passage from the Hashiyah narrates the events surrounding Gog and Magog after the Dajjal. The author describes their emergence, their enormous size, and the building of a massive dam by Dhul-Qarnayn. The story also emphasizes the miraculous preservation of the dam until the appointed time, when Gog and Magog are released and then destroyed by a plague in their necks.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then read the English translation. Note the sequence of events.
The Arabic contains some unclear OCR; focus on the main story.
2
Identify the key events
List the main events in order: emergence of Gog and Magog, description of their size and habits, building of the dam, daily digging, release, and destruction.
This is a chronological narrative.
3
Reflect on the divine role
Consider how the text emphasizes Allah's control over the dam's restoration and the final destruction of Gog and Magog.
The dam is restored daily until the appointed time.

Commentary
This passage narrates the events related to Gog and Magog after the Dajjal. The author begins by stating that the Dajjal is killed by Jesus, then Gog and Magog emerge. They are described as having enormous size, with one ear large enough to use as a mat and the other as a blanket. They devour everything. Then the narrative shifts to Dhul-Qarnayn, who builds a dam to contain them. The dam is constructed with iron and molten copper. The Gog and Magog dig at it daily but it is restored until the appointed time when they are released. Upon release, they drink water and people flee. Then Allah destroys them with a disease in their necks, causing them to die as one man. The passage ends with a citation from al-Nafrawi's commentary.

?

?
The destruction of Gog and Magog comes suddenly through a disease in their necks. Consider a sin you think you have under control. If your end came from an unexpected source, would you be ready to meet Allah? What is one step you can take right now to turn back to Him?

The Beast of the Earth: The Fourth Major Sign
The author lists the Beast as the fourth sign and explains its speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Beast of the Earth as the fourth major sign of the Hour, its Quranic basis, and the three interpretations of its speech.

Core Idea
The Beast speaks multiple things—everyone will know their destiny.

Among the major signs of the Hour is the emergence of a mysterious Beast that will speak to all people. The Quran mentions this event in Surah al-Naml. In this lesson, we explore the verse, its meaning, and the various traditions about what the Beast will say.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how the author first states the sign, then quotes the verse, explains it, and presents multiple interpretations.
Pay attention to the use of the past tense in the verse.
2
Identify the Beast's role
The Beast is the fourth major sign of the Hour. Understand that its primary function is to speak to people. Reflect on why speech is emphasized.
3
Examine the three interpretations
The passage lists three possible sayings of the Beast: (1) declaring nullity of all religions except Islam, (2) individually addressing each person about their fate, (3) stating that people were not certain of Allah's signs. Note that these are not mutually exclusive.
The different interpretations come from various traditions.
4
Reflect on the past tense usage
The verse uses the past tense ('We brought forth') even though the event is future. The author explains this is because all time is present in Allah's knowledge. Consider how this relates to divine omniscience.
5
Summarize the significance
This sign emphasizes individual accountability and the definitive truth of Islam. The Beast's speech will leave no doubt about one's fate or the validity of faith.
Think about how this sign relates to the purpose of life.

Source Text

The fourth of them: the emergence of the Beast that speaks to the people at the end of time, indicated by His saying, the Exalted: 'And when the word falls upon them, We will bring forth for them a Beast from the earth speaking to them' (Surah al-Naml: 82); that is, when the meaning of the word approaches upon them, which is what they were promised of resurrection and punishment, We will bring forth for them a Beast from the earth speaking to them. It is said: It speaks to them of the nullity of religions except the religion of Islam. And it is said: It says, 'O so-and-so, you are from the people of Paradise, and O so-and-so, you are from the people of Hellfire.' And it is said: It says, 'Indeed, mankind were not certain of Our signs.' His saying: (that is, when the occurrence of the meaning of the word approaches: that is, He only expressed it in the past tense because of its occurrence in Allah's knowledge; because the past, present, and future are all one in Allah's knowledge, due to His encompassing it.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage defines the fourth major sign of the Hour: the emergence of the Beast. The author cites the Quranic verse and explains its meaning: when the decree of resurrection and punishment is imminent, Allah will bring forth a Beast that speaks to people. He then presents three interpretations of what the Beast will say: (1) it will declare the nullity of all religions except Islam, (2) it will individually address each person telling them their fate in Paradise or Hell, or (3) it will state that people were not certain of Allah's signs. The author also comments on the use of the past tense in the verse, explaining that it is because all time is present in Allah's knowledge.

The Beast of the Earth will speak to everyone at the end of time, conveying their individual fate and the truth of Islam.

?
The passage mentions people were 'not certain of Our signs.' Are there signs of Allah in your life that you have dismissed or doubted? What would it take for you to become absolutely certain?

The Beast That Speaks: A Major Sign of the Hour
Al-Sawi defines the fourth major sign: the Beast and its speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth major sign of the Hour, the Beast's speech, and the scholarly interpretations of what it says.

Core Idea
The Beast's speech separates truth from falsehood on Judgment Day.

After discussing other major signs, al-Sawi now turns to the fourth: the emergence of the Beast. This passage explains the Beast's role in speaking to people at the end of time, citing the Quran and presenting multiple interpretations of its message. Let's read and explore.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Let the author's own words set the stage.
2
Identify the three interpretations of the Beast's speech
The passage lists three possible meanings of what the Beast will say. Mark each one and note the key difference between them.
The first two assign individuals to paradise or hell, while the third states general disbelief.
3
Understand the grammatical note about the past tense
The author explains why the Quran uses past tense for a future event. Consider how divine knowledge collapses time.
This shows the importance of God's timeless knowledge.
4
Reflect on the significance of this sign
Ask yourself: why is the Beast's speech a decisive sign? How does it relate to the final judgment?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رابعها : خروج الدَّابَّة التي تُكلّم النَّاس آخر الزمان المُشار إليها بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا وَقَعَ الْقَوْلُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَخْرَجْنَا لَهُمْ دَابَّةً مِّنَ الْأَرْضِ تُكَلِّمُهُمْ ﴾؛ أي : وإذا قَرُب وقوع معنى القول عليهم، وهو ما وعدوا به البعث والعذاب أخرجنا لهم دابَّةٌ من الأرض تكلّمهم. قيل : تُكلّمهم ببطلان الأديان إلا دين الإسلام. وقيل : تقول : يا فلان أنت من أهل الجَنَّة، ويا فلانُ أنت من أهل النار. وقيل : تقول : إنَّ النَّاس كانوا بآياتنا لا يوقنون. قوله : (أي: وإذا قرب وقوع معنى القول) أي: وإِنَّما عبّر بالماضي لحصوله في علم الله؛ لأنَّ الماضي والحال والاستقبال في علم الله واحد لإحاطته به.
The fourth of them: the emergence of the Beast that speaks to people at the end of time, referred to by His statement, the Exalted: {And when the word falls upon them, We will bring forth for them a Beast from the earth speaking to them} (Quran 27:82); meaning: when the occurrence of the meaning of the statement draws near upon them, which is what they were promised of resurrection and punishment, We brought forth for them a Beast from the earth speaking to them. It is said: It speaks to them about the invalidity of religions except the religion of Islam. And it is said: It says: Indeed, the people were not certain of Our signs. Commentary
This passage defines the fourth major sign of the Hour: the emergence of the Beast that speaks to people. It begins by naming this sign and citing the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Naml. The author explains the verse, interpreting 'when the word falls upon them' as when the promise of resurrection and punishment draws near. Then he presents three interpretations of what the Beast will say: first, that it declares all religions false except Islam; second, that it tells each person their destination of Paradise or Hell; third, that it says people were not certain of God's signs. This shows the Beast's speech is a decisive separation. Finally, the author comments on the grammatical aspect of the verse, noting that the past tense is used because everything is present in God's knowledge, and there is no temporal distinction for Him.

Hadith on the Beast's Emergence from the Sacred Mosque and Its Three Emergences
Al-Sawi narrates hadiths on the Beast's place of emergence and three emergences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith details regarding the Beast's place of emergence and its three distinct emergences as narrated by al-Sawi.

Core Idea
The Beast emerges in three stages, each with unique location and timing.

In this passage, al-Sawi presents two hadiths that provide specific details about the emergence of the Beast of the Earth. The first hadith identifies its starting point as the Sacred Mosque in Mecca. The second hadith elaborates on three separate emergences, each with distinct geographical and temporal features, culminating in a dramatic appearance during the time of Prophet Jesus. Understanding these details is important for eschatology.

Guided Path
1
Read the first hadith on place of emergence
The first hadith states that the Beast emerges from the greatest mosque, meaning al-Masjid al-Haram. Notice the wording 'from the greatest of mosques in sanctity'.
2
Identify the three emergences
The second hadith lists three emergences: in farthest Yemen, near Mecca, and a final one during Jesus's time. Note how the spread of news changes with each.
3
Observe the final emergence description
The final emergence is dramatic: the ground shakes, al-Safa splits, and the Beast's head emerges. Its size is immense—only a third emerges after three horse-days.
4
Learn the name of the Beast
The passage calls it al-Jassasa. Reflect on why it is called 'the spy' or 'the one who searches'.
5
Avoid a common misunderstanding
Some think the Beast emerges only once. The hadith clearly says 'three emergences', so understand that there are multiple appearances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سئل عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام عن مخرجها فقال: «من أعظم المساجد حرمة على الله تعالى»؛ يعني : المسجد الحرام. وروي عنه عليه الصَّلاة والسَّلام أنّ لها ثلاث خرجات : خَرْجة بأقصى اليمن، فيفشو ذِكْرُها في البادية، ولا يدخل ذِكرُها مكَّة، ثمَّ تمكث زمناً طويلاً، وخَرْجة قريبة من مكّة، فيفشو ذكرها بالبادية وبمكة، وخَرْجة بينما عيسى بن مريم بالبيت ومعه المسلمون، إذ تهتز الأرض تحتهم، وينشقُ الصَّفا مما يلي المشعر، فتخرج رأسُ الدَّابَّة من الصَّفا تجري الفرس ثلاثة أيام وما خرج ثلثها، وبعد خروجها يمس رأسُها السَّحابَ، وتسمى : الجسَّاسة.
He (peace and blessings be upon him) was asked about its place of emergence, and he said: 'From the greatest of mosques in sanctity to God Almighty'; meaning: the Sacred Mosque. And it is narrated from him (peace and blessings be upon him) that it has three emergences: an emergence in the farthest Yemen, and its mention spreads in the desert, and its mention does not enter Mecca, then it stays for a long time; and an emergence near Mecca, and its mention spreads in the desert and in Mecca; and an emergence while Jesus son of Mary is at the House with the Muslims, when the earth shakes beneath them, and al-Safa splits from the side of al-Mash'ar, so the head of the Beast emerges from al-Safa, overtaking a horse for three days while not even a third of it has emerged, and after its emergence its head touches the clouds, and it is called: al-Jassasa.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage narrates two hadiths concerning the Beast. The first hadith specifies that the Beast will emerge from the most sacred mosque, which is al-Masjid al-Haram in Mecca. The second hadith describes three emergences: first in the farthest part of Yemen, where knowledge of the Beast spreads in the desert but does not reach Mecca; after a long interval, a second emergence near Mecca, spreading both in the desert and in Mecca; and finally, a third emergence at a time when Jesus is in the House with the Muslims. At that moment, the earth shakes, al-Safa splits, and the Beast's head emerges from it. Its speed is such that a horse would take three days to cover the distance it emerges, yet only a third of its body would have appeared. After full emergence, its head reaches the clouds. This Beast is called al-Jassasa (the spy). The passage thus provides geographical and temporal details of the Beast's appearance.

Key Terms
المسجد الحرام
الخرجات
الجساسة
الصفا
المشعر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Beast of the Earth will emerge only once in a single event.
Correction: The hadith explicitly states there are three emergences: one in farthest Yemen, one near Mecca, and a final one during the time of Jesus.

Checkpoint
How many emergences does the Beast have according to the hadith?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The Beast of the Earth will emerge from the Sacred Mosque in three stages, the final one during the time of Jesus, and it is called al-Jassasa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Beast is called al-Jassasa, 'the spy' that exposes truth. If your hidden deeds were exposed today, what would they reveal? What single sin are you most afraid of being exposed, and what will you do about it tonight?
?
The Beast's emergence is a certainty, yet we live as if the Hour is distant. If you knew the Beast would appear tomorrow, what would you change about your daily routine starting now? Be specific.
?
During the third emergence, the earth shakes and the mountain splits. Is your faith rooted so deeply that it would withstand that shaking? What are you building your certainty upon—the scholars' words or your own conviction based on evidence?

The Beast: Size and Emergence Variants
Al-Sawi reports hadith on Beast's size and two emergence locations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the physical description of the Beast and the two narrations regarding where it emerges.

Core Idea
The Beast's size and emergence location are specified in hadith with variant reports.

This short passage from al-Sawi's commentary adds concrete details about the Beast's appearance and the place of its emergence. It clarifies that the Beast is described as sixty cubits long (using Adam's cubit), with legs, fur, and feathers. It also mentions two different narrations about where its head first appears: from al-Safa or from a specific spot near the Kaaba. Let's examine these details.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the specific details: length, limbs, and location options.
2
Identify the two narrations
The passage mentions two narrations about the Beast's emergence. Find them and note the differences.
One mentions al-Safa, the other mentions a location near the Kaaba's corner.
3
Understand the cubit clarification
The commentary explains that 'sixty' refers to sixty cubits using the cubit of Adam. Understand why this clarification is important.
This connects the hadith measurement to a prophetic scale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الحديث : أنَّ طولها ستُون ، ولها أربعة قوائم وزَغَب وريش. قوله : ( فتخرج رأس الدَّابَّة من الصَّفا هذا أحد روايتين، والأخرى أنَّها تخرج من بين الرُّكن حذاء دار بني مخزوم عن يمين الخارج من المسجد ). قوله : ( أنَّ طولها ستُون) : المراد ستون ذراعاً بذراع آدم كما ورد.
And in the hadith: that its length is sixty, and it has four legs, fur, and feathers. His statement: (so the head of the Beast emerges from al-Safa; this is one of two narrations, and the other is that it emerges from between the corner opposite the house of Banu Makhzum to the right of the one exiting the mosque). His statement: (that its length is sixty) means sixty cubits by the cubit of Adam, as has been reported.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage provides additional details about the Beast from another hadith. It states that the Beast has a length of sixty, implying cubits, and that it has four legs, fur, and feathers. It then discusses a variant regarding the location of its emergence: one narration says it emerges from al-Safa, while another says it emerges from between the corner (of the Kaaba) opposite the house of Banu Makhzum, to the right of the person leaving the mosque. Finally, it clarifies that the length of sixty refers to sixty cubits measured by the cubit of Adam, as mentioned in the reports. This shows the detailed physical description of the Beast.

The Emergence and Description of the Beast (Dābbah)
Hadith reports on the Beast's emergence, size, and composite features.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith reports on the Beast (dābbah), including its place of emergence, three emergences, size, and composite appearance as described in Islamic tradition.

Core Idea
The Beast of the End Times is a real, composite creature detailed through prophetic and companion reports.

This passage collects key hadith and companion reports about the Beast (dābbah) that will emerge near the end of time. It describes its place of emergence, multiple appearances, and a striking composite image formed from parts of many animals. These details affirm the tangible reality of the Beast as part of Islamic eschatology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the narrative flow.
Notice the sequence: place of emergence, three emergences, then description.
2

Find the three emergences: farthest Yemen, near Mecca, and the final one during Jesus' time. Note the details given for each.
The final emergence from al-Safa is described with dramatic imagery.
3

Review the description from Ka‘b, listing animal parts. Also note the other physical details like length, wings, and colors.
The Beast is said to have parts from donkey, ox, pig, elephant, ostrich, lion, leopard, cat, ram, and camel.

He, peace and blessings be upon him, was asked about its place of emergence and said: 'From the greatest mosques in sanctity to Allah,' meaning the Sacred Mosque. And it was narrated from him, peace and blessings be upon him, that it has three emergences: an emergence in farthest Yemen, and its mention spreads in the desert but does not enter Mecca, then it remains for a long time; and an emergence near Mecca, and its mention spreads in the desert and Mecca; and an emergence while Jesus son of Mary is at the House with the Muslims, when the earth shakes beneath them, and al-Safa splits from the side of al-Mash'ar, and the head of the Beast comes out from al-Safa, running as a horse runs for three days while only a third of it has emerged, and after its emergence its head touches the clouds, and it is called al-Jassāsah. His saying: ('Then the head of the Beast emerges from al-Safa') this is one of two narrations, and the other is that it emerges from between the Corner opposite the house of Banī Makhzūm to the right of the one leaving the mosque. His saying: ('Its length is sixty'): meaning sixty cubits by the cubit of Adam as has been reported. And two wings, no fugitive escapes it and no seeker catches it. And from Ka'b: its image is the image of a donkey; it is said: it has the head of an ox, the eye of a pig, the ear of an elephant, the neck of an ostrich, the chest of a lion, the color of a leopard, the flank of a cat, the tail of a ram, and the hoof of a camel. Commentary
This passage collects several hadith and reports about the Beast (dābbah) that emerges at the end of time. It begins by noting that the Prophet was asked about its place of emergence and replied that it comes from the greatest mosque in sanctity, i.e., the Sacred Mosque (Mecca). Then it mentions three separate emergences: one in Yemen, one near Mecca, and a final one during the time of Jesus, when the earth shakes and the Beast's head emerges from al-Safa. The Beast is called al-Jassāsah. Its length is given as sixty cubits (by Adam's cubit), and it has four legs, fur, and feathers. There are two narrations on the exact spot of emergence from Mecca. The Beast also has two wings, and nothing can escape it. A report from Ka'b describes its composite appearance combining parts of many animals: donkey, ox, pig, elephant, ostrich, lion, leopard, cat, ram, and camel. The gloss then explains two phrases from that description: 'ear of an ayyil' (a type of animal) and 'hoof of a camel', giving additional measurements. Finally, a hadith from Abu Hurayrah states it has every color and its horns are a farsakh apart, and the correct identification is that it is the young she-camel of Prophet Salih.

The Sun Rising from the West and the Closure of Repentance
Explanation of the fifth major sign: the sun rising from the west and its effect on repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth major sign of the Hour—the sun rising from the west—and its consequence of closing the door of repentance for sinful believers and disbelievers.

Core Idea
The sun rising from the west signals the final closure of repentance.

This lesson presents the fifth major sign of the Hour: the sun rising from the west. It explains the disagreement about its duration and clarifies its ultimate effect: the closing of the door of repentance. The passage distinguishes between the general view that it closes for all sinners and the minority view that it is specific to disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifth sign
Read the passage and note that the fifth major sign is the sun rising from the west. Recognize that this is a supernatural event that breaks the normal order.
2
Observe the difference of opinion
The passage mentions a difference: whether the sun rises from the west in one day or three. Notice that after this event, the sun sets in the east, disrupting its usual path.
3
Understand the closure of repentance
The key consequence is that the door of repentance is closed. The passage states it is closed for both the sinful believer and the disbeliever, but a minority view restricts it to the disbeliever. Reflect on the significance of this sign.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خامسها : طلوع الشمس من مغربها. ثمَّ واختلف في ذلك، هل هو في يوم واحد، أو في ثلاثة أيام، تطلع من المشرق على عادتها إلى يوم القيامة ، وإذا طلعت من المغرب غربت في المشرق، وعند ذلك يُغلق باب التّوبة على المؤمن العاصي والكافر ، وقيل : هو خاص بالكافر
Fifth of them: The rising of the sun from its west. Then they differed concerning this: whether it is in one day or in three days, it rises from the east as is its custom until the Day of Resurrection, and when it rises from the west it sets in the east, and at that time the door of repentance is closed upon the sinful believer and the disbeliever, and it is said: it is specific to the disbeliever.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth major sign of the Hour: the sun rising from the west. It notes a difference of opinion on whether this event happens in a single day or over three days, but the sun will rise from the west and then set in the east, breaking its normal pattern. The key consequence is that at that moment, the door of repentance (bāb al-tawbah) is closed. The text states that it is closed upon both the sinful believer (al-mu'min al-‘āṣī) and the disbeliever (al-kāfir), but a minority view restricts it to the disbeliever only. This sign marks the point after which no new repentance is accepted.

The Beast (Dābba) and Its Identification
Al-Sawi describes the beast's features and identifies it as Salih's she-camel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the beast (dābba) as a major sign of the Hour and its identification as the young she-camel of the prophet Salih.

Core Idea
The beast of the Hour is the young she-camel of Salih.

The beast (dābba) is one of the ten major signs of the Day of Resurrection. Scholars have described its appearance in detail, and there is a well-known identification that connects it to the miracle of Prophet Salih. In this passage, al-Sawi presents both the physical description and the correct identification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without analysing, then read the translation. Let the descriptions sink in before interpreting.
Notice the variety of animal parts mentioned.
2
Analyze the description of the beast

The beast is said to have features from multiple animals.
3
Understand the identification
Focus on the final part where al-Sawi states the correct view: the beast is the young she-camel of Salih. Read the story of how it hid in a rock after its mother was hamstrung.
This identification links the beast to a known prophetic miracle.

Signs of the Day of Resurrection: and two wings, no fugitive escapes it nor any pursuer catches it. And from Ka'b: its form is the form of a donkey; it is said: it has the head of a bull, the eye of a pig, the ear of a camel, the neck of an ostrich, the chest of a lion, the color of a leopard, the flank of a cat, the tail of a ram, and the hoof of a camel. Then a hadith from Abu Huraira describes its multicolored appearance and the great distance between its horns. Finally, Sawi notes the disagreement about which specific creature this beast is, and asserts that the correct view is that it is the young she-camel of the prophet Salih, which hid in a rock after its mother was hamstrung, and will emerge at the appointed time.

The Fifth Major Sign: Sun Rising from the West
Sawi presents the fifth sign and the initial debate on repentance closure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the fifth major sign (the sun rising from the west), the disagreement about its duration, and the two opinions regarding the closing of repentance.

Core Idea
The sun rising from the west signals the closure of repentance for all.

This passage introduces one of the major signs of the Hour: the sun rising from its west. It not only describes the phenomenon but also raises a key debate: does repentance close for everyone, or only for disbelievers? Let's explore Sawi's explanation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the fifth sign
Read the Arabic source and translation for the description of the sun rising from the west. Notice the disagreement about whether it happens in one day or three.
The sun normally rises from the east; this event is a reversal.
2
Identify the two opinions on repentance
The passage states that the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, but some say it is specific to the disbeliever. Understand both views.
The difference hinges on the interpretation of Quran 6:158.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this sign is placed at such a high station. It marks the point after which no repentance is accepted, so it emphasizes urgency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خامسها : طلوع الشمس من مغربها ثمَّ واختلف في ذلك، هل هو في يوم واحد، أو في ثلاثة أيام، تطلع من المشرق على عادتها إلى يوم القيامة، وإذا طلعت من المغرب غربت في المشرق، وعند ذلك يُغلق باب التوبة على المؤمن العاصي والكافر، وقيل : هو خاص بالكافر. قوله : (لقوله تعالى: يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانَهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا) ظاهره أنه دليل للقول الثاني وليس كذلك، بل الآية منشأ الخلاف، فقيل: إنَّ معناها لا ينفع نفساً؛ أي: كافرة أو مؤمنة عاصية، ويكون قوله: لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ راجعاً للأولى، وقوله: أَوْ كَسَبَتْ، راجعاً للثانية، ويكون التقدير: لا ينفع نفساً كافرة لم تكن آمنت من قبل إيمانها الآن، ولا ينفع نفساً من المعاصي، فقوله: أَوْ كَسَبَتْ معطوف على آمَنَتْ ففي الكلام حذف، وعليه فغلق باب التوبة عام في المؤمن العاصي والكافر، وقيل معناها: أو نفساً منافقة كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا، أي: تصديقاً باطناً، وعليه فهو خاص بالكافر. وهل ذلك خاص بالمكلَّف أو عام، وهل يستمر إلى يوم القيامة؟ وهو ظاهر قول البرهان اللقاني في شرح جوهرته: عقرت أمه، هرب، فانفتح له حجر، فدخل في جوفه ثم انطبق عليه الحجر فهو فيه حتى يخرج بإذن الله.
The fifth sign: the rising of the sun from its west. Then there is disagreement about that: is it in one day or in three days? It rises from the east as usual until the Day of Resurrection, and if it rises from the west it sets in the east, and at that the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, and it is said: it is specific to the disbeliever. His saying: (concerning the saying of the Most High: 'On the day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good in its faith') – its apparent meaning is that it is evidence for the second opinion, but it is not so; rather the verse is the source of the disagreement. For it is said: its meaning is that it does not benefit a soul – i.e., a disbelieving soul or a disobedient believing soul – and His saying 'had not believed before' refers to the first, and His saying 'or earned good' refers to the second. And the implied meaning is: it does not benefit a disbelieving soul that had not believed before its present belief, nor does it benefit a soul from its sins. So His saying 'or earned good' is conjoined with 'had believed', so there is ellipsis in the speech, and upon that the closing of the door of repentance is general for the disobedient believer and the disbeliever. And it is said: its meaning is 'or a hypocritical soul that earned good in its faith', i.e., inward attestation, and upon that it is specific to the disbeliever. And is that specific to the morally responsible person or general, and does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? And it is apparent from the saying of al-Burhān al-Laqānī in his commentary on al-Jawhara: 'Its mother was hamstrung, it fled, and a rock opened for it, so it entered into its interior, then the rock closed over it, so it is inside until it emerges by Allah's permission.'
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth major sign: the sun rising from the west. Sawi first notes the disagreement about whether this occurs in one day or three, and then explains that when the sun rises from the west, the door of repentance is closed for both the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, though some say it is only for the disbeliever. He then analyzes the verse from Surah al-An'am (6:158) which is the basis for these opinions. One interpretation takes the verse as general: no soul benefits from faith after the sign, whether it is a disbeliever who had no prior faith or a sinful believer who failed to do good deeds. This makes the closing of repentance universal. The second interpretation restricts the verse to hypocrites, whose faith is only outward, so the closing is specific to disbelievers. Finally, Sawi raises the question of whether the closure applies only to those morally responsible (mukallaf) or to everyone, and whether it continues until the Day of Judgment. He cites al-Laqānī's statement about the she-camel of Salih as evidence for the general view, linking the beast's hiding story to the timing of repentance's closure.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
باب التوبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume repentance is closed only for non-Muslims after the sun rises from the west.
Correction: The passage shows a valid opinion that it also applies to sinful Muslims.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two opinions exist about the closing of repentance after the sun rises from the west?
A) It is closed for everyone or only for believers.
B) It is closed for the disobedient believer and disbeliever, or only for the disbeliever.
C) It is closed for all humans and jinn.
D) It remains open for the repentant until the Day of Judgment.

Key Takeaway
The sun rising from the west is a major sign that marks the closing of the door of repentance for sinners, with a debated scope.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the sun were to rise from the west tomorrow, where would you stand? Are you relying on a future repentance that may never come? What would you do tonight if you knew the door would close before dawn?
?
The scholars debated whether repentance is closed for the disobedient believer or only the disbeliever. If you label yourself a believer but continue in a sin you know is wrong, which side of that debate would you be on? What one sin are you postponing repentance for right now?
?
This sign is one of the major signs of the Hour—are you living as if it could happen at any moment? If your spouse or child saw your actions today, would they see someone who believes the door could close tonight? What will you do differently in the next hour?
