Interpreting the Verse on Repentance's Closure
Sawi analyzes Quran 6:158 and its two interpretations regarding repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations of Quran 6:158 that underlie the debate on whether repentance closure is universal or restricted to disbelievers, and the further questions about its scope.

Core Idea
Two interpretations of the verse yield two different rulings on repentance.

The previous lesson introduced the sign and the two opinions. Now Sawi dives into the Quranic verse that is the source of disagreement. He explains how the same verse can be read to support either a general closure or one limited to disbelievers. He also raises additional questions about whether the closure applies only to the morally responsible and whether it lasts until the Resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and Sawi's commentary
Read the Arabic and translation from 'قوله' to the end. Notice that Sawi says the verse is the source of the disagreement, not evidence for one side.
The verse is from Surah al-An'am (6:158).
2
Analyze the first interpretation (general)
The first interpretation takes 'لا ينفع نفسا إيمانها' to refer to two categories: a disbelieving soul that had not believed before, and a believing soul that had not earned good deeds. This makes the closure general.
This reading requires an ellipsis: 'or a soul that earned good in its faith' is construed differently.
3
Analyze the second interpretation (specific)
The second interpretation sees the verse as referring to a hypocritical soul whose faith was only outward, thus it applies only to disbelievers.
Here 'أو كسبت في إيمانها خيرا' is taken literally: a hypocritical soul that performed good deeds outwardly but had no inner belief.
4
Consider the further questions
Sawi raises two more issues: is the closure specific to the morally responsible (mukallaf)? And does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? He cites al-Laqani's example of the she-camel as evidence for continuity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خامسها : طلوع الشمس من مغربها ثمَّ واختلف في ذلك، هل هو في يوم واحد، أو في ثلاثة أيام، تطلع من المشرق على عادتها إلى يوم القيامة، وإذا طلعت من المغرب غربت في المشرق، وعند ذلك يُغلق باب التوبة على المؤمن العاصي والكافر، وقيل : هو خاص بالكافر. قوله : (لقوله تعالى: يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانَهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا) ظاهره أنه دليل للقول الثاني وليس كذلك، بل الآية منشأ الخلاف، فقيل: إنَّ معناها لا ينفع نفساً؛ أي: كافرة أو مؤمنة عاصية، ويكون قوله: لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ راجعاً للأولى، وقوله: أَوْ كَسَبَتْ، راجعاً للثانية، ويكون التقدير: لا ينفع نفساً كافرة لم تكن آمنت من قبل إيمانها الآن، ولا ينفع نفساً من المعاصي، فقوله: أَوْ كَسَبَتْ معطوف على آمَنَتْ ففي الكلام حذف، وعليه فغلق باب التوبة عام في المؤمن العاصي والكافر، وقيل معناها: أو نفساً منافقة كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا، أي: تصديقاً باطناً، وعليه فهو خاص بالكافر. وهل ذلك خاص بالمكلَّف أو عام، وهل يستمر إلى يوم القيامة؟ وهو ظاهر قول البرهان اللقاني في شرح جوهرته: عقرت أمه، هرب، فانفتح له حجر، فدخل في جوفه ثم انطبق عليه الحجر فهو فيه حتى يخرج بإذن الله.
The fifth sign: the rising of the sun from its west. Then there is disagreement about that: is it in one day or in three days? It rises from the east as usual until the Day of Resurrection, and if it rises from the west it sets in the east, and at that the door of repentance is closed upon the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, and it is said: it is specific to the disbeliever. His saying: (concerning the saying of the Most High: 'On the day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good in its faith') – its apparent meaning is that it is evidence for the second opinion, but it is not so; rather the verse is the source of the disagreement. For it is said: its meaning is that it does not benefit a soul – i.e., a disbelieving soul or a disobedient believing soul – and His saying 'had not believed before' refers to the first, and His saying 'or earned good' refers to the second. And the implied meaning is: it does not benefit a disbelieving soul that had not believed before its present belief, nor does it benefit a soul from its sins. So His saying 'or earned good' is conjoined with 'had believed', so there is ellipsis in the speech, and upon that the closing of the door of repentance is general for the disobedient believer and the disbeliever. And it is said: its meaning is 'or a hypocritical soul that earned good in its faith', i.e., inward attestation, and upon that it is specific to the disbeliever. And is that specific to the morally responsible person or general, and does it continue until the Day of Resurrection? And it is apparent from the saying of al-Burhān al-Laqānī in his commentary on al-Jawhara: 'Its mother was hamstrung, it fled, and a rock opened for it, so it entered into its interior, then the rock closed over it, so it is inside until it emerges by Allah's permission.'
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth major sign: the sun rising from the west. Sawi first notes the disagreement about whether this occurs in one day or three, and then explains that when the sun rises from the west, the door of repentance is closed for both the disobedient believer and the disbeliever, though some say it is only for the disbeliever. He then analyzes the verse from Surah al-An'am (6:158) which is the basis for these opinions. One interpretation takes the verse as general: no soul benefits from faith after the sign, whether it is a disbeliever who had no prior faith or a sinful believer who failed to do good deeds. This makes the closing of repentance universal. The second interpretation restricts the verse to hypocrites, whose faith is only outward, so the closing is specific to disbelievers. Finally, Sawi raises the question of whether the closure applies only to those morally responsible (mukallaf) or to everyone, and whether it continues until the Day of Judgment. He cites al-Laqānī's statement about the she-camel of Salih as evidence for the general view, linking the beast's hiding story to the timing of repentance's closure.

Key Terms
الآية
المكلَّف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the first interpretation (general) understand the phrase 'أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا'?
A) As referring to a hypocritical soul that performed good deeds outwardly.
B) As referring to a believing soul that did not earn good deeds, with an ellipsis.
C) As a separate category of soul that never did any good.
D) As specifying that only disbelievers are affected.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse allows two interpretations, one making repentance closure universal and the other specific to disbelievers, and further questions about its scope remain.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'no soul will benefit from its faith', do you feel a sense of urgency about your own repentance? What specific sin are you holding onto that you assume will be forgiven even if the signs begin? If the door of repentance closed before you could turn back, what would be your state?
?
The second interpretation says that only hypocrites are affected by the closure. But look at your own heart: is your faith ever performative or insincere? Do you sometimes do good deeds for show? The verse warns that such a 'faith' might not benefit when the signs come. What would it take for you to purify your intention right now?
?
Sawi raises the question of whether the closure applies only to the morally responsible. But you are reading this lesson as a responsible adult. How would your life change if you truly believed that any day could bring a sign that closes the door of repentance? What would you stop procrastinating on?

Two Interpretations of the Repentance Closure Verse
Explains two interpretations of Quran 6:158 on repentance closure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main interpretations of Quran 6:158 regarding whether the closure of repentance applies to both believers and disbelievers or only to disbelievers.

Core Idea
The verse on repentance closure is the source of disagreement, not a proof for one side.

The Quranic verse about the coming of a sign (the sun rising from the west) has been understood in two ways. Some scholars see it as applying to both disbelievers and disobedient believers, while others restrict it to disbelievers. This lesson unpacks those interpretations and their implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its literal meaning
Begin by reading the Arabic verse and its translation. Notice how the verse is quoted as the basis for discussion.
2
Identify the first interpretation
The first interpretation says the verse refers to both a disbelieving soul and a disobedient believing soul. Understand the grammatical analysis of 'or earned good' being connected to 'believed'.
This interpretation makes the closure general for all sinners.
3
Identify the second interpretation
The second interpretation restricts the verse to a hypocritical soul (a disbeliever hiding faith). Note how the grammatical connection changes the meaning.
This interpretation limits closure to disbelievers only.
4
Reflect on the disagreement
Consider why both interpretations emerged from the same verse. The passage states the verse is the source of the disagreement, not decisive for either side.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لقوله تعالى: (يَوْمَ يَأْتِي بَعْضُ آيَاتِ رَبِّكَ لَا يَنفَعُ نَفْسًا إِيمَانُهَا لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ قَبْلُ أَوْ كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَانِهَا خَيْرًا) ظاهره أنه دليل للقول الثاني وليس كذلك، بل الآية منشأ الخلاف، فقيل: إنَّ معناها لا ينفع نفساً؛ أي: كافرة أو مؤمنة عاصية، ويكون قوله: لَمْ تَكُنْ آمَنَتْ راجعاً للأولى، وقوله: أَوْ كَسَبَتْ، راجعاً للثانية، ويكون التقدير: لا ينفع نفساً كافرة لم تكن آمنت من قبل إيمانها الآن، ولا ينفع نفساً مؤمنة عاصية كسبت في إيمانها خيراً، فقوله: أَوْ كَسَبَتْ معطوف على آمَنَتْ ففي الكلام حذف، وعليه فغلق باب التوبة عام في المؤمن العاصي والكافر، وقيل معناها: أو نفساً منافقة كَسَبَتْ فِي إِيمَنِها خَيْراً، أي: تصديقاً باطناً، وعليه فهو خاص بالكافر. الحقُّ أنَّ من يوم طلوع الشمس من مغربها إلى يوم القيامة لا تقبل توبة أحد، كما في حديث ابن عمر، لكن صحح الأجهوري في «حاشيته على الرّسالة»: أنَّ عدم قبولها من المؤمن والكافر خاص بمن شاهد الطلوع وهو مميّز، أمَّا غير المميّز لصباً أو جنون، ثم حصل له التَّمييز، أو وُلد بعد ذلك؛ فإنّه تُقبل منه التَّوبة، وقال في شر شرحه على المختصر: (عن ابن عبّاس: لا تُقبل توبة الكافر إلّا إذا كان صغيراً، ثمَّ أسلم بعد ذلك فإنَّها تُقبل منه، وأمّا المؤمن المذنب فتقبل توبته).
For His statement: (The day when some of the signs of your Lord come, no soul will benefit from its faith if it had not believed before or earned good in its faith). Its apparent meaning is that it is evidence for the second opinion, but it is not so; rather, the verse is the source of the disagreement. It was said: its meaning is that it does not benefit any soul—that is, a disbeliever or a disobedient believer—and His statement 'had not believed before' refers to the first, and His statement 'or earned good' refers to the second, and the estimation is: it does not benefit a disbelieving soul that had not believed before [i.e.,] its faith now, nor does it benefit a believing disobedient soul that earned good in its faith. So His statement 'or earned good' is coordinated with 'believed', so there is ellipsis in the speech, and accordingly the closing of the door of repentance is general to the disobedient believer and the disbeliever. And it was said: its meaning is: or a hypocritical soul that earned good in its faith, i.e., inward affirmation, and accordingly it is specific to the disbeliever. The truth is that from the day of the sun rising from its west until the Day of Resurrection, the repentance of no one is accepted, as in the hadith of Ibn Umar. But al-Ajhuri corrected in his 'Hashiyah on al-Risalah' that the non-acceptance of it from the believer and the disbeliever is specific to the one who witnesses the rising while he is discerning. As for the non-discerning—whether due to youth or insanity—then later he obtains discernment, or is born after that, then repentance is accepted from him. And he said in [his] commentary on al-Mukhtasar: (From Ibn Abbas: The repentance of the disbeliever is not accepted unless he was young, then he became Muslim after that, then it is accepted from him. As for the sinful believer, his repentance is accepted.)
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the Quranic verse (6:158) about the closure of repentance after the coming of certain signs, specifically the sun rising from the west. The author begins by noting that the verse is the source of disagreement, not a proof for one side. He explains two interpretations: the first makes the verse general—meaning it applies to both the disbelieving soul and the disobedient believing soul, so the door of repentance closes for everyone (believer and disbeliever). The second interpretation restricts the verse to the hypocrite, meaning it only applies to the disbeliever. The author then states the correct view: from the moment the sun rises from the west until the Day of Resurrection, no one's repentance is accepted, based on a hadith. However, he cites al-Ajhuri's correction that this non-acceptance only applies to those who witness the sign while they are discerning (mumayyiz). Those who are not discerning—children, the insane—who later become discerning, or those born after the sign, their repentance is accepted. He also quotes Ibn Abbas that a disbeliever's repentance is not accepted unless he was a child before the sign and then becomes Muslim after, while a sinful believer's repentance is always accepted. The passage thus clarifies the nuanced ruling on repentance after this major sign.

Key Terms
باب التوبة
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
آية الأنعام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse clearly supports that repentance closure is only for disbelievers.
Correction: The verse is the source of disagreement, and the apparent meaning is not decisive for either side; both interpretations have merit.

Checkpoint
According to the first interpretation presented, the verse applies to which groups?
A) Only disbelievers
B) Only disobedient believers
C) Both disbelievers and disobedient believers
D) Only hypocrites

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse on the sign is open to two interpretations, one general and one specific, and it is the source of scholarly disagreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the first interpretation—that repentance is closed even for the disobedient believer—what does that do to the way you view your own sins? Are you treating repentance casually, assuming you can always delay it?
?
The second interpretation reserves closure for hypocrites. If you were to honestly examine your heart right now, are there areas where your faith is merely outward? What would it cost you to make it genuine?
?
Both interpretations agree that a day will come when faith no longer benefits. If you knew that tomorrow was that day, what would you change today? What is stopping you from making that change now?

The Correct View and Exceptions for Repentance After the Sign
States the correct view and exceptions to the closure of repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct position that repentance is closed for those who witness the sign while discerning, and the exceptions for non-discerning individuals and those born after.

Core Idea
Repentance is closed only for discerning witnesses; others may still repent.

After presenting the interpretations, the author states the truth (al-haqq) based on a hadith, but then introduces a crucial correction by al-Ajhuri that limits the closure. This lesson examines the correct ruling and the exceptions for children, the insane, and those born after the sign.

Guided Path
1
Read the truth statement
Read the Arabic from 'الحقُّ' to the end. Note the hadith of Ibn Umar as evidence.
The truth is that from the day of rising until Resurrection, no repentance is accepted.
2
Examine al-Ajhuri's correction
Al-Ajhuri restricts non-acceptance to those who witness the sign while being discerning (mumayyiz). Understand the exception for non-discerning people and those born after.
Non-discerning includes children and the insane.
3
Consider Ibn Abbas's quote
The quote says a disbeliever's repentance is accepted if he was a child before the sign and becomes Muslim after. A sinful believer's repentance is always accepted.
This seems to imply that believers are not affected by the sign closure.
4
Synthesize the overall ruling
Combine the hadith, al-Ajhuri's correction, and Ibn Abbas's statement to understand the full picture of repentance after the sign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Reflect on the urgency of sincere repentance: are you relying on future repentance while continuing in sin? What is one sin you need to repent from right now?
?
Imagine you were born after the sign—would you immediately turn to Allah? Or would you be like many who ignore? Examine your current state: are you truly repentant, or are you just assuming you have time? What concrete step will you take today to ensure your repentance is accepted?

Events After the Sun Rises from the West
Describes the 120-year period after the sign with two phases: believers' enjoyment then disbelievers' corruption.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the 120-year period after the sun rises from the west, including the believers' temporary enjoyment, their death, and the moral decay of disbelievers before the Hour.

Core Idea
The 120-year period after the sign ends with the worst people.

This lesson covers the specific timeline and events that occur after the major sign of the sun rising from the west. The text narrates a detailed sequence: believers enjoy fulfillment for 40 years, then death removes them, and disbelievers sink into open fornication until only illegitimate children remain as the worst of people when the Hour begins. Understanding this sequence clarifies the final state of humanity before the Day of Judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage Carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the narrative flow and its details sink in.
The passage is a continuous description, not an argument.
2
Identify the Timeline Structure
The passage outlines a 120-year period divided into phases: 40 years for believers, then death of believers, then disbelievers' fornication, then 30 years of barrenness. Notice the sequence.
The phases are: 1) believers' enjoyment (40 years), 2) believers die, 3) disbelievers fornicate openly, 4) God makes women barren (30 years), leading to children of fornication.
3
Note the Specific Details
Pay attention to the extreme moral decay: intercourse in streets, best person merely suggests moving aside, no legitimate births. Reflect on how this contrasts with the believers' earlier state.
The description emphasizes shamelessness and the absence of lawful marriage.
4
Reflect on the Purpose
Consider why this detailed description is given. It highlights the degradation of humanity after the righteous are gone and serves as a sign of the nearness of the Hour.
The Hour will arise upon the worst of people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (الحقُّ أنَّه من يوم طلوع الشَّمس من مغـربـهـا إلـى يـوم القيامة . . . إلخ): ورد أنَّه مئة وعشرون سنة، فيتمتّع المؤمنون فيها أربعون سنة لا يتمتُّون شيئاً إلَّا أعطوه، ثمَّ يعود فيهم الموت ويسرع فلا يبقى مؤمن، ويبقى الكفَّار يتهارجون في الطرق كالبهائم، حتّى ينكح الرَّجل المرأة في وسط الطريق يقوم واحد عنها وينزل واحد، وأفضلهم من يقول: لو تنحيتم عن الطَّريق لكان أحسن فيكونون على مثل ذلك حتّى لا يولد لأحد من نكاح، ثمَّ يعقم الله النِّساء ثلاثين سنة، ويكون كلُّهم أولاد زنا عند الساعة شرار الناس عليهم تقوم.
His statement: (The truth is that from the day of the sun rising from its west to the Day of Resurrection... etc.): It is narrated that it is one hundred and twenty years. The believers will enjoy therein forty years—they will not wish for anything but they will be given it. Then death will return among them and become swift, so that no believer remains. And the disbelievers will remain, fornicating in the roads like beasts, until a man will have intercourse with a woman in the middle of the road—one gets up from her and another gets down. The best among them is the one who says: 'If you would move aside from the road, that would be better.' They will be in such a state until no child is born from any intercourse. Then God will make women barren for thirty years, and all of them will be children of fornication at the Hour—the worst of people, upon whom the Hour will arise.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is an eschatological description of the period following the sun's rising from the west. The author comments on the phrase stating that from that sign to the Day of Judgment is a period of 120 years. He narrates specific events: first, believers will enjoy 40 years of perfect fulfillment of desires; then death will become rampant among them, eliminating all believers. After that, disbelievers—who are left—will engage in open and shameless fornication in the streets, to the point that no legitimate offspring are born. The best among them is merely the one who suggests moving aside from the road. Then God will make women barren for 30 years, so that all children born are illegitimate (children of fornication). These are described as the worst people, and upon them the Hour will come. The passage emphasizes the moral decay and the end of righteous lineage as a sign of the Last Day.

أولاد زنا
الساعة
شرار الناس

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the period after the sun rises from the west is short or uneventful.
Correction: The text specifies it is 120 years with distinct phases: 40 years of believers' enjoyment, then rapid death of believers, then rampant fornication among disbelievers, and 30 years of barrenness, culminating in children of fornication who are the worst people at the Hour.

?
The best among the disbelievers is merely the one who suggests moving aside from the road. In your own life, are you settling for 'better than nothing' instead of striving for excellence in obedience to Allah? What is one step you can take today to raise your standard?

The Ruling on Repentance After the Sun Rising from the West
Al-Sawi clarifies the ruling on repentance after the sun rising from the west.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nuanced ruling on repentance after the sun rises from the west, including the distinction between discerning and non-discerning individuals.

Core Idea
Repentance after the sign is only closed for those who witness it with discernment.

The sun rising from the west is a major sign of the Hour that signals the closure of the door of repentance. However, scholars have specified that this applies only to those who are discerning (mumayyiz) at the time. Al-Sawi presents the correct view and an important correction from al-Ajhouri that exempts children and the insane, among others.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through.
2
Identify the general rule
Note the statement that repentance is not accepted after the sun rises from the west.
This is the starting point before the correction.
3
Understand the correction
Al-Ajhouri specifies that non-acceptance is for those who witness while discerning (mumayyiz). Who is excluded?
The non-discerning (due to youth or insanity) and those born after.
4
Reflect on the Ibn Abbas quote
Consider how the repentance of a young disbeliever and a sinful believer is accepted.
This reinforces the exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علامات يوم القيامة
الحقُّ أنَّ من يوم طلوع الشمس من مغربها إلى يوم القيامة لا تقبل توبة أحد، كما في حديث ابن عمر (۱) ، لكن صحح الأجهوري في «حاشيته على الرّسالة» : أنَّ عدم قبولها من المؤمن والكافر خاص بمن شاهد الطلوع وهو مميّز ، أمَّا غير المميّز لصباً أو جنون، ثم حصل له التَّمييز ، أو وُلد بعد ذلك ؛ فإنّه تُقبل منه التَّوبة، وقال في شر شرحه على المختصر : ( عن ابن عبّاس : لا تُقبل توبة الكافر إلّا إذا كان صغيراً، ثمَّ أسلم بعد ذلك فإنَّها تُقبل منه، وأمّا المؤمن المذنب فتقبل توبته» ) .
قوله : (الحقُّ أنَّه من يوم طلوع الشَّمس من مغـربـهـا إلـى يـوم القيامة . . . إلخ) : ورد أنَّه مئة وعشرون سنة، فيتمتّع المؤمنون فيها أربعون سنة لا يتمتُّون شيئاً إلَّا أعطوه، ثمَّ يعود فيهم الموت ويسرع فلا يبقى مؤمن، ويبقى الكفَّار يتهارجون في الطرق كالبهائم، حتّى ينكح الرَّجل المرأة في وسط الطريق يقوم واحد عنها وينزل واحد، وأفضلهم من يقول: لو تنحيتم عن الطَّريق لكان أحسن فيكونون على مثل ذلك حتّى لا يولد لأحد من نكاح، ثمَّ يعقم الله النِّساء ثلاثين سنة، ويكون كلُّهم أولاد زنا الساعة (٢) شرار الناس عليهم تقوم
قوله : (وأما المؤمن المذنب . . . إلخ) : هذا هو المعتمد .
Signs of the Day of Judgment. The correct view is that from the day the sun rises from its west until the Day of Judgment, no repentance is accepted from anyone, as in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar (1). However, al-Ajhouri corrected in his gloss on al-Risala that the non-acceptance of repentance from the believer and the disbeliever is specific to the one who witnesses the rising while being discerning. As for the non-discerning, whether due to youth or insanity, then later becomes discerning, or is born after that, then repentance is accepted from him. And he said in the explanation of his commentary on al-Mukhtasar: (From Ibn 'Abbas: The repentance of the disbeliever is not accepted unless he was young, then he becomes Muslim after that, then it is accepted from him. As for the sinful believer, his repentance is accepted.) His statement: (The correct view is that from the day the sun rises from its west until the Day of Judgment... etc.): It has been reported that it is one hundred and twenty years. The believers will enjoy forty years in which they will not desire anything except they are given it, then death returns among them and spreads quickly so no believer remains. And the disbelievers remain mating in the streets like beasts, until a man has intercourse with a woman in the middle of the road; one rises from her and another goes down, and the best of them is the one who says: 'If you would move away from the road, it would be better.' They will continue like that until no one is born from intercourse. Then Allah will make women barren for thirty years, and all of them will be children of fornication at the Hour (2), the worst of people upon whom the Hour will be established. His statement: (As for the sinful believer... etc.): This is the relied-upon view.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the major sign of the sun rising from the west and its impact on repentance. The author begins by stating the correct view that after the sun rises from the west, repentance is not accepted, citing a hadith from Ibn Umar. Then he notes a correction by al-Ajhouri specifying that the non-acceptance applies only to those who witness the sign while being discerning (mumayyiz). Those who are not discerning due to youth or insanity and later become discerning, or those born after, can have their repentance accepted. The author then elaborates on the narration about the duration of events after this sign: 120 years, including 40 years of enjoyment for believers, then death of believers, then moral decay among disbelievers, then barrenness, and finally the worst people at the Hour. He concludes by affirming the relied-upon view regarding the sinful believer's repentance.

Key Terms
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
توبة
مميّز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: After the sun rises from the west, no one's repentance is accepted under any circumstances.
Correction: The non-acceptance applies only to those who witness the sign while being discerning. Children, the insane, and those born after can have their repentance accepted.

Checkpoint

B) Only disbelievers
C) Those who witness the rising while being discerning
D) Only sinners

Key Takeaway
The door of repentance after the sun rises from the west is only closed for those who are discerning at the time of the sign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to see the sun rising from the west today, would your repentance be accepted? What does your answer reveal about your current state of discernment and accountability before Allah?
?
Are there truths about the Hereafter that you witness daily but fail to discern deeply? How does that negligence affect your readiness for the final hour?
?
What would it mean for you to lose the opportunity of repentance because you witnessed the truth but were not truly discerning? What steps will you take today to ensure you are among those who respond to Allah's signs with full awareness?

The Events Following the Sign: Duration and Description
Al-Sawi describes the events and duration after the sun rising from the west.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narrated events that occur after the sun rises from the west, including the duration of 120 years and the moral decay before the Hour.

Core Idea
After the sun rises from the west, the world experiences 120 years of gradual decline until the Hour.

After establishing the ruling on repentance, al-Sawi elaborates on what happens after this major sign. He narrates a tradition that describes a 120-year period, including 40 years of enjoyment for believers, then the death of believers, followed by moral decay among disbelievers, and finally the worst people.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the timeline.
2
Identify the three phases
Note the phases: 40 years of believers' enjoyment, death of believers, then disbelievers' decay.
3
Understand the moral decay description
Reflect on the graphic description of public fornication and the absence of shame.
This highlights the severity of the end times.
4
Note the barrenness and worst people
After 30 years of barrenness, only children of fornication are born, who are the worst.
This leads to the establishment of the Hour.

Virtue of 'La ilaha illa Allah' in Hadith
The author lists five hadiths on the virtue of the shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the immense virtue of the declaration 'La ilaha illa Allah' as attested by multiple authentic hadiths.

Core Idea
The sincere utterance of the shahada is the key to Paradise and salvation.

This lesson presents a collection of hadiths from the text that highlight the unparalleled merit of saying 'La ilaha illa Allah.' These narrations emphasize that this simple phrase, when uttered with sincerity, guarantees entrance to Paradise, opens the gates of heaven, and is the best of deeds. Understanding this virtue motivates the believer to increase its recitation.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths
Read each of the five hadiths carefully. Notice the different rewards promised for saying 'La ilaha illa Allah'.
2
Identify key rewards
List the specific rewards mentioned: protection from Hell, renewal of faith, key to heavens, best deed on Judgment Day, and opening of heaven's doors.
The last hadith conditions the reward on avoiding major sins.
3
Reflect on sincerity
Notice that many hadiths mention sincerity (ikhlāṣ) as a condition for the reward. This shows the importance of inner faith.
4
Connect to action
Understand that these hadiths provide the basis for the command to increase recitation, which will be discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها : «إنَّ الله قد حرَّم على النَّار من قال : (لا إله إلا الله يبتغي بذلك وجه الله) (1)
ومنها : جددوا إيمانكم ، قيل : يا رسول الله ؛ وكيف نجدد إيماننا ؟ قال : أكثروا من قول : (لا إله إلا الله) (2)
ومنها: «لكلِّ شيءٍ مفتاح، ومفتاح السَّماوات قول: (لا إله إِلَّا الله) (3) .
ومنها : «ليس من عبد يقول : (لا إله إلَّا الله مئة مرة إلا بعثه الله تعالى يوم القيامة ووجهه كالقمر ليلةَ البدرِ ، ولم يرفع لأحدٍ يومئذ عمل أفضل من عمله إلا من قال مثل قوله أو زاد) (4) .
ومنها : «ما قال عبد : (لا إله إلا الله) قط مخلصاً إِلَّا فُتحت له أبواب السَّماء حتَّى تُفضي إلى العرش ما اجتنبت الكبائر» (5)
إذا علمت ذلك (فأكثرن) - بنون التوكيد الخفيفة - من ذكرها أي: كلمة الإسلام بالأدب أي مع الآداب التي ذكرها القوم .
ومنها : من قال : (لا إله إلا الله مخلصاً دخل الجنة) (1).
ومنها : «لا إله إلا الله لا يسبقها عمل، ولا تترك ذنباً» (2)، وغير ذلك من الأحاديث التي لا تحصى كثرة .
قوله : (إذا علمت ذلك ... إلخ) : أشار بذلك إلى أنَّ الفاء في قوله : (فأكثرن) للفصيحة أفصحت عن جواب شرط مقدَّر .
And among them: 'Verily Allah has forbidden the Fire to one who says: La ilaha illa Allah seeking thereby the face of Allah' (1). And among them: 'Renew your faith.' It was said: O Messenger of Allah, how do we renew our faith? He said: 'Increase in saying: La ilaha illa Allah' (2). And among them: 'For everything there is a key, and the key to the heavens is the saying: La ilaha illa Allah' (3). And among them: 'There is no servant who says: La ilaha illa Allah one hundred times except that Allah will resurrect him on the Day of Resurrection with his face like the full moon, and no deed will be raised for anyone on that day better than his deed except for one who said the like of his saying or added more' (4). And among them: 'No servant says: La ilaha illa Allah sincerely except that the doors of heaven are opened for him until they reach the Throne, so long as he avoids major sins' (5). If you know that, then increase (fa'akthirun) - with the light nun of emphasis - your mention of it, meaning the word of Islam with adab, i.e., with the etiquettes mentioned by the people. And among them: 'Whoever says: La ilaha illa Allah sincerely will enter Paradise' (1). And among them: 'La ilaha illa Allah: no deed precedes it, and it leaves no sin' (2), and other such hadiths that are too numerous to count. His saying: 'If you know that ... etc.': he indicated by that that the fa in his saying 'fa'akthirun' is the fa of eloquence, revealing the answer to a suppressed conditional.
Source pages p. 399

Commentary
This passage presents a series of hadiths proving the immense virtue of the declaration "La ilaha illa Allah", followed by an exhortation to recite it frequently and a grammatical comment on the word "fa'akthirun" (so increase) from the original text. The hadiths show that the sincere utterance of the shahada guarantees salvation, opens the gates of heaven, is the key to paradise, and is the best deed. The author then says: 'If you know that, then increase (fa'akthirun) your mention of it (i.e., the word of Islam) with adab (proper conduct) as mentioned by the scholars.' He then adds two more hadiths. Finally, he comments on the phrase 'fa'akthirun': the fa (fā') is the 'fa of eloquence' (fā' al-faṣīḥa), which reveals the answer to a suppressed conditional (jawāb shart muqaddar). This is a grammatical point: the command to increase is implicitly conditioned on the preceding knowledge. The author explains that the fa is not simply a conjunction but indicates that the command is the apodosis of a conditional clause that is not explicitly stated, e.g., 'If you know that, then increase it.' This highlights the importance of understanding the virtue before acting.

Key Terms
لا إله إلا الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can say the shahada and then commit major sins without any consequence.
Correction: The fifth hadith specifies that the doors are opened 'so long as he avoids major sins', indicating that major sins can prevent the full benefit of the shahada.

Checkpoint
According to the hadiths in this passage, what condition is mentioned for the opening of the doors of heaven?
A) Saying it 100 times
B) Avoiding major sins
C) Saying it in congregation
D) Reciting it at dawn

Key Takeaway
The hadiths establish that the sincere utterance of 'La ilaha illa Allah' is a deed of immense merit, with multiple specific rewards, and it should be recited frequently.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'La ilaha illa Allah,' do you seek His face alone, or are you distracted by hopes of worldly gain or praise? How can you purify your intention starting today?
?
The Prophet commanded us to renew our faith by increasing this dhikr. How many times did you say it today? What practical step will you take to multiply your recitation this week?
?
The fifth hadith warns that the doors of heaven open only if you avoid major sins. Is there a major sin you are clinging to that shuts those doors? Will you repent from it now and never return?

Commentary on 'Fa'akthirun' and Further Hadiths
The author commands increasing recitation of the shahada with adab and explains the grammatical function of 'fa' in 'fa'akthirun'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the grammatical nuance of the command 'fa'akthirun' and its connection to the preceding virtues.

Core Idea
The command to increase recitation is contingent on understanding the virtue, and the 'fa' reveals a suppressed condition.

After presenting the hadiths on the virtue of the shahada, the author exhorts the reader to increase their recitation. This lesson dissects the phrase 'fa'akthirun' and explains the grammatical concept of the 'fa of eloquence' (fā' al-faṣīḥa), which indicates that the command is the answer to a suppressed conditional. It also includes additional hadiths reinforcing the virtue.

Guided Path
1
Read the exhortation

2
Identify the grammatical note
The author explains the 'fa' in 'fa'akthirun' as the 'fa of eloquence'. Understand what this grammatical term implies.
The 'fa of eloquence' reveals the answer to a suppressed conditional sentence.
3
Consider the added hadiths
Two more hadiths are included: one promising Paradise for sincere utterance, and another stating no deed precedes it and it leaves no sin.
4
Reflect on the connection
The command to increase is based on the knowledge of the virtue. Reflect on how this understanding should motivate action.

Two Journeys and the Seven Souls
Classification of spiritual wayfaring and seven souls

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between the spiritual journey of prophets and non-prophets, and how the seven types of souls are different descriptions of a single reality.

Core Idea
The prophetic journey begins where others end; all souls are one, only descriptions differ.

This passage from al-Sawi's commentary distinguishes the spiritual journeys of prophets and non-prophets, then introduces the famous classification of seven souls. It emphasizes that the quality of one's beginning determines the illumination of one's end, and that the seven souls are not separate entities but different states of the same soul. Understanding this helps clarify how spiritual transformation unfolds for different types of people.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning. Note the structure: first the prophetic journey, then non-prophetic, then the seven souls.
Pay attention to the terms 'tashkik' and 'mujahada' – they are key to understanding the gradation of wayfaring.
2
Identify the two journeys
Locate the description of the prophetic journey (mabda'uhu al-taraqqi min nufus mutahhara) and the non-prophetic journey (min nufus ammara aw lawwama). Notice the contrast in starting points.
The prophetic journey begins from perfection; the non-prophetic from deficiency.
3
Grasp the principle of beginnings and ends
Find the sentence 'al-nihayat takhtalif fi al-ishraq bihasb ikhtilaf al-bidayat'. Understand that the illumination of the end depends on the 'burning' (mujahada) of the beginning.
This principle connects spiritual effort to outcome.
4
Understand the seven souls
Read the last part: the souls are seven by description but one in essence. Reflect on how this classification is used in the Khalwati order.
The seven souls are not separate entities; they are stages or aspects of the same soul.

Source Text

فسلوك الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام مبدؤه الترقي من نفوس مطهرة كمالية إلى ما لا نهاية له من المقامات الإحسانية، وهو في نفسه متفاوت، فسلوك أولي العزم منهم أعلى وأجل من سلوك غيرهم، وسلوك سيد أولي العزم عليه وعليهم أفضل الصلاة والسلام أعلى من غيره، إذ مبدؤه نهاية غيره.

The wayfaring of the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, its beginning is the ascension from purified, perfect souls to endless degrees of Ihsani stations, and it is in itself differentiated. So the wayfaring of the Messengers of firm resolve (ulu al-azm) among them is higher and more sublime than the wayfaring of others, and the wayfaring of the master of the Messengers of firm resolve, may the best peace and blessings be upon him and them, is higher than others, since its beginning is the end of others. As for the wayfaring of others: it is from commanding (ammara) or blameworthy (lawwama) dark souls to a complete, truthful (siddiqiyya) soul. And the ends differ in illumination according to the difference of the beginnings, so by burning the beginning, the illumination of the end occurs. Explanation of the seven types of souls: And the souls are seven according to their descriptions, otherwise they are one. His saying: 'and it is in itself differentiated' meaning: wayfaring is said by analogy (bi al-tashkik). His saying: 'the end of others' i.e., from the Messengers of firm resolve. His saying: 'and the ends differ… etc.' i.e., the ends of those other than the prophets, peace be upon them. His saying: 'so by burning the beginning' i.e., by striving (mujahada) with remembrance (dhikr) and reflection (fikr). And his saying: 'the illumination of the end occurs' i.e., through the sciences, gnostic knowledge, and secrets. His saying: 'and the souls are seven' i.e., according to the masters of the Khalwati order, and according to the masters…
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage is a classification of spiritual wayfaring and an explanation of the seven souls. It begins by describing the wayfaring of prophets: their starting point is already purified, perfect souls, and they ascend to infinite stations of ihsan (spiritual excellence). This wayfaring is itself graded (mutafawit) – the journey of the Messengers of firm resolve (ulu al-azm) is higher than that of other prophets, and the journey of the Prophet Muhammad (sayyid ulu al-azm) is the highest of all because his starting point is the end of others. Then it describes the wayfaring of non-prophets: they begin from commanding (ammara) or blameworthy (lawwama) dark souls and aim for a complete, truthful (siddiqiyya) soul. A key principle follows: the ends differ in illumination according to the beginnings; by 'burning' (i.e., through strenuous effort, mujahada) of the beginning, the illumination of the end is achieved. The author then announces an explanation of the seven types of souls, noting that souls are seven in description but one in essence. The remaining lines are commentary notes: 'his saying: and it is in itself differentiated' means that wayfaring (suluk) is used in an analogical sense (tashkik). 'His saying: the end of others' refers to the other ulu al-azm. 'His saying: and the ends differ…' refers to the ends of non-prophets. 'His saying: so by burning the beginning' means through striving using dhikr and fikr. 'His saying: the illumination of the end' means through sciences, gnosis, and secrets. 'His saying: and the souls are seven' specifies that this classification is according to the Khalwati order. The passage thus compares prophetic and non-prophetic journeys, introduces the seven souls, and clarifies key terms.

Misconception: The seven souls are seven different entities or distinct souls.
Correction: The passage explicitly says they are one in essence, differing only in description.

Key Takeaway
The spiritual journey's quality depends on its starting point, and the seven souls are one reality seen through different descriptions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your spiritual journey began somewhere. If you are honest with yourself, is your starting point closer to the 'dark souls' of ammara and lawwama, or have you already tasted purification? What will you do today to 'burn' that beginning through dhikr and reflection so that your end may be illuminated?

The Prophet's beginning was the end of others. Do you ever compare your spiritual progress to those around you, forgetting that your starting point and capacity are unique? Will you stop measuring yourself against others and instead focus on transforming your own soul from its current description to a higher one?
?
The seven souls are one in essence, yet they differ in description. Which description best fits your soul right now—are you commanding, blaming, inspired, or at peace? What one concrete step will you take this week to move toward a more complete and truthful soul (siddiqiyya)?

Definition of Repentance (Tawba) and Its Stages
Definition of the first foundation of the path: repentance, its linguistic and technical meaning, and its stages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and technical definition of repentance (tawba) in Islamic spirituality, as well as the hierarchical stages of repentance from major sins to subtle self-regard.

Core Idea
Repentance is not just leaving sin; it is a journey from sin to selflessness.

This lesson explores the first foundation of the spiritual path: repentance. While commonly understood as turning away from sin, the author presents a deeper, multi-layered view where repentance begins with major sins and eventually includes purifying the heart from even the satisfaction of one's own good deeds. Let us read the passage to discover the full scope of tawba.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without stopping. Note the poem commentary at the beginning, then the definition of tawba, then the list of stages.
The poem line is from an earlier context; focus on the definition and stages.
2
Understand the linguistic and technical definitions
The passage gives two definitions: linguistic (absolute return) and technical (return from blameworthy to praiseworthy in Sharia). How do these differ?
The technical definition specifies the criterion: Sharia.
3
Trace the hierarchy of repentance stages
List the stages in order: from major sins, minor sins, disliked acts, abandoning better, seeing good deeds, seeing oneself as among the poor, seeing one's own truthfulness, and finally any thought not pleasing to God.
Notice the progression from outward actions to inward states.
4
Reflect on the deeper meaning
The last stages involve purifying one's self-perception. Why is 'seeing one's good deeds' considered something to repent from?
This guards against spiritual pride.

The foundations of the path leading to God are ten: first: repentance. The first: repentance from every sin. His saying: 'So it returned' meaning: it became restful for me. And his saying: 'And whatever I load upon it' meaning: from hardships whose easier part is easier than death. And his saying: 'It bore from me' meaning: it took it with acceptance, openness, and satisfaction because of its intimacy with the Truth and its rejection of creation. His saying: 'And its foundations are ten' meaning: the foundations of the path of the brave among the people of love and longing, and it has been mentioned that six of them are specific to them, and four are general. Commentary
This passage defines the first foundation of the spiritual path: repentance (tawba). The author begins by quoting a poem line 'So it returned' meaning the soul became restful. He then explains that the foundations of the path are ten, six specific to the elite and four general. He gives the linguistic definition of repentance as return, and the technical definition as turning from blameworthy to praiseworthy in the Sharia. Repentance has a beginning and an end. The beginning is a hierarchical progression: first from major sins, then minor sins, then disliked acts, then from abandoning what is better, then from seeing one's own good deeds (as a point of pride), then from seeing oneself as among the poor (spiritual elite), then from being satisfied with one's own truthfulness in repentance, and finally from any thought that is not for the pleasure of God. This reflects a deep spiritual psychology where repentance is not merely giving up sins but purifying the heart from all self-regard.

?

?

Are you willing to admit that your repentance itself may be tainted and still needs forgiveness? How would you feel if Allah accepted your repentance but you never felt pleased with it?

The Seventh Foundation: Seclusion
Sawi defines seclusion and supports it with hadith and sayings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of seclusion in the spiritual path, its permissible exceptions, its benefits for the heart, and the scriptural foundations supporting it.

Core Idea
Seclusion protects the heart from darkness and preserves one's religion.

Sawi presents the seventh foundation of the spiritual journey: seclusion from people. He clarifies that while seclusion is essential for heart purification, it does not mean complete isolation; contact with one’s spiritual guide and necessary interactions remain permitted. The passage then provides prophetic hadith and wise sayings that underscore the value of seclusion for safeguarding one’s faith and inner peace.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the full meaning before analysis.
2
Identify the definition and exceptions
Notice how Sawi defines seclusion and lists the three exceptions: the shaykh, a righteous brother, and necessity.
3
Understand the reason for seclusion
Reflect on why mixing with people darkens the heart, even if free from sin, and how seclusion benefits the heart.
4
Study the supporting proofs
Go through each proof: the hadith about the best people, the saying of some, the wisdom of al-Sakandari, the hadith about fleeing with religion, and the poem.
Notice the variety: direct hadith, sayings of the pious, and poetry.
5
Apply the lesson
Consider how seclusion can be practiced today while maintaining necessary contacts and avoiding extremes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سابعاً : العزلة عن النَّاس قاطبةً إلا عن شيخه المربّي له، أو أخ صالح يعينه على الطَّاعة والهمة، وإلا لضرورة بيع أو شراء، إذ مخالط ة النّاس تُكسب القلب ظلمة، لو فرض أنّها تخلو عن ارتكاب المحرَّمات، فكيف ولا يخلو مجلس عنها من غيبة ونميمة وغيرها. قوله : (العزلة عن النَّاس قاطبة) أي لما فيها من خيري الدنيا والآخرة؛ لما ورد أنَّ رجلاً قال : يا رسول الله ؛ أيُّ النَّاس أفضل ؟ قال : رجل يجاهد بنفسه وماله في سبيل الله ، قال : ثم من؟ قال : «رجل يعتزل في شعب من الشعاب يعبد ربه». وقال بعضهم : ( من أراد أن يسلم له دينه، وأن يستريح بدنه، ويقل غمه ؛ فليعتزل النَّاس). وقال السَّكندري في حكمه : (ما نفع القلب مثل عزلة يدخل بها میدان فكرة). وفي الحديث : ليأتين على النَّاس زمان لا يسلم لذي دين دينه إلَّا من فرَّ بدينه من قرية إلى قرية ومن شاهق إلى شاهق، ومن جحر إلى جحر كالثعلب الذي يزوغ. ولبعضهم : لقاء النّاس ليس يُفيد شيئا سوى الهَدِّيانِ من قبل وقال فاقلِلْ من لقاء النّاسِ إلّا لألحل العلم أو إصلاح حال
Seventh: Seclusion from all people except from his shaykh who trains him, or a righteous brother who helps him in obedience and resolve, and except for necessity of selling or buying, since mixing with people earns the heart darkness, even if it were supposed that it is free from committing prohibitions, so how [can it be] when no gathering is free from backbiting and gossip and other things? His saying: (Seclusion from all people) i.e. for what it contains of the goods of this world and the Hereafter; for it was reported that a man said: O Messenger of Allah, which people are best? He said: A man who struggles with his self and his wealth in the way of Allah. He said: Then who? He said: 'A man who secludes himself in a mountain pass and worships his Lord.' And some said: 'Whoever wants his religion to be safe, his body to rest, and his grief to lessen, let him seclude himself from people.' And al-Sakandari said in his aphorisms: 'Nothing benefits the heart like seclusion by which it enters the field of reflection.' And in the hadith: There will come upon people a time when no one with religion will have his religion safe except one who flees with his religion from village to village and from peak to peak and from hole to hole like a fox that dodges. And some said: Meeting people does not benefit anything except exchanging greetings and talk, so reduce meeting people except for the sake of knowledge or reforming one's state.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage defines the seventh foundation of the spiritual path: seclusion. The author begins by stating that seclusion is to be from all people except one's spiritual master, a righteous companion who aids in obedience, or necessity of trade. The reason is that mixing with people darkens the heart, even if free from sin—yet gatherings are rarely free from backbiting and gossip. He then supports this with proofs: the hadith where the best is the mujahid, then the one who secludes to worship; a saying that seclusion preserves religion, body, and lessens grief; al-Sakandari's wisdom that nothing benefits like seclusion for reflection; a hadith about fleeing with one's religion like a fox; and a poem criticizing socializing except for knowledge or reform.

Key Terms
العزلة
الشيخ المربي
القلب
الظلمة
الغيبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seclusion means cutting off all contact with everyone, including one's spiritual guide and essential worldly needs.
Correction: As Sawi clarifies, seclusion permits exceptions for one's shaykh, a righteous brother, and necessary transactions like buying and selling.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary benefit of seclusion?
A) Earning more wealth
B) Protecting the heart from darkness and preserving religion
C) Avoiding all social contact permanently
D) Gaining fame among scholars

Key Takeaway
Seclusion, when practiced with proper exceptions, protects the heart from spiritual darkness and is strongly supported by prophetic guidance and saintly wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How much of your daily conversation is free from backbiting or gossip? Are you willing to seclude yourself to protect your heart even if it means losing social approval?
?
The hadith speaks of fleeing with your religion like a fox from hole to hole. What 'holes' are you currently fleeing to, or are you staying in places that weaken your faith?
?
Al-Sakandari says nothing benefits the heart like seclusion entering the field of reflection. When did you last truly reflect in seclusion? What excuses prevent you from doing so this week?

The Ruling of Du'a: What Makes It Invalid
Al-Sawi enumerates three types of impossibility that invalidate du'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of impossibility that render a du'a invalid according to Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Du'a is invalid if it asks for something impossible by reason, law, or custom.

Du'a is a powerful act of worship, but not every request is permissible. Al-Sawi begins by clarifying the boundaries: du'a is generally valid unless it involves something that is impossible by reason, by divine law, or by normal custom. In this lesson, we will explore each category with examples from the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the ruling of du'a
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the three conditions for invalidity.
2
Understand 'impossible by reason'
The author gives the example of combining two opposites. This is logically impossible.
This category covers anything that contradicts rationality.
3
Understand 'impossible by sacred law'
Asking for something prohibited by Sharia, like wine, is invalid.
This category covers anything that contradicts divine commands.
4
Understand 'impossible by custom'
Asking for something contrary to normal, habitual occurrences, like ascending to the sky without a cause.
This is about physical impossibility under normal circumstances.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم الدعاء يكون بممتنع عقلاً، أو شرعاً، أو عادة. وينبغي أن يكون مصاحباً للذُّلّ والانكسار، وأن يكون في الأوقات الشَّريفة كالأسحار وعقب الصلوات . وألا يكون فيه تحجير على الله تعالى كأن يسأل قضاء حاجة بخصوصها في هذا الوقت بعينه مثلاً ، ما لم يشتد الكرب؛ كالخلاص من ظالم مثلاً . ثمَّ إِنَّ الدُّعاء في ذاته هو مخ العبادة؛ لأنَّ فيه إظهار الفقر والفاقة إلى الله تعالى، وإنَّ الله هو الغنيُّ القادر على كل شيء، وإن لم تحصل استجابة . وعدم حصول الإجابة إما لتخلُّف شرط، وإما لعلم الله أنَّ عدم الإجابة خير . ثم: قوله : (بممتنع عقلاً) : أي : كالجمع بين الصِّدِّين. وقوله : (أو شرعاً) : أي : كالدُّعاء بأنَّ الله يأتيه بمحرم؛ كالخمر ونحوه . وقوله : ( أو عادة أي : كصعود للسَّماء مثلاً . قوله : (وعدم حصول إجابة ) : أي : بعين المطلوب. قوله : (إمَّا لتخلُّف شرط) : أي : من شروط الإجابة بعين المطلوب إذ هي كثيرة؛ منها : أكل الحلال، والثّقة بالله . وله آداب ؛ منها : الوضوء، واستقبال القبلة ورفع الأيدي، وتخليله
The ruling of supplication: it is [valid] except when it involves something impossible by reason, or by sacred law, or by custom. And it should be accompanied by humility and brokenness, and it should be in noble times like the pre-dawn hours and after prayers. And it should not involve imposing restrictions upon Allah, like asking for a specific need at this particular time, for example, unless distress is severe, like deliverance from an oppressor, for example. Moreover, supplication in itself is the core of worship, because it manifests poverty and neediness to Allah, and that Allah is the Self-Sufficient, the Powerful over everything, even if response is not obtained. And the non-occurrence of response is either due to a missing condition, or due to Allah's knowledge that non-response is better. Then: His statement: (impossible by reason) i.e., like combining two opposites. His statement: (or by sacred law) i.e., like supplicating that Allah bring him something forbidden, like wine and the like. His statement: (or by custom) i.e., like ascending to the sky, for example. His statement: (and the non-occurrence of response) i.e., regarding the specific requested thing. His statement: (either due to a missing condition) i.e., from the conditions of response for the specific requested thing, for they are many; among them: eating lawful food, and trust in Allah. And it has etiquettes; among them: ablution, facing the qibla, raising the hands, and... [incomplete]
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling and etiquette of du'a (supplication) as a commentary. It begins by stating that du'a is valid unless it involves something impossible by reason (e.g., combining opposites), by sacred law (e.g., asking for something forbidden like wine), or by custom (e.g., ascending to the sky without a cause). The supplicant should be humble and broken, choose noble times like pre-dawn and after prayers, and avoid imposing restrictions on Allah by demanding a specific outcome at a specific time, except in severe distress like deliverance from a tyrant. The passage then emphasizes that du'a is the core of worship because it demonstrates neediness and acknowledges Allah's self-sufficiency and power, even if the response is not granted. Non-response can be due to a missing condition (such as eating lawful food and trusting in Allah) or because Allah knows that non-response is better for the person. The commentator clarifies each phrase from the main text, explaining that 'impossible by reason' refers to logical impossibilities like combining two opposites, 'by sacred law' refers to asking for something prohibited, and 'by custom' refers to things impossible by habit. The conditions for response are many, including lawful sustenance and trust in Allah. Finally, it lists some etiquettes of du'a: ablution, facing the qibla, raising hands, and... (the text cuts off).

Key Terms
دعاء
ممتنع
عقلاً
شرعاً
عادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think du'a is always valid regardless of content.
Correction: This passage clarifies that du'a can be invalid if it asks for something impossible by reason, law, or custom.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of something impossible by reason?
A) Asking for wine
B) Ascending to the sky without cause
C) Combining two opposites
D) Asking for a specific time

Key Takeaway
The validity of du'a is limited to requests that are rationally, legally, and habitually possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What impossible things have you been asking Allah for in your du'a? Are they rationally, legally, or customarily impossible? How does this lesson force you to reconsider the sincerity and adab of your supplication? Resolve today to check your du'a against these three categories and remove any request that is invalid.
?
Have you ever felt that your du'a was not answered, perhaps because it asked for something that contradicts Allah's law? In light of this lesson, what must change in the way you ask? Will you commit to aligning your desires with what Allah has permitted, even if it means giving up a request you held dear?
?
Is there a habit or custom you follow in du'a that might be considered impossible according to the sunnah? For example, expecting an outcome without taking means. Examine your heart: do you trust Allah's wisdom in making some things impossible by custom? Write one such du'a you need to stop making and replace it with a valid one.

The Etiquette of Du'a: Humility, Timing, and Its Essence
Al-Sawi describes the proper manner and spiritual status of du'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the recommended manner of making du'a and why it is considered the core of worship.

Core Idea
Du'a is the essence of worship, requiring humility and trust in Allah's wisdom.

Having established the boundaries of valid du'a, Al-Sawi now turns to its proper practice. He emphasizes humility, choosing noble times, and avoiding imposing conditions on Allah unless in severe distress. Above all, du'a is the 'marrow of worship' because it reveals our total dependence on Allah, whether or not the request is granted.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on du'a etiquette
Focus on the three recommended behaviors: humility, noble times, and avoiding tahjir.
2
Understand the importance of humility
Du'a should be accompanied by brokenness and neediness.
This reflects sincerity.
3
Understand the preferred times
Pre-dawn and after prayers are special moments.
These are times when du'a is more likely to be accepted.
4
Understand the prohibition of tahjir
Do not restrict Allah by demanding a specific outcome at a specific time, except in extreme distress like deliverance from oppression.
This shows adab towards Allah.
5
Reflect on du'a as the core of worship
Du'a epitomizes worship because it manifests our poverty before Allah and acknowledges His power and self-sufficiency.
Even if not answered, the act is still valuable.

Why Du'a May Not Be Answered: Conditions and Etiquettes
Al-Sawi explains reasons for unanswered du'a and lists conditions and etiquettes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reasons for unfulfilled du'a and the conditions and etiquettes that increase the likelihood of response.

Core Idea
Non-response to du'a is either due to missing conditions or divine wisdom, and proper conditions include lawful food and trust.

Al-Sawi now addresses a common concern: if du'a is so powerful, why is it sometimes not answered? He provides two possibilities: either a condition for response was missing, or Allah knows that non-response is better. He then lists some conditions for response, such as eating lawful food and trusting in Allah, and mentions external etiquettes like ablution and facing the qibla.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on non-response and conditions
Identify the two reasons for non-response and the conditions mentioned.
2
Understand the two reasons for non-response
Either a condition is missing, or Allah's wisdom deems non-response better.
This increases trust in Allah.
3
Learn the conditions for response
Among them: eating lawful food and having trust in Allah.
These are internal and external purity.
4
Note the etiquettes of du'a
Ablution, facing qibla, raising hands, and other practices.
The list is incomplete in the text.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

When your du'a goes unanswered, do you secretly feel that Allah is ignoring you or that you are not worthy? How does knowing that Allah’s wisdom might be shielding you from harm change the way you feel about that unanswered prayer?
?
If you were to examine your last week, how many moments did you truly trust that Allah knows what is better for you—especially when you didn't get what you wanted? What would it look like to live with that trust every day starting now?

beginner
5 min
Supplication for a Good End
Al-Sawi presents a supplication and explains its phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning and significance of the supplication asking Allah to seal our lives with good and to grant us mercy.

Core Idea
This prayer teaches us to seek a good end and divine mercy.

In this passage, Al-Sawi presents a heartfelt supplication that asks Allah to seal our deeds, states, and lifespans with good. He then explains each phrase, showing how it reflects the believer's hope for a good end and reliance on Allah's mercy. The prayer also alludes to the famous hadith about mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the supplication carefully
Read the Arabic text of the supplication once without analysis, then its translation. Let the prayer's own flow come through.
2
Understand the key phrases
Focus on the meaning of 'seal with good', 'take our souls in Your hand', and 'at stumbles'. The commentary explains these phrases.
3
Notice the hadith allusion
The phrase 'O Merciful' alludes to the well-known hadith about mercy. Recognize how the prayer is connected to prophetic teaching.
This hadith is also discussed in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قل بذل : يا رب (اختم) لنا أعمالنا وأحوالنا وأعمارنا (بخير) حتّى لا تقبضنا إليك إلا على أتم حالات التَّوحيد، على شوق إليك، ورغبة فيك، واقبض أرواحنا بيدك، وبدل سيئاتنا حسنات، وخُذ بأيدينا عند العثرات، ربَّنا آمنا بما أنزلت واتَّبعنا الرسول فاكتبنا مع الشاهدين. (يا رحيم) أي : يا أرحم (الرُّحما) فيه إشارة وتلميح إلى قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : الراحمون يرحمهم الرحمن تبارك وتعالى ارحموا من في الأرض يرحمكم من في السماء». قوله : (واقبض أرواحنا بيدك) : أي بحيث لا نشاهد ملكاً يقبضها. قوله : ( عند العثرات) : أي : عند حصول المشاق والمتاعب. قوله : (فيه إشارة وتلميح ... إلخ) وفيه إشارة أيضاً إلى حديث : إذا قال العبد يا أرحم الراحمين قال الله له أنا أرحم الراحمين أقبل عليك فسل» . قوله : ( يرحمكم من في السَّماء») : يحتمل أنَّ (من) واقعة على الملائكة وهو ظاهر ويحتمل وقوعه على الله تعالى وحينئذ فالمعنى من في السماء أمره وسلطانه.
Say: O Lord, seal our deeds, states, and lifespans with good, so that You do not take us to You except in the most perfect states of tawhid, with longing for You and desire for You, and take our souls in Your hand, and exchange our evil deeds for good deeds, and take our hands at stumbles. Our Lord, we have believed in what You revealed and followed the messenger, so write us among the witnesses. O Merciful, i.e. O Most Merciful of the merciful. In it is an allusion to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The merciful are shown mercy by the Merciful, Blessed and Exalted; have mercy on those on earth and He who is in heaven will have mercy on you.' His saying: 'and take our souls in Your hand': i.e., such that we do not see any angel taking them. His saying: 'at stumbles': i.e., at the occurrence of hardships and troubles. His saying: 'In it is an allusion, etc.': And in it is also an allusion to the hadith: 'When the servant says O Most Merciful of the merciful, Allah says to him: I am the Most Merciful of the merciful; turn to Me and ask.' His saying: 'He who is in heaven will have mercy on you': It is possible that 'he who' refers to the angels, which is apparent, and it is possible that it refers to Allah Almighty; in that case the meaning is he whose command and authority is in heaven.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage presents a supplication composed by the author, along with the author's own commentary on its phrases. The passage begins with the supplication text: 'Say: O Lord, seal our deeds, states, and lifespans with good, so that You do not take us to You except in the most perfect states of tawhid...' The prayer asks for a good end, for the soul to be taken directly by God (not by an angel), for sins to be replaced with good deeds, and for divine help at times of difficulty. It also includes a verse from the Quran asking to be written among the witnesses. Then the prayer ends with 'O Merciful, i.e. O Most Merciful of the merciful,' which alludes to the well-known hadith: 'The merciful are shown mercy by the Merciful; have mercy on those on earth and He who is in heaven will have mercy on you.' The author then comments on the prayer phrase by phrase. The commentary explains that 'take our souls in Your hand' means the soul is taken without witnessing an angel. 'At stumbles' means at times of hardship. The author notes that the phrase 'In it is an allusion' also alludes to another hadith about saying 'O Most Merciful of the merciful.' Finally, the author discusses the hadith 'He who is in heaven will have mercy on you,' offering two interpretations: either 'he who' refers to the angels (the apparent meaning) or it refers to Allah, in which case 'in heaven' means His command and authority. This shows the author's careful theological nuance in interpreting scriptural references to God's location, affirming divine transcendence.

Key Terms
اختم بخير
الراحمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does 'واقبض أرواحنا بيدك' mean according to the commentary?
A) We see an angel taking our souls
B) We do not see an angel taking our souls
C) We see Allah taking our souls directly
D) It is a metaphor for death

Key Takeaway
This supplication teaches us to ask Allah for a good end and to rely on His mercy, understanding that true sealing of life is in His hands.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long for Allah so much that you would ask Him to take your soul directly, without the mediation of an angel? What does your daily desire for Allah say about the sincerity of that request?
?
This prayer begs for your bad deeds to be turned into good ones. Is there a particular sin you are still holding onto, unwilling to fully repent from? Will you today beg Allah to transform it into a good deed, and then act as if He has?
?
The hadith here warns: 'The merciful are shown mercy.' Think of one person you have withheld mercy from, or whom you find hard to forgive. What would it cost you to show them mercy today, and what would it gain you with the Most Merciful?

Interpreting 'He Who is in Heaven'
Al-Sawi interprets the phrase 'من في السماء' from a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible interpretations of the phrase 'من في السماء' in the hadith about mercy.

Core Idea
The phrase 'He who is in heaven' can refer to angels or to Allah's authority.

In this part of the commentary, Al-Sawi discusses the meaning of the hadith 'have mercy on those on earth and He who is in heaven will have mercy on you.' He offers two interpretations for the phrase 'من في السماء': either it refers to the angels (apparent meaning) or to Allah, meaning His command and authority. This shows the care scholars take to avoid attributing physical location to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and commentary
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully. Notice the additional hadith about 'O Most Merciful of the merciful'.
2
Understand the first interpretation
The author says the apparent meaning is that 'he who' refers to the angels. Consider why this is straightforward.
This interpretation is the apparent one.
3
Understand the second interpretation
The alternative is that 'he who' refers to Allah, meaning 'he whose command and authority is in heaven.' This avoids physical location.
This interpretation safeguards tanzih (transcendence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قل بذل : يا رب (اختم) لنا أعمالنا وأحوالنا وأعمارنا (بخير) حتّى لا تقبضنا إليك إلا على أتم حالات التَّوحيد، على شوق إليك، ورغبة فيك، واقبض أرواحنا بيدك، وبدل سيئاتنا حسنات، وخُذ بأيدينا عند العثرات، ربَّنا آمنا بما أنزلت واتَّبعنا الرسول فاكتبنا مع الشاهدين. (يا رحيم) أي : يا أرحم (الرُّحما) فيه إشارة وتلميح إلى قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : الراحمون يرحمهم الرحمن تبارك وتعالى ارحموا من في الأرض يرحمكم من في السماء». قوله : (واقبض أرواحنا بيدك) : أي بحيث لا نشاهد ملكاً يقبضها. قوله : ( عند العثرات) : أي : عند حصول المشاق والمتاعب. قوله : (فيه إشارة وتلميح ... إلخ) وفيه إشارة أيضاً إلى حديث : إذا قال العبد يا أرحم الراحمين قال الله له أنا أرحم الراحمين أقبل عليك فسل» . قوله : ( يرحمكم من في السَّماء») : يحتمل أنَّ (من) واقعة على الملائكة وهو ظاهر ويحتمل وقوعه على الله تعالى وحينئذ فالمعنى من في السماء أمره وسلطانه.
Say: O Lord, seal our deeds, states, and lifespans with good, so that You do not take us to You except in the most perfect states of tawhid, with longing for You and desire for You, and take our souls in Your hand, and exchange our evil deeds for good deeds, and take our hands at stumbles. In it is an allusion to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The merciful are shown mercy by the Merciful, Blessed and Exalted; have mercy on those on earth and He who is in heaven will have mercy on you.' His saying: 'and take our souls in Your hand': i.e., such that we do not see any angel taking them. His saying: 'at stumbles': i.e., at the occurrence of hardships and troubles. His saying: 'In it is an allusion, etc.': And in it is also an allusion to the hadith: 'When the servant says O Most Merciful of the merciful, Allah says to him: I am the Most Merciful of the merciful; turn to Me and ask.' His saying: 'He who is in heaven will have mercy on you': It is possible that 'he who' refers to the angels, which is apparent, and it is possible that it refers to Allah Almighty; in that case the meaning is he whose command and authority is in heaven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that 'من في السماء' implies Allah is physically located in heaven.
Correction: The commentary clarifies that it can mean His command and authority, avoiding physical location.

Checkpoint
What are the two possible referents of 'من' in 'يرحمكم من في السماء' according to Al-Sawi?
A) Angels or Allah
B) Only angels
C) Only Allah
D) The Prophet

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'He who is in heaven' is understood either as angels or as Allah's sovereignty, never as a physical location.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith that seems to describe Allah in human terms, do you instinctively accept a literal image in your mind, or do you pause to affirm His transcendence? What steps will you take to guard your heart from forming unworthy thoughts of the Creator?
?
The phrase 'He who is in heaven' could be interpreted as Allah's authority. How does this shift in understanding affect the reverence with which you call upon Him? Does your dua truly reflect that He is beyond physical space?
?
Are you willing to accept the scholars' nuanced interpretation even when it challenges your initial assumption? What fears or attachments keep you from fully embracing Allah's absolute transcendence in this matter?
